('88', 0, 2, 3, 72) POONA, August 30, 1945
('88', 0, 3, 4, 95) LILI, I do not remember having answered your letter.
('88', 0, 3, 5, 148) Just now, after the prayer, I have taken out the old letters.
('88', 0, 3, 6, 210) This is just to tell you that I think of you.
('88', 0, 3, 7, 256) Continue your studies and pass.
('88', 0, 3, 8, 288) Do not lose courage.
('88', 0, 3, 9, 309) Do not spoil your health.
('88', 0, 3, 10, 335) There is no time to write more.
('88', 0, 3, 11, 367) Sardar’s treatment is going on.
('88', 0, 3, 12, 399) I am well.
('88', 0, 4, 13, 410) Blessings from BAPU

('88', 0, 6, 15, 500) 2. LETTER TO PRABHAVATI 1
('88', 0, 7, 16, 526) POONA, August 30, 1945
('88', 0, 8, 17, 549) PRABHA, I do not at all remember whether I have written to you.
('88', 0, 8, 18, 613) Your letter of the 1st is lying in front of me.
('88', 0, 8, 19, 661) I am writing this after the morning prayer.
('88', 0, 8, 20, 705) I hope you keep good health.
('88', 0, 8, 21, 734) You may come when you can.
('88', 0, 8, 22, 761) Just now I shall have to stay with Sardar in Poona.
('88', 0, 8, 23, 813) I may have to be here for three months.
('88', 0, 8, 24, 853) After that I shall be touring.
('88', 0, 8, 25, 884) You should stay in the Ashram.
('88', 0, 8, 26, 915) If there is suitable work for you there and you enjoy peace of mind and keep good health, settle down there.
('88', 0, 8, 27, 1024) Do as you please.
('88', 0, 8, 28, 1042) How is Father?

('88', 10, 1, 2, 10109) 25. LETTER TO DHANNO GIDWANI
('88', 10, 2, 3, 10138) POONA, September 1, 1945
('88', 10, 3, 4, 10163) MY DEAR DHANNO 1, I wonder whether you know Gujarati, Hindustani or Sindhi, seeing that you write to me in bad English?
('88', 10, 3, 5, 10283) Your mother knows Hindustani and Sindhi.
('88', 10, 3, 6, 10324) Your father knew all the above three well.
('88', 10, 3, 7, 10367) But this I write in the language you evidently know best.
('88', 10, 3, 8, 10425) You see now is the time for every patriot to be tested.
('88', 10, 3, 9, 10481) You wear khadi not for family tradition which may or may not be good, not for my sake (that would be of no use), not for the poor (there are other ways of serving them perhaps), but for swaraj to be gained non violently.
('88', 10, 3, 10, 10702) Then you have to wear and use khadi at all cost.
('88', 10, 3, 11, 10751) Then to strengthen your conviction you may add all the other causes.
('88', 10, 3, 12, 10820) Use of khadi is the least you should do and brave the little difficulty you mention.
('88', 10, 3, 13, 10905) Supposing you slave for a showy maintenance for 10 hours, why won’t you lighten your slavery by doing recreative spinning for half an hour daily?
('88', 10, 3, 14, 11051) While you are doing it, you will have the glow of spinning swaraj daily for half an hour.
('88', 10, 3, 15, 11141) Very little if you were the only one.
('88', 10, 3, 16, 11179) But one can multiply oneself into forty crores and then there is swaraj without perhaps more.
('88', 10, 3, 17, 11273) But if you can say to yourself honestly that you have no time for non violent swaraj, you must leave khadi alone and use the cloth you like best and forget family traditions, the poor and me.
('88', 10, 3, 18, 11465) What are you earning?
('88', 10, 3, 19, 11487) Are you married?
('88', 10, 4, 20, 11504) BAPU CHI.
('88', 10, 4, 21, 11514) DHANNO GIDWANI C/O AMBICA MILL NO.
('88', 10, 4, 22, 11549) 1 AHMEDABAD
('88', 10, 5, 23, 11561) From a photostat: G.N. 6759. Also Pyarelal Papers.
('88', 10, 5, 24, 11612) Courtesy: Pyarelal
('88', 10, 6, 25, 11631) 1 Son of A. T. Gidwani
('88', 11, 0, 1, 11654) 12 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI

('88', 11, 6, 14, 12285) 27. LETTER TO NARAHARI D. PARIKH September 1, 1945
('88', 11, 7, 15, 12336) NARAHARI, Khimji 1 had brought your letter.
('88', 11, 7, 16, 12380) I replied at once.
('88', 11, 7, 17, 12399) You must have got the reply by now.
('88', 11, 7, 18, 12435) I would not know if there was any defect in Khimji’s eye.
('88', 11, 7, 19, 12493) Generally I do not observe people too closely.
('88', 11, 7, 20, 12540) And if the parties choose each other despite one of them having an obvious defect, why need a third person object?
('88', 11, 7, 21, 12655) What right does even a father have ?
('88', 11, 7, 22, 12692) I have seen the blind and the crippled also getting married.
('88', 11, 7, 23, 12753) I would be very much surprised if Munnalal has raised any objection.
('88', 11, 7, 24, 12822) When you all who are quite independent have made a selection, what objection can be raised?
('88', 11, 8, 25, 12914) Blessings from BAPU
('88', 11, 9, 26, 12934) From a photostat of the Gujarati: S.N. 9137
('88', 11, 10, 27, 12978) 1 Khimjibhai Patel
('88', 12, 0, 1, 12997) VOL.88: 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 13
('88', 12, 1, 2, 13041) 28. LETTER TO MUNNALAL G. SHAH September 1, 1945
('88', 12, 2, 3, 13090) MUNNALAL, Naraharibhai writes to tell me that as Khimji has a defect in his eye you have raised an objection to his marrying Vina and are even ready to write to her father.
('88', 12, 2, 4, 13263) This surprises me.
('88', 12, 2, 5, 13282) I, therefore, used an “if” in my reply 1 to Narahari.
('88', 12, 2, 6, 13336) When K. and N. have made the selection, what objection can we have?
('88', 12, 2, 7, 13404) Besides, how can you write to Vina’s father?
('88', 12, 2, 8, 13449) Vina is not marrying the man in defiance of anybody’s advice.
('88', 12, 2, 9, 13511) I personally do not see what right a father can have to interfere if the two have selected each other despite an obvious defect in one of them.
('88', 12, 2, 10, 13655) And do all the blind remain unmarried?
('88', 12, 3, 11, 13694) Blessings from BAPU

('88', 18, 9, 12, 21707) 42. DISCUSSION WITH NARENDRA DEV 2 AND SURAJ PRASAD AWASTHI
('88', 18, 10, 13, 21767) POONA, [Before September 2, 1945] 3
('88', 18, 11, 14, 21803) In the course of their interview, the two leaders asked Mahatma Gandhi as to whether the Hindustan Mazdoor Sevak Sangh like the Indian National Congress and the All India Trade Union Congress could adopt the words “peaceful and legitimate” instead of “truth and non violence” in its constitution.
('88', 18, 11, 15, 22100) Mahatma Gandhi is understood to have replied that he disagreed with those who held that “truth and
('88', 18, 12, 16, 22199) 1 Which was to be held in Poona from September 12 to 18 2 (1889 1956); President, All India Kisan Sabha, 1939 and 1942; member, All India Congress Socialist Party and later Praja Socialist Party; Vice Chancellor, Lucknow University and later Banaras Hindu University 3 This report appeared under the date line “Cawnpore, September 5” with an introductory note that “Acharya Narendra Dev and Suraj Prasad Awasthi, M.L.As., met Mahatma Gandhi at Poona last week”.
('88', 18, 12, 17, 22661) The discussion, therefore, must have taken place before Sunday, September 2.
('88', 19, 0, 1, 22738) 20 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 19, 1, 2, 22779) non violence” were not political terms.
('88', 19, 1, 3, 22819) In the political context, the words “peaceful and legitimate” were considered to be more appropriate.
('88', 19, 1, 4, 22921) Even this expression, Mahatma Gandhi said, had been introduced by him in the Congress constitution 1. Since they had to deal with the working class, the objection on grounds of political terminology did not matter.
('88', 19, 1, 5, 23136) The workers must be told in a straight and direct way as to what they should or should not do.
('88', 19, 2, 6, 23231) On the question of trusteeship, which was absent from the constitution of the Sangh, Mahatma Gandhi is said to have pointed out that since the theory of trusteeship was stressed by him and had a permanent association with his name, it was legitimate to make it a matter of dispute.
('88', 19, 2, 7, 23513) He said that he did not want to accentuate class struggle.
('88', 19, 2, 8, 23572) The owners should become trustees.
('88', 19, 2, 9, 23607) They might insist that they should become trustees and yet they might choose to remain owners.
('88', 19, 2, 10, 23702) We shall then have to oppose and fight them.
('88', 19, 2, 11, 23747) Satyagraha will then be our weapon.
('88', 19, 2, 12, 23783) Even if we want a classless society we should not engage in a civil war.
('88', 19, 2, 13, 23856) Non violence should be depended upon to bring a classless society.
('88', 19, 3, 14, 23923) The Hindu, 7 9 1945
('88', 19, 4, 15, 23943) 43. TELEGRAM TO JATINDAS M. AMIN

('88', 21, 4, 6, 25914) 46. LETTER TO JATINDAS M. AMIN
('88', 21, 5, 7, 25945) September 2, 1945
('88', 21, 6, 8, 25963) AMIN, Today I am sending a wire 1 regarding your fast.
('88', 21, 6, 9, 26018) There is a rule that no one should go on a fast without my permission.
('88', 21, 6, 10, 26089) It is possible that you are not aware of it but Prabhakar knows this.
('88', 21, 6, 11, 26159) Both of you are at fault in going on a fast.
('88', 21, 6, 12, 26204) When all of you should render service in treating [cholera] patients, why enfeeble yourselves by fasting?
('88', 21, 6, 13, 26310) I would say that those who are not willing to be inoculated against cholera should not be persuaded to do so by fasting.
('88', 21, 6, 14, 26431) Those who cannot abide by the rules of an institution should leave it.
('88', 21, 6, 15, 26502) We do not have such rules [in our Ashram].
('88', 21, 6, 16, 26545) I am primarily responsible for this because I do not believe in inoculation, etc.
('88', 21, 6, 17, 26627) Right from South Africa I have been holding these views.
('88', 21, 6, 18, 26684) We should make arrangements for those who wish to be inoculated but we should not force those who are unwilling by resorting to a fast.
('88', 21, 6, 19, 26820) If you want to know when one can go on a fast, come to me when I have some leisure.
('88', 21, 6, 20, 26904) Who were the persons involved in beating Kotwal?
('88', 21, 6, 21, 26953) What happened to him?
('88', 21, 6, 22, 26975) Give me the details when you have time.
('88', 21, 6, 23, 27015) Show this letter to Prabhakar and others after translating it into Hindi.
('88', 21, 7, 24, 27089) Blessings from BAPU

('88', 51, 7, 12, 64197) September 10, 1945
('88', 51, 8, 13, 64216) AMALPRABHA 1, I have your letter.
('88', 51, 8, 14, 64250) I have passed the budget for Rs. 810. I shall pass the other one also but I have had a committee set up for the camp 2. I want to pass it after making any changes that may be necessary after the committee submits its report.
('88', 51, 8, 15, 64475) The committee has given me the authority about Assam, so if there is any delay I shall be to blame.
('88', 51, 8, 16, 64575) But I shall not let that happen.
('88', 51, 8, 17, 64608) The purchase of muga 3 should be taken in hand.
('88', 51, 8, 18, 64656) With regard to the method it will be enough if the following things are kept in mind: 1. Let the work of the camp be based on the principle of self sufficiency.
('88', 51, 8, 19, 64817) This means that the camp should become self sufficient by the time it is wound up.
('88', 51, 8, 20, 64900) There would thus be no harm if the camp is kept going for a longer period.
('88', 51, 8, 21, 64975) Maybe, prolonging it will lead to knowledge becoming richer and deeper.
('88', 51, 8, 22, 65047) 2. Spinning and the entire processing of cotton should be done with full knowledge.
('88', 51, 8, 23, 65131) 3. Some good craft should also be taught.
('88', 51, 8, 24, 65173) That too should be done with full knowledge.
('88', 51, 8, 25, 65218) There should be perfect cleanliness in the camp as also among individuals.
('88', 51, 9, 26, 65293) 1 Daughter of Dr. Das of Gauhati 2 Which was subsequently set up at Saraina near Gauhati for Gandhiji’s proposed visit in January 1946 3 A variety of silk yarn
('88', 52, 0, 1, 65453) VOL.88: 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 53
('88', 52, 1, 2, 65497) 4. The basis of self sufficiency should be silk.
('88', 52, 1, 3, 65546) 5. The work of the camp should be done so far as possible by the inmates.
('88', 52, 1, 4, 65620) Let there be as few servants as possible.
('88', 52, 1, 5, 65662) 6. The workers, as far as possible, should be women.
('88', 52, 1, 6, 65715) 7. The camp should be located in or near a village and the life in the camp should resemble the life of the villagers.
('88', 52, 1, 7, 65834) I have written this much by way of giving guidelines.
('88', 52, 1, 8, 65888) The rules that may be received from the central authority must be followed.
('88', 52, 1, 9, 65964) What I have written should be sufficient.
('88', 52, 1, 10, 66006) If not, let me know.

('88', 54, 3, 18, 68985) 121. LETTER TO M. VISVESVARAYYA
('88', 54, 4, 19, 69017) NATURE CURE CLINIC, 6 TODIWALA ROAD, POONA, September 11, 1945
('88', 54, 5, 20, 69080) DEAR SIR VISVESVARAYYA 1, I have your letter of the 7th July.
('88', 54, 5, 21, 69142) I know I am very late in replying to it but it was inevitable.
('88', 54, 5, 22, 69205) As it is I am sending even this late line under pressure.
('88', 54, 5, 23, 69263) I appreciate your zeal in the cause you have at heart and marvel at the fact that at your time of life you throw into your work so much energy and thought.
('88', 54, 5, 24, 69419) There, however, my appreciation, I fear, stands.
('88', 54, 5, 25, 69468) Of course, verbally our objectives appear the same but when I look at our means, the difference seems to me to be unbridgeable.
('88', 54, 5, 26, 69596) It may be that both of us being old and hardened are unable to see eye to eye.
('88', 54, 5, 27, 69675) If you regard South Africa as an elongated part of the West, I have passed the best part of my life in the West.
('88', 54, 5, 28, 69788) I have seen people, high and low, working with amazing speed and with the most modern machinery, the income of the commonest European labourer being higher than that of the American.
('88', 54, 5, 29, 69971) Yet it was there that I learnt to recoil from their method and manner.
('88', 54, 5, 30, 70042) They preyed upon the misery of the
('88', 54, 6, 31, 70077) 1 Mokshagundam Visvesvarayya(1861 1962); engineer and statesman; ex Dewan of Mysore
('88', 55, 0, 1, 70161) 56 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 55, 1, 2, 70202) Negro, holding him and his wife as beasts of burden.
('88', 55, 1, 3, 70255) Things, therefore, that attract you do not attract me but rather repel me.
('88', 55, 1, 4, 70330) Much as I would love to work as a humble co worker side by side with you, I cannot.
('88', 55, 1, 5, 70414) Your detailed, patient replies 1 carefully prepared, fail to convince me.
('88', 55, 1, 6, 70488) What is the use of taxing you further with my questions?
('88', 55, 1, 7, 70545) Let me tell you that I claim to have been working schemes fairly successfully among the village population with well knit organizations.
('88', 55, 1, 8, 70682) Nearly four crores (as I can recall) have been distributed among the villagers, not as doles, but for solid work done—and this in the face of heavy odds.
('88', 55, 1, 9, 70836) Had it not been for the opposition of the Government and their unreasoned wrath after the August of 1942, the said organizations would have shown greater results.
('88', 55, 1, 10, 70999) But I cannot expect you with your Krishnasagar marvels to your credit even to look at my scheme.
('88', 55, 1, 11, 71096) I can, therefore, only conclude by expressing my eagerness to follow not your scheme but your solid work and learn from it, if I see anything to learn.
('88', 55, 1, 12, 71248) I hope you are keeping perfectly well and fit.
('88', 55, 2, 13, 71295) Yours sincerely, M. K. GANDHI SIR M. VISVESVARAYYA, K.C.I.E. UPLANDS, HIGH GROUND BANGALORE

('88', 58, 3, 7, 75938) 126. LETTER TO LORD WAVELL
('88', 58, 4, 8, 75965) NATURE CURE CLINIC, 6 TODIWALA ROAD, POONA, September 14, 1945
('88', 58, 5, 9, 76028) DEAR FRIEND, I am sorry that I have to worry you almost immediately on your return from London.
('88', 58, 5, 10, 76124) My only excuse is that my mission is purely humanitarian.
('88', 58, 5, 11, 76182) Shri Haridas Mitra, an M.A. of the Calcutta University and the husband of Shri Subhas Chandra Bose’s young niece 1, aged 22 years, is under sentence of death over what appears to be an untenable ground.
('88', 58, 5, 12, 76385) I have perused the petition for mercy by the uncle of the condemned as also of Advocate Carden Noad.
('88', 58, 5, 13, 76486) I suggest that they furnish cogent grounds for the exercise of mercy.
('88', 58, 5, 14, 76556) In any event the case for mercy becomes irresistible in that the war with Japan is over.
('88', 58, 5, 15, 76645) It will be a political error of the first magnitude if this sentence of death is carried into effect.
('88', 58, 5, 16, 76747) I rejoiced to learn that you had ordered postponement of execution till after consideration of the case by you on your return.
('88', 58, 5, 17, 76874) My attention was drawn to the case by the prisoner’s wife as she has often sung at my prayer meetings when I had the honour of being a guest of Advocate Sarat Chandra Bose whom I am happy to learn the Government of India has ordered to be released.
('88', 58, 6, 18, 77123) Yours sincerely, M. K. GANDHI H. E. THE VICEROY THE VICEROY’S HOUSE NEW DELHI Gandhiji’s Correspondence with the Government, 1944 47, pp.

('88', 72, 7, 10, 94767) In one of the circulars I see that people have been asked to send their replies by the 21st or 22nd September at the time of the Committee’s meeting.
('88', 72, 7, 11, 94917) If the pamphlet was to be sent only after you got my reply, then the time is over.
('88', 72, 7, 12, 95000) Till today I have not been able to read the pamphlet.
('88', 72, 7, 13, 95054) And ever if I had sent my reply, I think it would have been impossible to send the circulars to all the Provinces and get their replies in time.
('88', 72, 7, 14, 95199) How can we work in such haste?
('88', 72, 7, 15, 95230) And it is almost impossible for me to send my reply by return of post.
('88', 72, 7, 16, 95301) At times I could reply to brief letters but not always.
('88', 72, 7, 17, 95357) What shall we do in such a situation?

('88', 72, 7, 20, 95632) I have gone through all the circulars.

('88', 74, 6, 11, 98151) 163. LETTER TO KAILAS D. MASTER
('88', 74, 7, 12, 98183) BIRLA HOUSE, MOUNT PLEASANT ROAD BOMBAY, September 21, 1945
('88', 74, 8, 13, 98243) KAILAS, I got your letter just as I reached Bombay.
('88', 74, 8, 14, 98295) Your handwriting is good but not clear enough to be read easily.
('88', 74, 8, 15, 98360) If you write slightly bigger letters and do not mix them up, it will be easier to decipher.
('88', 74, 8, 16, 98452) You cannot ride on two horses.
('88', 74, 8, 17, 98483) A family cannot run properly if all the children stay with the parents all the time.
('88', 74, 8, 18, 98568) When children grow older, they have to go out for earning, studying or serving.
('88', 74, 8, 19, 98648) And when they go out, they have to forget their old and ailing parents.
('88', 74, 8, 20, 98720) So why do you feel unhappy for what is inevitable?
('88', 74, 8, 21, 98771) When your parents sent you out, they and you yourself must have thought not only that your duty was to serve your parents, but that it was time that you started earning and lessened their burden.
('88', 74, 8, 22, 98967) That is exactly what you are doing.
('88', 74, 8, 23, 99003) It is good that you are doing all your work and slowly learning every thing.
('88', 74, 8, 24, 99080) You will bring credit to yourself, your parents and the Ashram if you settle down there, stop worrying and take care of your health.
('88', 74, 8, 25, 99213) I am very happy to know that you wanted to have chillies but gave them up on your own.
('88', 74, 8, 26, 99300) I know that some people are so much
('88', 74, 9, 27, 99336) 1 Ruler of Thana Devli, a State in Kathiawar
('88', 75, 0, 1, 99381) 76 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 75, 1, 2, 99422) used to chillies that they would rather die than give them up.
('88', 75, 1, 3, 99485) This shows that taking chillies is not a good habit.
('88', 75, 1, 4, 99538) In India it so happens that the poor cannot afford anything else and they add a few chillies and salt to the rotla 1 to somehow make it digestible.
('88', 75, 1, 5, 99686) To conclude from this that all must take chillies is sheer ignorance.
('88', 75, 1, 6, 99756) When a person takes all kinds of food including rotlas as well, the latter cannot be regarded as part of his diet.
('88', 75, 1, 7, 99871) On the contrary they may be superfluous and might even prove to be harmful.
('88', 75, 2, 8, 99947) Blessings from BAPU
('88', 75, 3, 9, 99967) From a copy of the Gujarati: Pyarelal Papers.

('88', 75, 4, 11, 100032) 164. LETTER TO KRISHNACHANDRA September 21, 1945
('88', 75, 5, 12, 100081) KRISHNACHANDRA, I arrived here at 4 o’clock today.
('88', 75, 5, 13, 100132) I have your letter.
('88', 75, 5, 14, 100152) When a person takes beer with two per cent alcohol content and is forbidden to take whisky with 75 per cent alcohol content, can I ask why beer and why not whisky?
('88', 75, 5, 15, 100316) You must see also that when we drink lemonade or eat things with some alcohol content in them nobody says that we are taking alcohol.
('88', 75, 5, 16, 100450) Equate chillies with whisky and then consider if chillies can go with turmeric or coriander.
('88', 75, 5, 17, 100543) Taking spices does not mean consuming all kinds of spices.
('88', 75, 5, 18, 100602) There is said to be a lot of difference between green chillies and red chillies.
('88', 75, 5, 19, 100683) It is surprising that all these simple things have escaped your attention.
('88', 75, 5, 20, 100758) Whatever spices we give, like turmeric, black pepper, coriander, etc., are given on doctor’s recommendation and on grounds of health.
('88', 75, 5, 21, 100892) Even so, who can prevent anyone from eating for taste, and how can it be done?
('88', 75, 5, 22, 100971) Have you not heard that a Vaghari 2 woman used to relish greatly a two day stale bajra chapati without ghee, but when she was given kheer 3 and wheat halwa 43 to eat every day she started shrinking and fell ill in the end.
('88', 75, 5, 23, 101194) Shall we then say that this Vaghari woman had con quered her palate and subsisted on dry bread, chillies and salt?
('88', 75, 5, 24, 101309) What else should I write?
('88', 75, 6, 25, 101335) 1 Chapati made from baejra or jowar flour 2 Name of a backward community 3 Sweet preparations 4 ibid
('88', 76, 0, 1, 101436) VOL.88: 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 77
('88', 76, 1, 2, 101480) Why did you not ask me till today about taking chillies on grounds of health?
('88', 76, 1, 3, 101558) Of course we do let Shakaribehn have chillies willingly.
('88', 76, 1, 4, 101615) But how can we give it to others?
('88', 76, 1, 5, 101649) The reason is not that chillies have no good qualities at all.
('88', 76, 1, 6, 101712) They certainly have some medicinal value.
('88', 76, 1, 7, 101754) But chillies have no place in a hospital except as a “pain killer” which is an extract of chillies.
('88', 76, 1, 8, 101854) In the Ashram we neither take nor give anything merely for taste.
('88', 76, 1, 9, 101920) But we do not ask everybody whether they relish what they eat and if they do so they should leave the Ashram.
('88', 76, 1, 10, 102030) If we take this view, none but animals and birds will be left in the Ashram.
('88', 76, 1, 11, 102107) Kamle should somehow calm down and improve his health.
('88', 76, 1, 12, 102162) I have already written about Purnachandraji.
('88', 76, 1, 13, 102207) While living in the Ashram everyone has to observe brahmacharya.
('88', 76, 1, 14, 102272) I did not know about Ramprasadji.
('88', 76, 1, 15, 102306) But I was under the impression that Ramprasad’s house was a little away from the other houses of the Ashram.
('88', 76, 1, 16, 102415) Niamat’s room was also there but she was never asked whether she wanted to observe brahmacharya.
('88', 76, 1, 17, 102512) But I had thought that Ramprasad had not come to live in the Ashram like Niamat.
('88', 76, 1, 18, 102593) However, when I came to know that the manner in which they lived they could even produce children I was perturbed.
('88', 76, 1, 19, 102708) Besides others this is the strorgest reason for one to leave the Ashram.
('88', 76, 1, 20, 102781) His having a separate kitchen also used to irk me.
('88', 76, 1, 21, 102832) But since this had been allowed in the case of others I could not be too insistent in dissuading him.
('88', 76, 1, 22, 102934) It is not enough to assume that Purnachandraji must be obser ving brahmacharya while staying in the Ashram.
('88', 76, 1, 23, 103042) It is necessary to ask him clearly.
('88', 76, 1, 24, 103078) I hope to go to Poona from here on the 24th.
('88', 76, 1, 25, 103123) Blessings from BAPU From a photostat of the Hindi: G.N. 4529

('88', 78, 4, 6, 105414) 168. FOREWORD 1
('88', 78, 5, 7, 105430) Dr. Bharatan Kumarappa has, in his pages on “Villagism”, a new word coined by him, furnished the lay reader and the village worker, not conversant with books on economics, a comparative and historical study of the modern movements known as Capitalism and Socialism, not excluding Marxism and Communism, and has earnestly, and I think convincingly, shown, amongst other reasons advanced by him, that the past two wars of our generation have proved the utter bankruptcy of such economic orders.
('88', 78, 5, 8, 105923) Incidentally, the wars seem to me to have proved the bankruptcy of war, meaning in forcible and naked language violence, which is not less because it is organized by States reputed to be civilized.
('88', 78, 5, 9, 106121) Whether non violence will effectively replace violence for keeping the peace of the world remains to be seen.
('88', 78, 5, 10, 106231) Certain it is that mankind, if it continues along its mad career of exploitation of the weak by the strong, must rush to annihilation fore told in all religions.
('88', 78, 5, 11, 106393) Dr. Bharatan Kumarappa shows that “Villagism” as it is being attempted in India, based as it is on truth and non violence, is well calculated to avert the doom.
('88', 78, 5, 12, 106554) If the reader is interested in the life saving process, he must turn to the instructive pages written by Dr. Bharatan Kumarappa during his recent imprisonment.
('88', 78, 6, 13, 106714) M. K. GANDHI
('88', 78, 7, 14, 106727) POONA, September 24, 1945
('88', 78, 8, 15, 106753) Capitalism, Socialism or Villagism?
('88', 78, 9, 16, 106789) 1 To Capitalism, Socialism or Villagism ?
('88', 78, 9, 17, 106831) 2 He Was arrested in 1942 and released in January 1945.

('88', 88, 1, 2, 117445) 191. LETTER TO NARANDAS GANDHI
('88', 88, 2, 3, 117476) September 28, 1945
('88', 88, 3, 4, 117495) NARANDAS, As Kakasaheb is going there, he himself may be regarded as my message.
('88', 88, 3, 5, 117576) Still I shall say this: The yajna this time is of a different character.
('88', 88, 3, 6, 117649) Yarn is taking the place of gold and silver coins.
('88', 88, 3, 7, 117700) In other words, labour takes the place of currency and claims equality with it.
('88', 88, 3, 8, 117780) If this new practice is kept up and spreads, it will have effects too far reaching to be estimated.
('88', 88, 3, 9, 117880) In this there should be no place for fraud or untruth.
('88', 88, 3, 10, 117935) Even the best of plans are ruined if they are mixed with fraud or untruth.
('88', 88, 3, 11, 118010) Blessings from BAPU From a microfilm of the Gujarati: M.M.U./II.

('88', 88, 6, 15, 118169) CHIMANLAL, I enclose herewith Chi.

('88', 88, 6, 17, 118245) Kishorelal.

('88', 88, 6, 25, 118641) Only you three should read it.
('88', 88, 6, 26, 118672) Write to me if you can think of something after some consultations; otherwise forget about it.
('88', 88, 6, 27, 118767) Give it up if too much time is consumed in discussion.
('88', 88, 6, 28, 118822) Naraharibhai is the secretary of the Committee, so he should think over both the letters: 1. Should the institutions be kept separate ?
('88', 88, 6, 29, 118958) Will that be possible now ?
('88', 88, 6, 30, 118986) (The subject matter of K.’s letter.,) 2. Can’t two neighbours live in amity?
('88', 88, 6, 31, 119063) They may cultivate the land separately and have their cattle, fruit trees, and water supply separate.

('88', 88, 6, 33, 119255) It seems Sharda is cured of the fever.
('88', 88, 6, 34, 119294) She had both typhoid and malaria.

('88', 93, 6, 11, 125034) 204. FOREWORD TO “NEHRU YOUR NEIGHBOUR”
('88', 93, 7, 12, 125074) POONA, [September 30, 1945] 1
('88', 93, 8, 13, 125104) This is an effective collection made by Shri P. D. Tandon 2 out of numerous writings of numerous admirers of Pandit Jawaharlal Nehru.
('88', 93, 8, 14, 125238) It gives at a glance a good picture of the patriot as seen by various eyes.
('88', 93, 8, 15, 125314) He shines easily as father, brother, writer, traveller, patriot or internationalist.
('88', 93, 8, 16, 125399) Nevertheless it is as an ardent devotee of his country and its freedom on whose altar he would sacrifice all his other loves that the leader will specially single him out from the essays.
('88', 93, 8, 17, 125587) Be it said to his credit, however, that he will consider it beneath his dignity to purchase that freedom at the price of any other country.
('88', 93, 8, 18, 125727) His nationalism is equal to internationalism.
('88', 93, 9, 19, 125773) M. K. GANDHI
('88', 93, 10, 20, 125786) Nehru Your Neighbour.

('88', 97, 5, 15, 130962) 212. YARN QUOTA FOR KHADI PURCHASE 1
('88', 97, 6, 16, 130999) [September 1945] It is true that the Congress adopted khadi, the Spinners’ Association imposed the condition of the yarn quota and khadi which is not certified by the Association is taboo for Congressmen.
('88', 97, 6, 17, 131204) A certain quantity of yarn has to be given as part of the price of khadi.
('88', 97, 6, 18, 131278) All this is true.
('88', 97, 6, 19, 131296) But I do not find anything wrong in this.
('88', 97, 6, 20, 131338) That action alone can be compulsion where there is penalty for refusing to do a particular thing.
('88', 97, 6, 21, 131436) What the form of punishment should be is a different matter.
('88', 97, 6, 22, 131497) There is no compulsion if I demand the price of khadi and refuse to give it free.
('88', 97, 6, 23, 131579) Similarly there is some condition or other attached to membership in any institution.
('88', 97, 6, 24, 131665) It is also no compulsion if subseque ntly any change is made in such conditions.
('88', 97, 6, 25, 131746) The case of uncertified kkadi is also similar.
('88', 97, 6, 26, 131793) If we go in for uncertified khadi, where is the guarantee of its purity and that a proper wage has been paid to the spinner ?
('88', 97, 6, 27, 131919) With the advance of time and experience, changes have to be made in the rules and regulations.
('88', 97, 6, 28, 132014) The only questions to be consi dered are whether the change fulfils the object, is in keeping with the principle of truth and non violence, and is actuated by selfish or
('88', 97, 7, 29, 132184) 1 This was in reply to a correspondent who had asked: “You persuaded the Congress to adopt khadi wear for its members and introduced the rule of yarn quota for the A. I. S. A. khadi.
('88', 97, 7, 30, 132367) Congressmen are prohibited from using khadi other than that certified by the A. I. S. A., and now khadi cannot be had from the Association without paying the yarn quota.
('88', 97, 7, 31, 132537) Is this not compulsion?”
('88', 98, 0, 1, 132562) VOL.88: 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 99
('88', 98, 1, 2, 132606) benevolent motives.
('88', 98, 1, 3, 132626) The answer to all these questions will show that the change was to fulfil the original object and the question of compulsion does not arise.
('88', 98, 2, 4, 132767) I should be thanked if, against my goods, I ask for yarn or some
('88', 98, 3, 5, 132832) other commodity in place of money.
('88', 98, 4, 6, 132867) Let us go a little deeper.
('88', 98, 4, 7, 132894) We believe that khadi is only for those
('88', 98, 5, 8, 132934) who believe that non violent swaraj can be established by making khadi universal.
('88', 98, 5, 9, 133016) Spinning, even for a little time, by the greatest number of people will be helpful in obtaining swaraj.
('88', 98, 5, 10, 133120) We do not therefore spin under compulsion but of our own accord.
('88', 98, 5, 11, 133185) An additional gain is that through spinning we come in direct contact with the poor.
('88', 98, 6, 12, 133270) Therefore, I am quite clear that there is absolutely no com 
('88', 98, 7, 13, 133331) pulsion in demanding part of the price of khadi in the form of yarn.
('88', 98, 8, 14, 133400) [From Hindi]
('88', 98, 9, 15, 133413) Khadi Jagat, October 1945

('88', 117, 4, 8, 158734) 255. LETTER TO JAWAHARLAL NEHRU
('88', 117, 5, 9, 158766) October 5, 1945
('88', 117, 6, 10, 158782) JAWAHARLAL,
('88', 117, 7, 11, 158794) I have long been intending to write to you but can do so only today.
('88', 117, 7, 12, 158863) I have also been wondering whether I should write in English or Hindustani.
('88', 117, 7, 13, 158939) In the end I have decided to write in Hindustani.
('88', 117, 7, 14, 158989) I take first the sharp difference of opinion that has arisen between us.
('88', 117, 7, 15, 159062) If such a difference really exists people should also know about it, for the work of swaraj will suffer if they are kept in the dark.
('88', 117, 7, 16, 159196) I have said that I fully stand by the kind of governance which I have described in Hind Swaraj 1. It is not just a way of speaking.
('88', 117, 7, 17, 159328) My experience has confirmed the truth of what I wrote in 1909 2. If I were the only one left who believed in it, I would not be sorry.
('88', 117, 7, 18, 159463) For I can only testify to the truth as I see it.
('88', 117, 7, 19, 159512) I have not Hind Swaraj in front of me.
('88', 117, 7, 20, 159551) It is better that I redraw the picture today in my own language.
('88', 117, 7, 21, 159616) Then it would not matter to me whether or no the picture tallies with that of 1909 3, nor should it to you.
('88', 117, 7, 22, 159724) I do not have to establish what I had said before.
('88', 117, 7, 23, 159775) What is worth knowing is only what I have to say today.
('88', 117, 7, 24, 159831) I believe that if India, and through India the world, is to achieve real freedom, then sooner or later we shall have to go and live in the villages—in huts, not in palaces.
('88', 117, 7, 25, 160004) Millions of people can never live in cities and palaces in comfort and peace.
('88', 117, 7, 26, 160082) Nor can they do so by killing one another, that is, by resorting to violence and untruth.
('88', 117, 7, 27, 160172) I have not the slightest doubt that, but for the pair, truth and non violence, mankind will be doomed.
('88', 117, 7, 28, 160275) We can have the vision of that truth and non violence only in the simplicity of the villages.
('88', 117, 7, 29, 160369) That simplicity
('88', 117, 8, 30, 160385) 1 Vide “Hind Swaraj” 2 The source however has “1908”.
('88', 118, 0, 1, 160439) VOL.88: 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 119
('88', 118, 1, 2, 160484) resides in the spinning wheel and what is implied by the spinning wheel.
('88', 118, 1, 3, 160557) It does not frighten me at all that the world seems to be going in the opposite direction.
('88', 118, 1, 4, 160648) For the matter of that, when the moth approaches its doom it whirls round faster and faster till it is burnt up.
('88', 118, 1, 5, 160761) It is possible that India will not be able to escape this moth like circling.
('88', 118, 1, 6, 160839) It is my duty to try, till my last breath, to save India and through it the world from such a fate.
('88', 118, 1, 7, 160939) The sum and substance of what I want to say is that the individual person should have control over the things that are necessary for the sustenance of life.
('88', 118, 1, 8, 161096) If he cannot have such control the individual cannot survive.
('88', 118, 1, 9, 161158) Ultimately, the world is made up only of individuals.
('88', 118, 1, 10, 161212) If there were no drops there would be no ocean.
('88', 118, 1, 11, 161260) This is only a rough and ready statement.
('88', 118, 1, 12, 161302) There is nothing new in this.
('88', 118, 1, 13, 161332) But even in Hind Swaraj I have not said all this.
('88', 118, 1, 14, 161382) While I appre ciate modern thought, I find that an ancient thing, considered in the light of this thought looks so sweet.
('88', 118, 1, 15, 161504) You will not be able to understand me if you think that I am talking about the villages of today.
('88', 118, 1, 16, 161602) My ideal village still exists only in my imagination.
('88', 118, 1, 17, 161656) After all every human being lives in the world of his own imagination.
('88', 118, 1, 18, 161727) In this village of my dreams the villager will not be dull—he will be all awareness.
('88', 118, 1, 19, 161812) He will not live like an animal in filth and darkness.
('88', 118, 1, 20, 161867) Men and women will live in freedom, prepared to face the whole world.
('88', 118, 1, 21, 161937) There will be no plague, no cholera and no smallpox.
('88', 118, 1, 22, 161990) Nobody will be allowed to be idle or to wallow in luxury.
('88', 118, 1, 23, 162048) Everyone will have to do body labour.
('88', 118, 1, 24, 162086) Granting all this, I can still envisage a number of things that will have to be organized on a large scale.
('88', 118, 1, 25, 162194) Perhaps there will even be railways and also post and telegraph offices.
('88', 118, 1, 26, 162267) I do not know what things there will be or will not be.
('88', 118, 1, 27, 162323) Nor am I bothered about it.
('88', 118, 1, 28, 162351) If I can make sure of the essential thing, other things will follow in due course.
('88', 118, 1, 29, 162434) But if I give up the essential thing, I give up everything.
('88', 118, 1, 30, 162494) The other day, at the final day’s meeting of the Working Committee, we had taken a decision to the effect that the Working Committee would meet for two or three days to work out this very thing.
('88', 118, 1, 31, 162689) I shall be happy if it meets.
('88', 118, 1, 32, 162719) But even if it does not meet, I want that we two should understand each other fully.
('88', 118, 1, 33, 162804) And this for two reasons.
('88', 118, 1, 34, 162830) Our bond is not merely political.
('88', 118, 1, 35, 162864) It is much deeper.
('88', 118, 1, 36, 162883) I have no measure to fathom that depth.
('88', 118, 1, 37, 162923) This bond can never be broken.
('88', 118, 1, 38, 162954) I therefore want that we should understand each other thoroughly in politics as well.
('88', 118, 1, 39, 163040) The second reason is that neither of us considers
('88', 119, 0, 1, 163090) 120 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 119, 1, 2, 163132) himself as worthless.
('88', 119, 1, 3, 163154) We both live only for India’s freedom, and will be happy to die too for that freedom.
('88', 119, 1, 4, 163240) We do not care for praise from any quarter.
('88', 119, 1, 5, 163284) Praise or abuse are the same to us.
('88', 119, 1, 6, 163320) They have no place in the mission of service.
('88', 119, 1, 7, 163366) Though I aspire to live up to 125 years rendering service, I am nevertheless an old man, while you are comparatively young.
('88', 119, 1, 8, 163490) That is why I have said that you are my heir.
('88', 119, 1, 9, 163536) 1 It is only proper that I should at least understand my heir and my heir in turn should understand me.
('88', 119, 1, 10, 163640) I shall then be at peace.
('88', 119, 1, 11, 163666) One thing more.
('88', 119, 1, 12, 163682) I had written to you 2 about Kasturba Trust and Hindustani.
('88', 119, 1, 13, 163742) You had said you would write after thinking things over.
('88', 119, 1, 14, 163799) I find that your name is already figuring in the Hindustani Sabha.
('88', 119, 1, 15, 163866) Nanavati reminded me that he had approached you and Maulana Saheb and that you had appended your signature.
('88', 119, 1, 16, 163974) That was in 1942. That was long ago.
('88', 119, 1, 17, 164011) You know where Hindustani stands today.
('88', 119, 1, 18, 164051) If you still stand by that signature, I wish to get some work out of you in this regard.
('88', 119, 1, 19, 164140) It will not involve much running about, but some work will be called for.
('88', 119, 1, 20, 164214) The work of Kasturba Memorial Trust is rather complicated.
('88', 119, 1, 21, 164273) I realize that if what I have said above is going to irk you or is irking you, you will not feel comfortable even in the Kasturba Trust.
('88', 119, 1, 22, 164410) The last point concerns the sparks that are flying about in the conflict with Sarat Babu.
('88', 119, 1, 23, 164500) 3 I have been pained by the episode.
('88', 119, 1, 24, 164537) I have been unable to trace it to its root.
('88', 119, 1, 25, 164581) If what you have told me is all there is to it and nothing more remains to be said, then I do not have to inquire further.
('88', 119, 1, 26, 164704) But if an explanation seems necessary, I very much want to hear it.
('88', 119, 1, 27, 164772) If we have to meet to thrash out all these matters, then we should find time for a meeting.
('88', 119, 1, 28, 164864) You are working very hard.
('88', 119, 1, 29, 164891) I trust you are in good health and Indu 4 is well.

('88', 136, 5, 9, 185586) 293. LETTER TO E. M. JENKINS
('88', 136, 6, 10, 185615) October 10, 1945
('88', 136, 7, 11, 185632) DEAR SIR EVAN,
('88', 136, 8, 12, 185647) I am the Chairman of the All India Spinners’ Association, a wholly philanthropic body of about 25 years’ standing, run solely in the interest of the millions of the poorest unemployed or partly unemployed women of India.
('88', 136, 8, 13, 185868) In order further to popularize hand spinning a rule was recently introduced at my instance to demand from the buyers of khadi a certain quantity of yarn in lieu of money.
('88', 136, 8, 14, 186039) Since the inception of the Association, some time known as Khadi Board,over four crores have been distributed among spinners all over India.
('88', 136, 8, 15, 186180) These include all Communities from among the poor village women.
('88', 136, 8, 16, 186245) Now, I understand, licensing rules are being issued by Provincial Administrations requiring khadi shops to take out licences as if they were dealers in millmade cloth.
('88', 136, 8, 17, 186413) Objection has also been taken to the price being partly demanded in hand spun yarn.
('88', 136, 8, 18, 186497) I am sure the Government do not intend to penalize khadi and thus the poor people.
('88', 136, 8, 19, 186580) As this is an all India matter, I venture to approach His Excellency in the hope of the impending wrong being redressed.
('88', 136, 8, 20, 186701) I may add that the matter has been taken up by the Honorary Secretary
('88', 136, 9, 21, 186771) 1 The addressee on October 13 replied that he was forwarding the letter and enclosure to the Viceroy who was “away on tour”.
('88', 136, 9, 22, 186896) Vide also “Letter to Sir E. M. Jenkins”, 7 11 1945.

('88', 137, 4, 5, 187146) 294. LETTER TO JAIRAMDAS DOULATRAM
('88', 137, 5, 6, 187181) POONA, October 10, 1945
('88', 137, 6, 7, 187205) MY DEAR JAIRAMDASBHAI,
('88', 137, 7, 8, 187228) I read out the whole of your letter to Bapu.
('88', 137, 7, 9, 187273) He says that the ban on sending yarn in large quantities to him was imposed because of the new rules preventing posting of yarn or cloth from one province to another and also in order to save postage.
('88', 137, 7, 10, 187474) He says if you can get over the rules and expense and send the yarn— if everyone insists on this—to him through someone who happens to be coming his way you may do so.
('88', 137, 7, 11, 187642) But he would prefer you to have the yarn woven into cloth and your proposals which are sound should be adopted.
('88', 137, 7, 12, 187754) You may send the dhotis, etc., to him for his personal use when anyone can bring them.
('88', 137, 7, 13, 187841) In regard to the signatures they cannot be had for less than Rs. 5 each.
('88', 137, 7, 14, 187914) Signature money can only go to the Harijan cause.
('88', 137, 7, 15, 187964) Khadi auctioned or yarn or cloth donated at the Jayanti, all goes to the A. I. S. A. I hope I have made Bapu’s wishes clear....
('88', 137, 8, 16, 188092) I am not keen on going 2 but Bapu feels I should go and take advantage of doing work by the way so to speak.
('88', 137, 8, 17, 188201) Bapu is all right again, I am glad to say.
('88', 137, 8, 18, 188244) Of course he gets tired easily.
('88', 137, 8, 19, 188276) But this place admits of good massage and treatment for him as also more protection from visitors than most others and the climate is better than [that of] Sevagram in August, September and October.
('88', 137, 8, 20, 188475) According to present plans he leaves for Sevagram on the 19th and after 9 days there leaves for Bengal, arriving in Calcutta on November 2nd.
('88', 137, 8, 21, 188617) But this depends on what progress Sardar makes this week.
('88', 137, 8, 22, 188675) Up till now there is no real improvement in his case but Bapu is hopeful that he will improve if he stays on....
('88', 137, 9, 23, 188788) AMRIT KAUR
('88', 137, 10, 24, 188799) From the original: C.W. 11060. Courtesy: Arjun Jairamdas

('88', 139, 5, 10, 191202) October 10, 1945
('88', 139, 6, 11, 191219) KISHORELAL,
('88', 139, 7, 12, 191231) Today just after the prayers I read with care your article on decimal coinage.
('88', 139, 7, 13, 191310) I liked it.
('88', 139, 7, 14, 191322) Why did you take so long in sending it?
('88', 139, 7, 15, 191362) Or did you send it and did I miss it by oversight?
('88', 139, 7, 16, 191413) I was in Panchgani then 2 and hardly looked at newspapers.
('88', 139, 7, 17, 191472) At present also the situation is just the same.
('88', 139, 7, 18, 191520) To say that I have carefully gone through the article does not mean that I have also checked up the calculations or that they are clear to me.
('88', 139, 7, 19, 191663) Since you are so good at calculations I take it that the figures are correct.
('88', 139, 7, 20, 191741) Suppose your figures are correct and your suggestions are very useful to the public, you cannot sit quiet after merely writing an article.
('88', 139, 7, 21, 191880) If your health permits, pursue the matter yourself or discuss it with Narahari, Jajuji and Kumarappa.
('88', 139, 7, 22, 191982) Vinoba also is an expert at figures.
('88', 139, 7, 23, 192019) If he agrees, Jajuji or Narahari can go deep into the matter and correspond with Kodanda Rao.
('88', 139, 7, 24, 192113) I am myself writing to him.
('88', 139, 7, 25, 192141) I have written to K. T. Shah 3, Vaikunth 4 and Gagan vihari and sent them copies of the article.
('88', 139, 7, 26, 192238) Now about Jajuji.
('88', 139, 7, 27, 192256) I don’t think we shall gain anything by sending him to the Assembly.
('88', 139, 7, 28, 192325) He would become weak.
('88', 139, 7, 29, 192347) Ours is a queer way of working and the people working there are even more queer.
('88', 139, 7, 30, 192428) People ask for Jajuju and others but will not listen to them after placing them on the throne.
('88', 139, 7, 31, 192523) Jajuji will be much more useful by remaining out of the Assembly.
('88', 139, 7, 32, 192589) Dada’s name is worth considering and perhaps he will be

('88', 141, 8, 16, 194958) CHAUNDE MAHARAJ, I have your letter.
('88', 141, 8, 17, 194995) I have expressed my opinion but that does not mean that a new institution is to be formed for the whole country.
('88', 141, 8, 18, 195108) The Goseva Sangh is already there and the work is going on.
('88', 141, 8, 19, 195168) But the task is a difficult one.
('88', 141, 8, 20, 195201) There should be a considerable number of people who know the science of goseva and can put it into practice.
('88', 141, 8, 21, 195310) Your ideas are noble but the work will not progress on mere ideas.
('88', 141, 8, 22, 195377) I did not like the scene I witnessed the day I went there.
('88', 141, 8, 23, 195436) Everyone was sentimental but they had no knowledge and no will for work.
('88', 141, 8, 24, 195509) Try to expand the scope of the goshala.
('88', 141, 8, 25, 195549) Till now there is no tannery there.
('88', 141, 8, 26, 195585) I do not know if there is a good bull.
('88', 141, 8, 27, 195624) Do you have a dairy expert?
('88', 141, 8, 28, 195652) If there is one and if the existing institution itself becomes an ideal dairy, I shall be too glad and hope to have great results from it.
('88', 141, 8, 29, 195791) A similar experiment is going on in Wardha under my supervision.
('88', 141, 8, 30, 195856) I cannot of course cite any significant results.
('88', 141, 8, 31, 195905) I realize that it is very difficult to attain perfection.
('88', 141, 8, 32, 195963) I know of

('88', 156, 6, 13, 215619) 332. LETTER TO MRIDULA SARABHAI October 15, 1945
('88', 156, 7, 14, 215668) MRIDULA, I have your resignation.
('88', 156, 7, 15, 215702) I think you have acted wisely in tendering it.
('88', 156, 7, 16, 215749) I know and I believe that in accepting the post of Joint Secretary your intention was to render wider service to the cause of women.
('88', 156, 7, 17, 215882) Equally good is your motive in resigning because you realized and I also saw that by continuing in that post you would not be able to realize your ideal.
('88', 156, 7, 18, 216036) There is temperamental incompatibility between Bapa and you.
('88', 156, 7, 19, 216097) You tried to adjust but who can remove inherent differences?
('88', 156, 7, 20, 216158) You saw that your method of working did not satisfy Bapa.
('88', 156, 7, 21, 216216) He, on his part, also tried to adjust but with little success.
('88', 156, 7, 22, 216279) I could see that the difference was enormous.
('88', 156, 7, 23, 216325) In my opinion neither of you is at fault.
('88', 156, 7, 24, 216367) Very often such differences are unbridgeable.
('88', 156, 7, 25, 216413) In these circumstances, the best thing is to work apart.
('88', 156, 7, 26, 216470) Bapa was, and is still, ready to quit.
('88', 156, 7, 27, 216509) But this is Bapa’s creation and Bapa is a seasoned hand in this kind of work.
('88', 156, 7, 28, 216587) It would be difficult for me, I think, to carry this burden without him.
('88', 156, 7, 29, 216660) It is Bapa’s wish and mine that all men should ultimately withdraw from the Samiti and the entire administration should be handed over to the sisters.
('88', 156, 7, 30, 216811) That will bring it real credit.
('88', 156, 7, 31, 216843) This effort will continue and none of us will rest on our oars till it succeeds.
('88', 156, 7, 32, 216924) Success will not come early by Bapa’s leaving it or allowing us to quit.
('88', 156, 7, 33, 216997) Hence I am allowing you to quit the Joint Secretaryship and am accepting your resignation.
('88', 156, 7, 34, 217088) I know that I am not losing your services thereby.
('88', 156, 7, 35, 217139) You are and will continue to be a
('88', 156, 8, 36, 217173) 1 One who serves
('88', 157, 0, 1, 217190) 158 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 157, 1, 2, 217232) trustee.
('88', 157, 1, 3, 217241) I am sure you will continue to work for the local Kasturba Nidhi committee of Gujarat; and you will also assist the Central Committee whenever it needs your help.
('88', 157, 1, 4, 217404) Thus I am confident that you will not lag behind in serving the Committee even when you relinquish its Joint Secretaryship.

('88', 161, 10, 22, 223601) 345. LETTER TO TARABEHN MODAK
('88', 161, 11, 23, 223631) October 16, 1945
('88', 161, 12, 24, 223648) DEAR SISTER, If you had written your article in ink, I myself would have read it earlier.
('88', 161, 12, 25, 223738) But as it was in pencil, I could not read the whole article
('88', 161, 13, 26, 223798) 1 Son of Kunverji Mehta, a Congressman of Bardoli taluk
('88', 162, 0, 1, 223854) VOL.88: 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 163
('88', 162, 1, 2, 223899) though there is plenty of light in my room.
('88', 162, 1, 3, 223943) Ultimately I made someone read it out.
('88', 162, 1, 4, 223982) I know from personal experience that there is a lot of difference between reading something and hearing it read.
('88', 162, 1, 5, 224095) Daily I make someone read out cuttings from newspapers and if and when I have time, I read them myself.
('88', 162, 1, 6, 224199) Sometimes when a thing is re read there is a striking change in my understanding.
('88', 162, 1, 7, 224281) I feel this must be a common experience.
('88', 162, 1, 8, 224322) Of course you have to realize yourself.
('88', 162, 1, 9, 224362) I have mentioned this important, though irrelevant, thing because I thought it worth mentioning.
('88', 162, 1, 10, 224459) I would be pleased if you accept that there is violence in writing in pencil things sent by post.
('88', 162, 1, 11, 224557) The letters written in pencil fade away in course of time.
('88', 162, 1, 12, 224616) I am sending back your article.
('88', 162, 1, 13, 224648) Please note the changes I have made in what I could read myself.
('88', 162, 1, 14, 224713) The changes are just from the point of view of language.
('88', 162, 1, 15, 224770) The rest I find is quite all right.
('88', 162, 1, 16, 224806) I am giving a gist of my experiences so as to make what I have said more clear.
('88', 162, 1, 17, 224886) I saw the work done by teachers trained under Madame Montessori, and carefully observed the working of the Nursery School.
('88', 162, 1, 18, 225009) Of course the things were foreign and the poor teacher had not digested what she had been taught.
('88', 162, 1, 19, 225107) What to speak of the children?
('88', 162, 1, 20, 225138) They could not even observe normal discipline.
('88', 162, 1, 21, 225185) I am not criticising anyone.
('88', 162, 1, 22, 225214) I have given the gist of my experience just for your information.
('88', 162, 1, 23, 225280) Imbibe whatever you find useful and discard the rest.
('88', 162, 1, 24, 225334) The conclusion I have drawn from this experience is that we shall be able to propagate scientific knowledge of child education only when our teachers are competent.
('88', 162, 1, 25, 225499) They should have the will to become one with children.
('88', 162, 1, 26, 225554) I am afraid I am not saying anything new in this.
('88', 162, 1, 27, 225604) These things are certainly not beyond your range of experience but since I have come to know you and also love you I hope you will not find fault with me for saying the things you already know.
('88', 162, 2, 28, 225798) From a copy of the Gujarati: Pyarelal Papers.
('88', 162, 2, 29, 225844) Courtesy: Pyarelal

('88', 163, 5, 7, 226325) POONA, October 16, 1945
('88', 163, 6, 8, 226349) MRIDU, I showed it to Bapa.
('88', 163, 6, 9, 226377) He returned my draft unchanged.
('88', 163, 6, 10, 226409) He said: “I cannot think of making any changes in this.
('88', 163, 6, 11, 226465) Do what you think proper.

('88', 163, 6, 13, 226539) But do what you think is correct.” So I am sending my draft as it is with my signature.
('88', 163, 6, 14, 226627) But if you wish to make any changes, send it back to me with the changes.

('88', 163, 6, 17, 226822) Bapa says: “I stick to what I said.
('88', 163, 6, 18, 226858) No one had sanctioned it.

('88', 163, 6, 21, 227091) It appears to me that Jog has written under your persuasion.
('88', 163, 6, 22, 227152) So I take that what will fully satisfy you will also satisfy her.
('88', 163, 6, 23, 227218) I understand that what you suggest is two months’ wages.
('88', 163, 6, 24, 227275) So I shall arrange for sanction for only two months.
('88', 163, 6, 25, 227328) I shall do about the matter as you want.

('88', 165, 2, 3, 228894) POONA, October 17, 1945
('88', 165, 3, 4, 228918) CHHAGANLAL, I have your letter.
('88', 165, 3, 5, 228950) I remember to have written to you that I would let you accompany me during some part of my tour.
('88', 165, 3, 6, 229047) 1 My view is that it would be convenient if you accompanied me in the Madras Presidency, for I am familiar with the work there.
('88', 165, 3, 7, 229175) The work in Bengal and Assam is rather difficult.
('88', 165, 3, 8, 229225) I don’t have a clear picture of it in my mind.
('88', 165, 3, 9, 229272) I, therefore, don’t wish to take with me there anybody who is not specially needed.
('88', 165, 3, 10, 229356) The date of my tour also has not been fixed.
('88', 165, 3, 11, 229401) Perhaps I may go to Bengal only after November 21. Everything depends on Sardar’s health.
('88', 165, 3, 12, 229491) I think your accepting money from the Rulers requires some consideration.
('88', 165, 3, 13, 229565) It was your letter which made me think about this.
('88', 165, 3, 14, 229616) Shouldn’t we ponder whether or not we can accept money from Rulers who pay no attention at all to the welfare of their subjects?
('88', 165, 3, 15, 229745) When the amount of Rs. 1,000 is received, I will credit it to the account of the Harijan Sevak Sangh.

('88', 166, 7, 8, 230698) 352. LETTER TO PRABHAVATI
('88', 166, 8, 9, 230724) October 17, 1945
('88', 166, 9, 10, 230741) PRABHA,
('88', 166, 10, 11, 230749) Why do you mark your letters “private”?
('88', 166, 10, 12, 230789) What is there private for a public worker?
('88', 166, 10, 13, 230832) And what was private in your letter?
('88', 166, 10, 14, 230869) I have not kept a copy of my letter.
('88', 166, 10, 15, 230906) What can I, therefore, write?
('88', 166, 10, 16, 230936) Probably it was about your study, Jayaprakash and your coming.
('88', 166, 10, 17, 230999) There may have been something concerning what you wrote regarding Banaras.
('88', 166, 10, 18, 231074) For more details ask me when I arrive there.
('88', 166, 10, 19, 231119) Learn to keep patience till then.
('88', 166, 10, 20, 231153) I am enquiring from Rajkumari and Sushilabehn about the letter to you.

('88', 169, 2, 3, 234299) POONA, October 18, 1945
('88', 169, 3, 4, 234323) BHAI PROFULLA, I have your letter and telegram about Jawaharlalji.
('88', 169, 3, 5, 234390) 2 I have understood the matter.
('88', 169, 3, 6, 234422) Sudhir came yesterday.
('88', 169, 3, 7, 234445) I have had long talks with Sudhir yesterday and today.
('88', 169, 3, 8, 234500) I could not send a telegram about my decision.
('88', 169, 3, 9, 234547) It would have been too long.
('88', 169, 3, 10, 234576) So I am sending this letter.
('88', 169, 3, 11, 234605) Sudhir must have sent you a brief telegram.
('88', 169, 4, 12, 234649) Taking everything into consideration I feel that at this stage you may announce this much: ‘Owing to unavoidable circums tances Gandhiji cannot come to Calcutta on the 2nd November.
('88', 169, 4, 13, 234831) As soon as the date is decided it will be announced.
('88', 169, 4, 14, 234884) It is likely that he will come in the last week of November or thereabouts.
('88', 169, 4, 15, 234960) His tour programme which has been published in the newspapers is also cancelled.
('88', 169, 4, 16, 235041) But wherever he is likely to go, the organizers will be informed so that they can make some arrangements.
('88', 169, 4, 17, 235147) No expen diture of any kind should be incurred at this stage.
('88', 169, 4, 18, 235209) Wherever he goes, his transport will have to be paid for, but that can be seen at that time only.
('88', 169, 4, 19, 235307) Gandhiji has made it clear that, health permitting, he will try his best to go to all the places he wanted to visit.
('88', 169, 4, 20, 235424) But consi dering his age and health, it is obvious that in spite of his desire to visit as many places as possible he will be able to visit only a few of them.’ You may publish this much.
('88', 169, 4, 21, 235612) Now I shall tell you what I want to do.
('88', 169, 4, 22, 235652) If possible I want to visit Midnapore, Chittagong, Dacca, Borkamta, Santiniketan and Assam.
('88', 169, 4, 23, 235744) If any other place is left out, like Feni, I would like to visit that also.
('88', 169, 4, 24, 235820) You can inform the local organizers about my programme which all of you there may decide for me.
('88', 169, 4, 25, 235917) Transport also would have to be arranged.
('88', 169, 4, 26, 235959) Do not give anything to the Press yet.
('88', 169, 4, 27, 235998) That can be done on my arrival.
('88', 169, 4, 28, 236030) It takes a little time to make the preliminary arrangements.
('88', 169, 4, 29, 236091) That is why I have suggested this.
('88', 169, 4, 30, 236126) It is for you to work out what places I can easily visit.
('88', 169, 4, 31, 236184) I don’t feel that it is necessary for me to let you know just now

('88', 174, 0, 1, 243566) VOL.88: 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 175
('88', 174, 1, 2, 243611) 366. LETTER TO MANGALDAS PAKVASA
('88', 174, 2, 3, 243644) October 18, 1945
('88', 174, 3, 4, 243661) BHAI MANGALDAS PAKVASA, Many Provincial governments permit the sale of cloth under licences.
('88', 174, 3, 5, 243754) They have now amended the terms.
('88', 174, 3, 6, 243787) A copy of the amendment introduced by the C. P. Government is enclosed.
('88', 174, 3, 7, 243859) In my view a product like khadi cannot be, ought not to be, licensed.
('88', 174, 3, 8, 243929) A leading counsel in South Africa with a flourishing practice had told me that one must proceed on the assumption that every tangible wrong had a remedy in law and seareh for it, assured that it would be found.
('88', 174, 3, 9, 244140) This had appealed to me very much, and I had always relied on it in my work in South Africa and succeeded in finding the remedies.
('88', 174, 3, 10, 244271) I believe the principle is true in India, too.
('88', 174, 3, 11, 244318) I have not read all the laws, but I feel that a law which applies to a mill owner worth millions cannot apply to khadi.
('88', 174, 3, 12, 244438) If you see the definition of a ‘dealer’, you will observe that it must include ‘business’.
('88', 174, 3, 13, 244529) There is no trace of ‘business’ in khadi, for all processes relating to it merely ensure a livelihood to those who make a living through khadi.
('88', 174, 3, 14, 244673) I have alluded to this argument merely as a suggestion to you.
('88', 174, 3, 15, 244736) You will also see that the Government is empowered to grant exemption to anybody.
('88', 174, 3, 16, 244818) This is not a matter of law, as yet.
('88', 174, 3, 17, 244855) I draw your attention to it.
('88', 174, 3, 18, 244884) You may write to Jajuji for any further information which you cannot get locally.
('88', 174, 3, 19, 244966) What I want you to do is this.
('88', 174, 3, 20, 244997) Consult anybody whom you wish to and then write to the Government yourself, or request the counsel whom you consult to do so.
('88', 174, 3, 21, 245123) If, however, you feel that whatever representation is to be made should be addressed by Jajuji as Secretary, we shall do that.
('88', 174, 3, 22, 245250) Send copies to Jajuji and me of any correspondence that you have.
('88', 174, 3, 23, 245316) And if you decide to write to the Government directly from there, send the letter after showing the draft to me.
('88', 174, 3, 24, 245429) I still cherish the belief that I may be able to suggest some improvements.
('88', 174, 3, 25, 245505) We should write immediately to the Provincial Government or to the Central Government, whichever you decide.
('88', 174, 3, 26, 245614) I have already addressed 1 a communication to the Central Government as President of the Charkha Sangh.
('88', 174, 3, 27, 245718) A copy is enclosed.
('88', 174, 3, 28, 245738) I have even received an acknowledgement of the letter.
('88', 174, 3, 29, 245793) The copy is only for your information for the present.
('88', 174, 3, 30, 245848) We do not wish to give publicity to this matter in
('88', 174, 4, 31, 245899) 1 Vide “Letter to E. M. Jenkins”, 10 10 1945
('88', 175, 0, 1, 245944) 176 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 175, 1, 2, 245986) newspapers just now or let everybody know about it.
('88', 175, 1, 3, 246038) Probably you know that by adopting such a procedure I had been able to save the Charkha Sangh during Linlithgow’s tenure.
('88', 175, 1, 4, 246160) Let us see what happens this time.
('88', 175, 1, 5, 246195) I am entrusting this important task to you relying on the assurance you have given to me, that you intend to use your ability and prestige as a lawyer, not for money but entirely for public service.
('88', 175, 1, 6, 246394) And that is what you have been doing for some time.
('88', 175, 1, 7, 246446) Isn’t that the best way for everybody to use their talents?
('88', 175, 1, 8, 246506) If you want any further information, please write to me.
('88', 175, 1, 9, 246563) The matter is urgent, since they have already started issuing licences.
('88', 175, 1, 10, 246635) I forgot about one thing.
('88', 175, 1, 11, 246661) Khadi is facing a special danger, namely, the U. P. Government’s objection to our practice of demanding yarn worth some pice from the buyers for khadi worth every rupee.
('88', 175, 1, 12, 246831) The objection seems to me ridiculous and harmful from every point of view.
('88', 175, 1, 13, 246906) However, please consider along with the other issue whether such an objection can be sustained in law.
('88', 175, 1, 14, 247009) In my view this is a secondary matter and can be easily dealt with.
('88', 175, 1, 15, 247077) The chief thing is that khadi must not be considered as falling within the scope of the licensing law.
('88', 175, 1, 16, 247180) We have even stores which sell less than 1,000 rupees worth of khadi every month.
('88', 175, 1, 17, 247262) To require a licence for sale of khadi is to put a restraint over the production of khadi, i.

('88', 177, 11, 22, 250144) 373. LETTER TO E. M. JENKINS
('88', 177, 12, 23, 250173) NATURE CURE CLINIC, 6 TODIWALA ROAD, POONA, October 19, 1945
('88', 177, 13, 24, 250234) DEAR SIR EVAN, Shri Jyotish Bose is a condemned prisoner with Shri Haridas Mitra and others.
('88', 177, 13, 25, 250327) The condemned prisoner’s father came to me two
('88', 177, 14, 26, 250374) 1 The letter is placed between those of October 18 and 19, 1945.
('88', 178, 0, 1, 250439) VOL.88: 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 179
('88', 178, 1, 2, 250484) days ago and showed me his petition for mercy.
('88', 178, 1, 3, 250531) If Shri Haridas Mitra’s sentence is commuted, as I hope it will, this one deserves commutation ipso facto.
('88', 178, 1, 4, 250638) Shri Jyotish Bose is the son of an uninfluential poor father.
('88', 178, 1, 5, 250700) But I am sure that poverty will be considered no bar to commutation.
('88', 178, 1, 6, 250769) I see from the legal papers that there are others of the batch awaiting execution.
('88', 178, 1, 7, 250852) The times when the sentences were pronounced were those of war when calmness was at a discount.
('88', 178, 1, 8, 250948) Now they are changed.
('88', 178, 1, 9, 250970) The war is over.
('88', 178, 1, 10, 250987) The condemned men have, no matter what the cause of delay was, survived the war.
('88', 178, 1, 11, 251068) Will it be too much if I suggest a reconsideration of all such cases in the shape of commutation of death sentences?
('88', 178, 1, 12, 251185) In my opinion, justice to be real justice requires extension of mercy to temper it.
('88', 178, 1, 13, 251269) May I ask you please to put this letter before His Excellency for consideration?
('88', 178, 2, 14, 251350) Yours sincerely, M.K. GANDHI
('88', 178, 3, 15, 251379) Gandhiji’s Correspondence with the Government, 1944 47, PP.

('88', 184, 1, 2, 258670) 387. LETTER TO BHAVANIDAYAL SANNYASI
('88', 184, 2, 3, 258707) October 19, 1945
('88', 184, 3, 4, 258724) BHAI BHAVANIDAYAL, I have your letter.
('88', 184, 3, 5, 258763) I am sorry to learn that you are not well.
('88', 184, 3, 6, 258806) Get well soon.
('88', 184, 3, 7, 258821) This is my hope as well as my wish.
('88', 184, 3, 8, 258857) It is surprising that you who know me from childhood should still fail to understand fully or to make others understand what I am doing.
('88', 184, 3, 9, 258994) Truly speaking, good work does not need anyone’s blessings because it is in itself a blessing.
('88', 184, 3, 10, 259089) That is to say, its success lies in the work itself.
('88', 184, 3, 11, 259142) Secondly, for what shall I send my blessings?
('88', 184, 3, 12, 259188) There is no reason to doubt that your aunt may be greater than all the mahatmas in her field and perhaps she is.
('88', 184, 3, 13, 259301) Moreover, she is certainly of an advanced age but it is my misfortune that I don’t know her.
('88', 184, 3, 14, 259394) In such a situation how can a man like me send blessings to her?
('88', 184, 3, 15, 259459) And where do I count among so many titled men and other bigwigs, and, pray, why should I?
('88', 184, 3, 16, 259549) When the rich take my blessings on some occasions you should take it that I know them and take service from them.
('88', 184, 3, 17, 259663) Otherwise none of the rich come to me or can get anything from me.
('88', 184, 3, 18, 259730) And what to say of the poor?
('88', 184, 3, 19, 259759) They are mine and I am theirs.
('88', 184, 3, 20, 259790) I am myself poor but if they get my blessings it is not going to appear in the newspapers.
('88', 184, 3, 21, 259881) So looking from all points of view, I cannot be a participant in your aunt’s memorial.
('88', 184, 3, 22, 259968) Those who are in it do not know me; so they can only criticize me.
('88', 184, 3, 23, 260035) What else can they do?
('88', 184, 3, 24, 260058) If people like you can convince them with love, you may do so.
('88', 184, 3, 25, 260121) What will you gain by writing to me except that I should waste my time in writing such long letters and give you the trouble of reading them even when you are not well?
('88', 184, 3, 26, 260290) I shall have done my job if I have been able to make you see the point and if I have not, I am helpless.
('88', 184, 4, 27, 260395) BHAVANIDAYAL SANNYASI PRAVASI BHAVAN ADARSH NAGAR, AJMER
('88', 184, 5, 28, 260452) From a copy of the Hindi: Pyarelal Papers.
('88', 184, 5, 29, 260495) Courtesy: Pyarelal

('88', 196, 4, 9, 277235) 412. LETTER TO BHULABHAI J. DESAI
('88', 196, 5, 10, 277269) POONA, October 21, 1945
('88', 196, 6, 11, 277293) BHAI BHULABHAI 1, As it is difficult to decipher my handwriting, I am dictating this letter so that it can be written in a clear hand.
('88', 196, 6, 12, 277428) Sardar and I keep receiving telegrams suggesting that you should be put up as a candidate for the Central Legislative Assembly.
('88', 196, 6, 13, 277556) I myself have no interest in the elections.
('88', 196, 6, 14, 277600) A durbar daily assembles round the Sardar, but I know nothing about it.
('88', 196, 6, 15, 277672) Ordinarily he does not talk to me not do I ask him anything.
('88', 196, 6, 16, 277733) I attend to my work and he attends to his.
('88', 196, 6, 17, 277776) The only reason for our being together this time is his nature care treatment.
('88', 196, 6, 18, 277855) He does not have much faith in nature care while I have.
('88', 196, 6, 19, 277912) An operation would be a very risky affair.
('88', 196, 6, 20, 277955) No doctor except Dr. Deshmukh advises it.
('88', 196, 6, 21, 277997) That is why he has put faith in me and is undergoing nature cure treatment.
('88', 196, 6, 22, 278073) I have, accordingly, brought him to Dr. Mehta for I have faith in him.
('88', 196, 6, 23, 278144) My own knowledge of nature cure is superficial.
('88', 196, 6, 24, 278192) I have given this introduction because I thought it necessary.
('88', 196, 7, 25, 278255) If Sardar receives any suggestion regarding you, he puts it before me.
('88', 196, 7, 26, 278326) Since you have accepted my advice, I assume that you yourself are not at all keen o getting into the Central Assembly, and that, therefore, those who send the telegrams do not do so at your
('88', 196, 8, 27, 278516) 1 (1877 1946); Leader of the Congress Party in the Central Assembly; President, Bombay Provincial Congress Committee; member of Congress Working Committee
('88', 197, 0, 1, 278671) 198 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 197, 1, 2, 278713) instance.
('88', 197, 1, 3, 278723) Some big people naturally desire your presence in the Assembly.
('88', 197, 1, 4, 278787) If I were not there, perhaps Sardar would have yielded to the pressure.
('88', 197, 1, 5, 278859) But I am firm, for I am acting as your well wisher.
('88', 197, 1, 6, 278911) I want a big service from you, if you can give it.
('88', 197, 1, 7, 278962) I wish to see you as a people’s man.
('88', 197, 1, 8, 278999) I don’t consider you an old man.
('88', 197, 1, 9, 279032) Why shouldn’t you also live up to 125?
('88', 197, 1, 10, 279071) If you do not aspire to live that long, as I do, please remember that I try to persuade everybody to have such as piration for the sake of service.
('88', 197, 1, 11, 279219) And it is not that there is no strength or effort behind my aspiration.
('88', 197, 1, 12, 279291) If there is non and my aspiration proves fruitless, I will accept that.
('88', 197, 1, 13, 279363) I am not, therefore, afraid of death if it should come today.
('88', 197, 1, 14, 279425) But I will cherish my aspiration till my last breath, for I have to serve —I have not yet finished with service.
('88', 197, 1, 15, 279538) There is a spirit of competition to serve which all of us should share.
('88', 197, 1, 16, 279610) From this standpoint I suggest to you that you yourself should issue a graceful statement, thanking all those who are trying on your behalf, explaining that you do not wish to be a member of the Assembly at the moment and that you have been doing, and will continue to do, whatever service you can from outside, that if you live long enough and feel later that you should also enter the Legislature, you yourself will come forward and seek people’s votes.
('88', 197, 1, 17, 280066) I like the work you are doing just now of defending the prisoners.
('88', 197, 1, 18, 280133) 1 It will bring you credit.
('88', 197, 1, 19, 280161) I also wish that like Jawaharlal and Sardar, and to a great extent Maulana Azad, you too should come into contact with the masses.
('88', 197, 1, 20, 280292) Perhaps I should cite Rajendra Babu’s case as offering the best example.
('88', 197, 1, 21, 280365) Rajendra Babu is sought after by Bihar, he himself does not go seeking the support of Bihar.
('88', 197, 1, 22, 280458) I can cite other similar instances, too.
('88', 197, 1, 23, 280499) But where is the need to do so for you?
('88', 197, 1, 24, 280539) Even what I have written above seems to me too long, but I cannot restrain my Moha 2. If desire also could be described as sattvika 3, I am sure this desire of mine is that and, therefore, I need not hide it.
('88', 197, 1, 25, 280748) I trust you are well and succeeding in your efforts.
('88', 197, 1, 26, 280801) Blessings from BAPU

('88', 198, 1, 2, 281340) 413. A NOTE
('88', 198, 2, 3, 281352) POONA, October 21, 1945 I have gone through this.
('88', 198, 2, 4, 281402) I liked it.
('88', 198, 2, 5, 281414) I would like to go a little further.
('88', 198, 2, 6, 281451) Khadi is a symbol of truth and ahimsa.
('88', 198, 2, 7, 281490) It should not subsist on the mercy of the Government.
('88', 198, 2, 8, 281544) It will be a different thing altogether if khadi is adopted deliberately after its real strength is realized.
('88', 198, 2, 9, 281654) The shortage of cloth will then be easily removed.
('88', 198, 2, 10, 281705) We can even have swaraj by non violent means and thereby bring credit to ourselves and to our Government.
('88', 198, 2, 11, 281811) Sooner or later that will come but how soon it will come, depends on the public acceptance of the new plan.
('88', 198, 2, 12, 281919) I do know that a time may come when we may even have to suspend the sale of khadi in our shops.
('88', 198, 2, 13, 282015) Self reliance is the only remedy.
('88', 198, 2, 14, 282049) From that point of view Jajuji’s article is a preliminary and an essential move.

('88', 199, 2, 3, 282711) October 21, 1945
('88', 199, 3, 4, 282728) ANANT RAM, Only today I could finish reading your letter of September 2. It is good.
('88', 199, 3, 5, 282813) Ramanama includes everything.
('88', 199, 3, 6, 282843) The order is: dharma, artha, kama and moksha 1. Artha cannot be opposed to kama, dharma and moksha.
('88', 199, 3, 7, 282943) Hence, artha is food, clothing and other necessities of life; kama is noble desire.
('88', 199, 3, 8, 283027) Ramanama transcends time and circumstance— it has to.
('88', 199, 3, 9, 283081) And it must issue from the heart, not from the mouth.
('88', 199, 3, 10, 283135) It requires persistent effort.
('88', 199, 3, 11, 283166) Get Asha Devi to write down the Gitanjali 2 songs in Bengali and send them to me.
('88', 199, 3, 12, 283248) Become good and do lot of service.

('88', 206, 7, 24, 294105) 433. LETTER TO V. V. DASTANE
('88', 206, 8, 25, 294134) October 23, 1945
('88', 206, 9, 26, 294151) BHAI DASTANE, I have your postcard.
('88', 206, 9, 27, 294187) It is not that I have not replied to your letter owing to lack of time, but since I have something new to say, there is no need to reply to your other questions.
('88', 206, 9, 28, 294349) The new thing is that
('88', 207, 0, 1, 294371) 208 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 207, 1, 2, 294413) till today you have considered public service as primary and have devoted to the family only whatever time was available after that.
('88', 207, 1, 3, 294546) Now having heard everything from Akka 1, I feel that you are no longer in a position to do so.
('88', 207, 1, 4, 294641) Naturally you have to take care of Akka and also look after your other daughters and manage their affairs.
('88', 207, 1, 5, 294748) You have to support your wife.
('88', 207, 1, 6, 294779) If you do not, who else will?
('88', 207, 1, 7, 294809) So it is the duty of people like you to give primary importance to the family responsibilities and devote to public service only as much time as you can after that.
('88', 207, 1, 8, 294974) One who shoulders the burden of the family as dharma also renders service.
('88', 207, 1, 9, 295049) One must clearly distinguish between family responsibility and family enjoyment.
('88', 207, 1, 10, 295130) You have long since given up indulgence.
('88', 207, 1, 11, 295171) Why should I discuss these things at length?
('88', 207, 1, 12, 295216) You should be able to understand them from what I have already said.
('88', 207, 1, 13, 295285) It should be clear enough that if you do not abide by what I have said the result will be quite to the contrary of what it should be.
('88', 207, 1, 14, 295419) I cannot say what I had in mind when I wrote “I cannot give” [answers to your other questions].
('88', 207, 1, 15, 295515) And what will you gain by thinking over it again and again?
('88', 207, 1, 16, 295575) If I was short of time, I should have said that I would reply to the other questions some other time.
('88', 207, 1, 17, 295677) At any rate, I was quite clear in my mind when I sent a letter 2 through Akka that I should tell you what according to me your dharma was without bothering you about other things.
('88', 207, 1, 18, 295857) Now the question arises only if you are not able to understand and approve of my stand.
('88', 207, 1, 19, 295945) You can discuss this letter with Vinoba and Kishorelal.
('88', 207, 1, 20, 296001) Of course also with Dhotre 3 and other relatives there.
('88', 207, 2, 21, 296057) VASUDEV DASTANE BHUSAWAL From a copy of the Hindi: Pyarelal Papers.
('88', 207, 2, 22, 296125) Courtesy: Pyarelal
