('88', 211, 2, 3, 300493) October 25, 1945
('88', 211, 3, 4, 300510) SUSHILA, I had a postcard from Chi.
('88', 211, 3, 5, 300546) Nilkanth yesterday saying that you wanted Arun to come to you with him.
('88', 211, 3, 6, 300618) I told Arun about it.
('88', 211, 3, 7, 300640) Kanu has the greatest influence over him.
('88', 211, 3, 8, 300682) He and others also told him.
('88', 211, 3, 9, 300711) But he remained stubborn.
('88', 211, 3, 10, 300737) He says he will come with me.
('88', 211, 3, 11, 300767) That means all of you will have to spend the Diwali without him.
('88', 211, 3, 12, 300832) Put up with his absence.
('88', 211, 3, 13, 300857) I am sure you do not wish that I should send him against his will.
('88', 211, 3, 14, 300924) With great difficulty he wrote the letter on the back of this last night.
('88', 211, 3, 15, 300998) He has no interest at all in study, but has plenty in playing and cycling.
('88', 211, 3, 16, 301073) Whatever is possible will have to be done only here.
('88', 211, 3, 17, 301126) Arun himself is quite happy.
('88', 211, 3, 18, 301155) He studies a little, but very little.
('88', 211, 3, 19, 301193) For all this backwardness I hold you, his mother, most responsible, since I have always believed you to be wise.
('88', 211, 3, 20, 301306) If Arun remains a dullard, I will surely regard you as stupid.
('88', 211, 3, 21, 301369) May you all spend a happy Diwali.
('88', 211, 3, 22, 301403) Reserve a share for us all in your happiness.
('88', 211, 3, 23, 301449) “Us all” includes all of us here and the dumb, poor millions of India.
('88', 211, 3, 24, 301520) Those who do not remember them even on the Diwali day, their Diwali, according to me, is worse than Holi.
('88', 211, 4, 25, 301626) Blessings from BAPU

('88', 214, 5, 13, 305360) BAPA, I had the circular you wanted to issue about the women village workers I don’t remember now why I did not give then the approval asked for.
('88', 214, 5, 14, 305506) I am sorry there has been this delay.
('88', 214, 5, 15, 305544) I have carefully gone through it.
('88', 214, 5, 16, 305578) Do circulate it.
('88', 214, 5, 17, 305595) Satyabhama Devi’s donation should be accepted if the Pro vincial Committee can make use of it and no burden falls on us.
('88', 214, 5, 18, 305716) I take it that the correspondence, etc., will be put in order.

('88', 214, 5, 20, 305854) It is commendable that facilities are made available by the Hospital.
('88', 214, 5, 21, 305924) But I have my doubts about the utility of such midwives as they will not be able to serve in villages.

('88', 218, 6, 12, 310592) 456. LETTER TO G. D. BIRLA
('88', 218, 7, 13, 310619) October 26, 1945
('88', 218, 8, 14, 310636) GHANSHYAMDAS, I have had Jehangir Patel’s 1 letter.
('88', 218, 8, 15, 310688) He also writes that only the school building would be suitable.
('88', 218, 8, 16, 310752) There should be some more facilities there.
('88', 218, 8, 17, 310796) There should also be provision for electricity and water.
('88', 218, 8, 18, 310854) Dinshaw suggests going straight into the school building when everything is ready.
('88', 218, 8, 19, 310937) In that case it will take nine months.
('88', 218, 8, 20, 310976) I favour moving at once into the sanatorium building and starting work there, and later shifting to the school building when it is ready.
('88', 218, 8, 21, 311114) Whether this is possible or not has to be decided by you people.
('88', 218, 8, 22, 311179) In the sanatorium building also more pipes will be required for water.
('88', 218, 8, 23, 311250) Maybe, something will have to be done about electricity too.
('88', 218, 8, 24, 311311) Water treatment requires plenty of water.
('88', 218, 8, 25, 311353) I see some difficulty in taking the school building.
('88', 218, 8, 26, 311406) If the school is to be housed there, it will be difficult to run two institutions in the same building.
('88', 218, 8, 27, 311510) If my idea takes shape, even the present building may not be enough.
('88', 218, 8, 28, 311579) For, my idea is that the poor also have to be admitted and I shall be interested in running nature cure clinics for them, too.
('88', 218, 8, 29, 311706) It seems to me that from the school building it would also be possible to serve the village people as I have planned to do.
('88', 218, 8, 30, 311830) Think over all this and let me know what you feel would be best to do.
('88', 218, 8, 31, 311901) Let me also give you Sardar’s view.
('88', 218, 8, 32, 311937) He believes that I should not
('88', 218, 9, 33, 311967) 1 A Trustee of the Nature Cure Clinic
('88', 219, 0, 1, 312005) 220 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 219, 1, 2, 312047) interest myself in this work to this extent.
('88', 219, 1, 3, 312092) If Dinshaw requires financial help I should have it provided to him and then stop at it.
('88', 219, 1, 4, 312181) In going further at the moment there is a risk of Dinshaw breaking down or my being disappointed and the great affection which Dinshaw is showing for me today coming to an end.
('88', 219, 1, 5, 312358) I have no such fear.
('88', 219, 1, 6, 312379) In my opinion Dinshaw can break down, but his affection for me cannot wane.
('88', 219, 1, 7, 312455) I know that he had the same affection for me even when no question of money was involved and when I did not even know him.
('88', 219, 1, 8, 312578) But Sardar understands human nature and he has too much consideration for me; so I think it is as well to place his view before you so that you may decide the question objectively.
('88', 219, 1, 9, 312759) Please do not think that just because I have been given assurance about Nasik no other alternative should be considered.
('88', 219, 1, 10, 312880) Nature cure work is of great importance.
('88', 219, 1, 11, 312921) If carried on well it can have far reaching results the scope of which can hardly be envisaged today.
('88', 219, 1, 12, 313023) It must also be considered to what extent Dinshaw can fit into this set up.
('88', 219, 1, 13, 313099) If you think it necessary to see me before taking any decision in the matter and if you can find some time, come and talk it over.
('88', 219, 1, 14, 313230) But if the matter can be settled through correspondence, you need not come.
('88', 219, 1, 15, 313306) In spite of my great interest in this work you should take it that I am acting in a detached way.
('88', 219, 1, 16, 313404) If I am to live for 125 years, there is also this condition that my sense of objectivity, that is, non attachment should increase day by day and approximate as much to perfection as is humanly possible.
('88', 219, 1, 17, 313607) I do not know how this can happen or whether it will happen at all.
('88', 219, 1, 18, 313675) Why should I even wish to know?
('88', 219, 1, 19, 313707) Let me keep that ideal in view and do what I consider to be my duty.
('88', 219, 1, 20, 313776) I know this much that it is difficult to reach that ideal.
('88', 219, 1, 21, 313835) But my life has been spent in tackling difficult tasks.
('88', 219, 2, 22, 313891) Blessings from BAPU

('88', 221, 1, 2, 315768) 459. LETTER TO G. RAMACHANDRA RAO
('88', 221, 2, 3, 315802) NATURE CURE CLINIC, 6 TODIWALA ROAD, POONA, October 27, 1945
('88', 221, 3, 4, 315863) MY DEAR RAMACHANDRA RAO,
('88', 221, 4, 5, 315888) Yours of the 13th to hand.
('88', 221, 5, 6, 315915) 1. Booklet 1 on health is still undergoing revision.
('88', 221, 5, 7, 315968) It was suspended after my premature discharge from jail and I never had the time for finishing it.
('88', 221, 5, 8, 316067) When it is finished you will know of this new publication.
('88', 221, 5, 9, 316126) You can certainly publish a translation.
('88', 221, 5, 10, 316167) It will not be called a new edition.
('88', 221, 5, 11, 316204) It will be, if it is ever published, a new thing altogether.
('88', 221, 5, 12, 316265) 2. There are many claimants for service of labour.
('88', 221, 5, 13, 316316) Unfortunately, Congress monopoly tacitly recognized by all is broken.
('88', 221, 5, 14, 316386) But if the Congress is challenged I suppose the Congress will say we are the only real servants of labour.
('88', 221, 5, 15, 316493) Who will establish the claim finally is in the womb of time.
('88', 221, 5, 16, 316554) My participation in the affairs of the Working Committee is very slight and, I fancy, growing slighter.
('88', 221, 5, 17, 316658) Therefore, don’t expect me to do anything in the matter of the flag designed by you.
('88', 221, 5, 18, 316743) 3. SWEEPERS.
('88', 221, 5, 19, 316756) You and a few others may recognize my claim to be the first sweeper, but I will cut a sorry figure in a sweepers’ conference.
('88', 221, 5, 20, 316882) The so called sweepers will themselves repudiate my claim as many do.
('88', 221, 5, 21, 316952) My sympathy will be with them in such repudiation.
('88', 221, 5, 22, 317003) The fortunate position of a self styled man, however, is that he does not require any outside recognition of a style adopted by himself.
('88', 221, 5, 23, 317140) Therefore, I must not bear the burden of having the conference even when the choice of the venue is left to me.
('88', 221, 5, 24, 317252) What is more, I have neither the time nor the wish to carry more burdens than I have.
('88', 221, 5, 25, 317338) You should therefore go on without counting on my service even in the way of a message.
('88', 221, 5, 26, 317426) Cultivate the belief that every bonafide service carries with it its own recognition.
('88', 221, 6, 27, 317512) 1 Gandhiji had started writing the Key to Health on August 27, 1942, during his incarceration in the Aga Khan Palace and completed it on December 18, 1942. The Gujarati original was translated into Hindustani and English by Sushila Nayyar under Gandhiji’s guidance.
('88', 221, 6, 28, 317778) For Key to Health, vide For Gandhiji’s earlier writings on the subject written in South Africa, .
('88', 221, 6, 29, 317876) These were later published in the form of a booklet under the title A Guide to Health.

('88', 222, 1, 4, 318100) The record you mention is certainly very good but it loses in public dignity and value.

('88', 224, 5, 12, 321877) 464. LETTER TO H. L. SHARMA
('88', 224, 6, 13, 321905) October 27, 1945
('88', 224, 7, 14, 321922) SHARMA, I have your letter written at 12 o’clock at night.
('88', 224, 7, 15, 321981) Your brother is gone.
('88', 224, 7, 16, 322003) From the empirical view it is only natural that you should grieve, but if you take the transcendental view, the integral view, what is there to grieve over in death?
('88', 224, 7, 17, 322169) What is there to rejoice over in birth?
('88', 224, 7, 18, 322209) These two go together, one must follow the other and the two are inseparably linked.
('88', 224, 7, 19, 322294) Hence at least to you death should cause no sorrow.
('88', 224, 7, 20, 322346) You have an added reason for devoting yourself to your duty.
('88', 224, 7, 21, 322407) It is all the more regrettable that you thought of going into the Assembly at the suggestion of your deceased brother.
('88', 224, 7, 22, 322526) About Gadodiaji, if you stick to everything [you have said] write to me point by point as 1, 2, 3. I am willing to send them to him.
('88', 224, 7, 23, 322659) I shall also suggest that they should be placed before an arbitrator.
('88', 224, 7, 24, 322729) These should cover all the complaints you had made to me.
('88', 224, 7, 25, 322787) The decision about other things may well depend on it, though now I must confess I have my suspicions.
('88', 224, 7, 26, 322890) I cannot write anything about Sardar because he and Dinshawji are in Bombay.
('88', 224, 7, 27, 322967) They will return on the 1st.
('88', 224, 7, 28, 322996) With the elder brother gone, who is shouldering the responsibility of the household?
('88', 224, 7, 29, 323081) How many brothers are you?
('88', 224, 8, 30, 323108) Blessings from BAPU

('88', 227, 1, 2, 325682) 469. LETTER TO MRS.
('88', 227, 1, 3, 325702) M. H. MORRISON 1
('88', 227, 2, 4, 325719) NATURE CURE CLINIC, 5 TODIWALA ROAD, POONA, October 28, 1945
('88', 227, 3, 5, 325780) DEAR MADAM, I have just received your letter of 20th September, and I have devoured almost every line of the enclosure to your letter.
('88', 227, 3, 6, 325915) Miss Slade whom we know here as Mirabai only, as she desires to be known, is in a basin of the Himalayas which she adores and loves.
('88', 227, 3, 7, 326048) It is near Hardwar, a celebrated place of pilgrimage, through which the mighty Ganges flows down.
('88', 227, 3, 8, 326146) Your Green Cross scheme appeals to me forcibly, not that there is anything new in it for me.
('88', 227, 3, 9, 326239) Your resolution is also brief and to the point, and therefore is a temptation and invitation for me to sign.
('88', 227, 3, 10, 326348) But I must resist the temptation.
('88', 227, 3, 11, 326382) The Green Cross Society will, I hope, forgive me for the resistance.
('88', 227, 3, 12, 326451) It will do so readily if it appreciates the fact that some, among whom I count myself, render greater help by refraining from signing anything like your resolution but working silently and probably effectively.
('88', 227, 3, 13, 326662) Though I refrain from sending you my signature I will ask you, if you at all can, to keep me in touch with your activities from time to time.
('88', 227, 3, 14, 326804) It may interest and even please you to know that I have enforced in my own life now for years your ‘ten don’ts’ 2 andinvited my neighbours to do likewise for I have long believed that there is a ‘spirit in the wood’, using the word ‘wood’ in a double sense.
('88', 227, 4, 15, 327062) Yours sincerely, MRS.
('88', 227, 4, 16, 327084) M. H. MORRISON HON.
('88', 227, 4, 17, 327104) SECRETARY THE GREEN CROSS SOCIETY 41 ASMUNS PLACE, LONDON N.W. 11 From a copy: Pyarelal Papers.

('88', 228, 1, 2, 328037) 470. LETTER TO ANNIE MASCARENE
('88', 228, 2, 3, 328068) Not for publication NATURE CURE CLINIC, 6 TODIWALA ROAD, POONA, October 28, 1945 DEAR MASCARENE, In continuation of the receipt of your resolution, you will not expect me to express any opinion because just now I have, so far as it is possible, steeled my heart against any expression of opinion.
('88', 228, 2, 4, 328365) I have not studied the question of primary education in Travancore so as to satisfy myself, and I observe that many persons of note have expressed emphatic views one way or the other.
('88', 228, 2, 5, 328549) I do not feel called upon to say anything.
('88', 228, 2, 6, 328592) Why did you drag my sister and her daughter ?
('88', 228, 2, 7, 328638) My sister is wholly illiterate.
('88', 228, 2, 8, 328670) Her daughter can with difficulty read or write something.
('88', 228, 2, 9, 328728) But neither takes any interest in public matters.
('88', 228, 2, 10, 328778) It is fraud upon the public to put such ignorant persons on the platform and make them repeat things parrot like, leading the public to believe that some good work has been done.
('88', 228, 2, 11, 328957) I felt sorry when I first heard that my sister had been dragged out of her merited obscurity in which she was happy and contented.
('88', 228, 2, 12, 329088) She has now come to me being on her way back to Rajkot.
('88', 228, 2, 13, 329144) She tells me that she had not the slightest intention of going to a meeting or sending her daughter.
('88', 228, 2, 14, 329245) She allowed herself to be tempted to go to Rameshwaram as a point of pilgrimage.
('88', 228, 2, 15, 329326) She had intended also to remain obscure and not let the people know that she was my sister.
('88', 228, 2, 16, 329418) If she had asked me I would have dissuaded her even from going to Rameshwaram, for I have no faith in these pilgrimages except under certain conditions.
('88', 228, 2, 17, 329571) But what is done cannot be undone.
('88', 228, 2, 18, 329606) I would how ever like you to give me your version of the story, so that I can have full facts enabling me to come to a right judgment, for I do not want to do yo any injustice by making up my mind on insufficient data.
('88', 228, 2, 19, 329825) Please therefore enlighten me.
('88', 228, 2, 20, 329856) And who was the party who wrote out the speech that my sister’s daughter read without understanding it?
('88', 228, 2, 21, 329960) Yours, BAPU MISS A. MASCARENE STATE CONGRESS OFFICE TRIVANDRUM From a copy: Pyarelal Papers.

('88', 229, 1, 2, 330179) 471. LETTER TO DAHYALAL H. JANI.
('88', 229, 2, 3, 330212) October 28, 1945
('88', 229, 3, 4, 330229) BHAI DAHYALAL, Don’t be angry with me but have a hearty laugh.
('88', 229, 3, 5, 330292) I don’t know who told me or where I read it or what happened but somehow I had the illusion that you had died.
('88', 229, 3, 6, 330403) Later one day when I saw Kishorelal revising your translation of the Gita, I came to know that you were alive and I was happy about it.
('88', 229, 3, 7, 330539) But I forgot about this and thought you were dead.
('88', 229, 3, 8, 330590) Meanwhile yesterday your letter came and now this won’t leave my mind.
('88', 229, 3, 9, 330661) So now you have to live long.
('88', 229, 3, 10, 330691) But l know that you may live beyond me, that is, you may live for more than 125 years, and yet will remain what you are now.
('88', 229, 3, 11, 330816) Isn’t that as good as being dead even when alive?
('88', 229, 3, 12, 330866) This is the impression I have got after reading your letter.
('88', 229, 3, 13, 330927) There is nothing new in what you have said about the five things.
('88', 229, 3, 14, 330993) Of course, there is some truth in it but according to me it is so full of ignorance that I have not found any one of them useful.
('88', 229, 3, 15, 331123) Your last sentence is: “If there is any service that I can do, do order me.” How incorrect this sentence is!
('88', 229, 3, 16, 331232) I did order you to do a lot of service and what did I get from it?
('88', 229, 3, 17, 331299) What could the country achieve or what benefit did you get?
('88', 229, 3, 18, 331359) Think over the other four things in the same way.
('88', 229, 3, 19, 331409) There is no need for a reply and this should not be published on anyaccount.
('88', 229, 3, 20, 331486) I have written this just to humour you in the hope that it may open your eyes one day.
('88', 229, 3, 21, 331573) If any time you are able to understand the hidden meaning behind it I would think it is better than getting your reply and would consider your living meaningful.

('88', 232, 2, 3, 335219) Let me add this much to the above 2. The verses originally included in this primer were those I had selected for Ramdas.
('88', 232, 2, 4, 335340) 3 Friends have added so much to it that it would be a departure from truth to call it “Rama Gita” or to attribute its compilation to me.

('88', 232, 4, 9, 335705) 479. LETTER TO E. M. JENKINS NATURE CURE CLINIC, 6 TODIWALA ROAD, POONA, October 29, 1945 DEAR SIR EVAN, This I write in fear and trembling, lest I may be overstepping my limit.
('88', 232, 4, 10, 335883) I am watching the progress of the trial of the members of the corps raised by or under Shri Subhas Babu.
('88', 232, 4, 11, 335988) Though I can have nothing in common with any defence by force of arms, I am never blind to the valour and patriotism often displayed by persons in arms, as seems to be the case here.
('88', 232, 4, 12, 336171) And can the Government afford to ignore the almost, if not the wholly, unanimous opinion of Indians of all shades of opinion?
('88', 232, 4, 13, 336297) India adores these men who are on their trial.
('88', 232, 4, 14, 336344) No doubt theGovernment have overwhelming might on their side.
('88', 232, 4, 15, 336406) But it will be misuse of that power if it is used in the teeth of universal Indian opposition.
('88', 232, 4, 16, 336501) It is not for me to say what should be done except that what is being done is not the way.
('88', 232, 4, 17, 336592) Let His Excellency decide what is best in the circumstances.
('88', 232, 5, 18, 336653) Yours sincerely, M. K. GANDHI
('88', 232, 6, 19, 336683) Gandhiji’s Correspondence with the Government, 1944 47, PP.

('88', 233, 1, 2, 337288) 480. LETTER TO E. M. JENKINS
('88', 233, 2, 3, 337317) NATURE CURE CLINIC, 6 TODIWALA ROAD, POONA, October 29, 1945
('88', 233, 3, 4, 337378) DEAR SIR EVAN, In continuation of my letter 1 of October 10, 1945, about khadi being licensed, may I add that the Privy Council had to consider the question of exempting the A.I.S.A. from the income tax.
('88', 233, 3, 5, 337582) The case is reported in A. I. R. 1944 Privy Council at p.
('88', 233, 3, 6, 337640) 88. His Excellency’s predecessor had at my request ordered that the collection of the tax be suspended, pending decision of the Privy Council.
('88', 233, 3, 7, 337783) 2 It reversed the decision of the Bombay High Court and expressed the opinion that the primary object of the Association is the relief of the poor, that its objects include the advancement of other purposes of general public utility and that the making of a commercial or private profit is not the purpose of the Association.
('88', 233, 3, 8, 338109) On these grounds they came to the conclusion that the Association is a charitable and philanthropic body and entitled to exemption from tax.
('88', 233, 3, 9, 338250) Can khadi manufactured and sold on behalf of the manufacturers—the profits, if any, going to the hand spinners and handloom weavers—be classed with mill cloth under the Anti Profiteering and Hoarding Regulations?
('88', 233, 3, 10, 338463) In my humbleopinion, it should be wholly exempt from such control, if the meagre earnings of the poor concerned are not to be taxed.
('88', 233, 4, 11, 338596) Yours sincerely, M. K. GANDHI
('88', 233, 5, 12, 338626) Gandhiji’s Correspondence with the Government, 1944 47 p.

('88', 234, 4, 13, 339469) 482. LETTER TO C. RAJAGOPALACHARI
('88', 234, 5, 14, 339503) [October 29, 1945] 2

('88', 238, 0, 1, 344462) VOL.88: 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 239
('88', 238, 1, 2, 344507) 490. DRAFT FOR CONGRESS CONSTITUTION
('88', 238, 2, 3, 344544) [On or after October 29, 1945] 1
('88', 238, 3, 4, 344577) 1. Constructive programme is the chief plank for winning Swaraj by truthful and non violent means.
('88', 238, 3, 5, 344676) Its full execution means complete independence.
('88', 238, 3, 6, 344724) But so long as the millions of India do not take to it, Parliamentary programme will remain as a supplement.
('88', 238, 3, 7, 344833) 2. The method of enrolment of Congress membership has been useful and Congress has been able to do a lot of good work.
('88', 238, 3, 8, 344952) But many defects have crept in.
('88', 238, 3, 9, 344984) Therefore, in future the Congress will consist of workers or servants of the nation only.
('88', 238, 3, 10, 345074) Any man or woman above the age of sixteen can become a Congress worker, provided he or she is a habitual wearer of khadi certified by the A.I.S.A. and pays a monthly fee of 1,920 rounds of handspun yarn to the Congress.
('88', 238, 3, 11, 345294) The spinners should be conversant with all the processes from picking cotton pods from the field to the point of making slivers and producing yarn.
('88', 238, 3, 12, 345442) They should also know how to put a spinning wheel in order.
('88', 238, 3, 13, 345502) 3. The Congress shall make it a point of duty to penetrate the 7,00,000 villages of India.
('88', 238, 3, 14, 345593) At least one Congress worker shall stay in each village and do the following: (a) He shall come in personal contact with every villager and keep a list of their names along with those of the other members of their families.
('88', 238, 3, 15, 345817) (b) He will enrol and train Congress workers from amongst the villagers themselves and keep a register of all those who come on the roll.
('88', 238, 3, 16, 345955) These shall form the Village Congress Committee.
('88', 238, 3, 17, 346004) (c) He shall keep a record of his work from day to day.
('88', 238, 3, 18, 346060) (d) It is possible that obstacles might be placed in his way by the Government or by the villagers themselves.
('88', 238, 3, 19, 346171) He shall fight all difficulties by truthful and non violent action even though he might perish in the attempt.
('88', 238, 3, 20, 346282) (e) He shall organize the villages so as to make them self contained and self supporting through their agriculture and handicrafts, treating the manufacture of Khadi as the centre, in accordance with the lines laid down by the A.I.S.A., A.I.V.I.A. and the Goseva Sangh.
('88', 238, 4, 21, 346552) 1 From the reference to Gandhiji’s drafting the Constitution of the Congress; vide “Letter to Kishorelal G. Mashruwala”, 29 10 1945
('88', 239, 0, 1, 346684) 240 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 239, 1, 2, 346726) (f) He shall organize sanitation and hygiene among the villagers and take all measures for prevention of disease among them.
('88', 239, 1, 3, 346851) (g) He shall organize the education of the villagers from birth to death along the lines of Nayee Talim, in accordance with the policy laid down by the Hindustani Talimi Sangh.
('88', 239, 1, 4, 347028) (h) For the above purposes and others to be added from time to time by the Congress, he shall train and fit himself for the due performance of duty, in accordance with the rules laid down by the Congress for time to time.
('88', 239, 1, 5, 347250) 4. The Congress shall take part in the elections in all Goverment managed or controlled institutions, beginning with the Village Panchayat to the Central Legislative Assembly and Council.
('88', 239, 1, 6, 347438) 5. The Congress shall contact all those who are on the Government’s voters’ list, and (a) will give them an idea of their duties and their rights, (b) shall produce the necessary literature for their education, (c) shall make arrangements to impart literacy to the illiterate amongst them.
('88', 239, 1, 7, 347728) (d) shall see that those whose names are missing on the Government registers are duly entered therein.
('88', 239, 1, 8, 347831) (e) shall encourage those who are legally unqualified for the franchise to acquire the necessary qualifications for getting the right.
('88', 239, 1, 9, 347966) (f) shall carry on agitation for adult franchise for all inhabitants of India who are not proved lunatics or otherwise unfit workers.
('88', 239, 1, 10, 348100) 6. Out of the existing workers the Congress shall maintain a Central Board of volunteers whose sole and special duty will be to reach help to and protect, in accordance with Truth and Non violence, the people in cases of rioting, stealing, robbery and like emergencies.
('88', 239, 1, 11, 348370) To this end the Congress shall conduct a teaching institution.
('88', 239, 1, 12, 348433) 7. The Congress shall run a Languages School so as to enable Congressmen and women to learn the national language (i.e., Hindustani spoken by the villagers–Hindus, Muslims and others in the villages of the North and written in the Nagari or Urdu script) and other Indian languages.
('88', 239, 1, 13, 348715) This work is to be done along the lines of the Hindustani Prachar Sabha and Bharatiya Bhawan.
('88', 239, 1, 14, 348809) 8. Representative Village Congress Sabhas being one per not less than 1000 voters and of workers being one per 1000 workers shall form the A.I.C.C. 9. The Indian National Congress will comprise: (1) Village Congress Committee
('88', 240, 0, 1, 349035) VOL.88: 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 241
('88', 240, 1, 2, 349080) (2) A.I.C.C. (3) Working Committee of the Congress (4) A.I.S.A. (5) A.I.V.I.A. (6) Hindustani Talimi Sangh (7) Institution for Removal of Untouchability (8) Anti Intoxicant Association (9) Labour Union (10) Kisan Union 10. The A.I.C.C. shall frame rules for smooth working of the constitution and for matter left unprovided for herein.
('88', 240, 2, 3, 349416) From a copy: Pyarelal Papers.
('88', 240, 2, 4, 349446) Nehru Memorial Museum and Library.
('88', 240, 2, 5, 349481) Courtesy: Beladevi Nayyar and Dr. Sushila Nayyar
('88', 240, 3, 6, 349530) 491. REFLECTIONS ON CONGRESS CONSTITUTION [On or after October 29, 1945] 1
('88', 240, 4, 7, 349605) I am becoming more and more convinced that the four anna membership should go.
('88', 240, 4, 8, 349684) The membership of the Congress should be forty crores, the whole of the population, no matter to what sect, religion or province or state or the so called independent possessions a particular individual belongs.
('88', 240, 4, 9, 349896) The members have an equal right with all to service by the Congress organization.
('88', 240, 4, 10, 349978) These forty crore members will exercise no privilege by reason of their recognition as such by the Congress.
('88', 240, 4, 11, 350087) The organization will be worked by those who are habitual wearers of khaddar one year before the date of commencement, who have renounced untouchability in all its forms and who are not dealers in foreign cloth or intoxicants, who have full belief in the constructive programme of the Congress and who are prepared and willing to do work referred to in Schedule A hereto and who have passed a probation period of six months in doing that work.
('88', 240, 4, 12, 350531) All Committees and sub committees shall be formed from the workers above named.
('88', 240, 4, 13, 350611) The Schedules to be prepared by P.

('88', 244, 11, 17, 354891) 502. LETTER TO CHHAGANLAL JOSHI
('88', 244, 12, 18, 354923) October 31, 1945
('88', 244, 13, 19, 354940) CHHAGANLAL, I have your letter.
('88', 244, 13, 20, 354972) While I was talking to Narandas about the money from the States, he promptly said, “Certainly stop it if you wish to.” Now we shall think over it when we meet.
('88', 244, 13, 21, 355132) I have received the money from Wankaner.
('88', 244, 13, 22, 355173) I shall send it to you as I received it—in two instalments and under insured cover.
('88', 244, 13, 23, 355257) I understand about Tryambaklal Choksi’s donation.
('88', 244, 13, 24, 355307) Just now I am not writing a letter of thanks.
('88', 244, 13, 25, 355353) I don’t approve of the condition laid down by him.
('88', 244, 13, 26, 355404) How can we have a trust for such a small amount?
('88', 244, 13, 27, 355453) Why does he not have faith in an institution like the Harijan Sevak Sangh?
('88', 244, 13, 28, 355528) And why all this fuss about making a trust?
('88', 244, 13, 29, 355572) He can give the shares to Harijan Sevak Sangh on condition that the money received from the shares will be utilized as decided by the Sangh for the Harijans of Sorath.
('88', 244, 13, 30, 355740) I also believe that if we can get more money by selling the
('88', 245, 0, 1, 355800) 246 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 245, 1, 2, 355842) shares, the Sangh should have the right to do so.
('88', 245, 1, 3, 355892) Think over this and discuss this with Tryambaklal if you wish to.
('88', 245, 1, 4, 355958) You can convey to Bapa my opinion about this.

('88', 246, 13, 29, 358575) You have laboured very hard.

('88', 247, 1, 5, 358840) There is one thing you must do.
('88', 247, 1, 6, 358872) What can there be personal with people like us ?
('88', 247, 1, 7, 358921) Are you any more an individual ?
('88', 247, 1, 8, 358954) If you continue to be an individual, it is not for writing personal things, but to preserve your individuality, which is done only when you reduce yourself to a zero and remain a zero.
('88', 247, 1, 9, 359139) If you do not know this, then follow my exeprience if you can.
('88', 247, 1, 10, 359202) Where there is ‘I’, there is individuality.
('88', 247, 1, 11, 359246) It is only when ‘I’ is eliminated, that individuality ceases to exist.
('88', 247, 1, 12, 359317) Take the letter ‘I’ of the English alphabet.
('88', 247, 1, 13, 359362) So long as it is straight, it appears like a scare crow.
('88', 247, 1, 14, 359419) If it wants to efface itself and realize its individuality it must turn itself into a cipher.

('88', 247, 1, 21, 359809) I know that even a long experience can be wrong.

('88', 247, 1, 23, 359912) Kanu agrees that what I have written to the Kasturba Nidhi about Bapa is correct, because Thakkar Bapa was instrumental in this.

('88', 250, 3, 7, 363938) 513. A THOUGHT FOR THE DAY 1
('88', 250, 4, 8, 363967) July 17, 1945 A man of the world can as little comprehend the universe as a fish living in the ocean can fathom its depths.
('88', 250, 4, 9, 364091) July 18, 1945 Not to do evil is the only true law of life, says Guru Teg July 19, 1945 Life is unreal, death is real and certain.
('88', 250, 4, 10, 364221) —Nanak July 20, 1945 Truth can be found by searching within, never through argument or disputation.
('88', 250, 4, 11, 364321) It is just the same if for ‘Truth’ one reads ‘God’.
('88', 250, 4, 12, 364373) July 21, 1945 Nanak says: “God dwells in every human heart, and so every heart is a temple of God.” July 22, 1945 If God resides in every heart, then who dare hate whom?
('88', 250, 4, 13, 364543) July 23, 1945 Nanak says: “If we obey the law of God, we then need no man made laws.” July 24, 1945 Nanak says: “God has ordained that all of us in this world itself are one family and each of us has to live for others,” July 25, 1945 The darkness of egoism is more impenetrable than darkness itself.
('88', 250, 5, 14, 364844) 1 At the request of Anand T. Hingorani and to comfort him Gandhiji had started the practice of writing a thought daily from November 20, 1944
('88', 251, 0, 1, 364986) 252 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 251, 1, 2, 365028) July 26, 1945 How shall we dispel this darkness of egoism?
('88', 251, 1, 3, 365087) By the light of uttermost humility.
('88', 251, 1, 4, 365123) July 27, 1945 Sorrow is but another aspect of joy.
('88', 251, 1, 5, 365174) Hence the one invariably follows the other.
('88', 251, 1, 6, 365218) July 28, 1945 Just as joy and sorrow are a pair that follow each other, in succession, so is the case with all things in life.
('88', 251, 1, 7, 365345) Consequently, to have real peace of mind, we must rise above such pairs of opposites.
('88', 251, 1, 8, 365431) July 29, 1945 How can he who realizes not the true value of the Self, nor is able to protect it, protect anything else in life?
('88', 251, 1, 9, 365559) July 30, 1945 Even one word, if true, is enough.
('88', 251, 1, 10, 365608) Untrue words, however many, are worth nothing.
('88', 251, 1, 11, 365655) July 31, 1945 The power of a true word is such that it leads one from selfishness to selflessness.
('88', 251, 1, 12, 365754) August 1, 1945 He alone lives in whose heart dwells Rama (God) and who is ever aware of such presence.
('88', 251, 1, 13, 365857) August 2, 1945 Real knowledge cannot be acquired by mere reading of the scriptures.
('88', 251, 1, 14, 365941) Indeed, it is difficult of attainment without the practice of virtue.
('88', 251, 1, 15, 366011) August 3, 1945 One can never find Truth if one is not wide awake every moment of one’s life.
('88', 251, 1, 16, 366104) August 4, 1945 There can be no such thing as rights for a satyagrahi.
('88', 251, 1, 17, 366174) For him there is only one right—the right to serve.
('88', 251, 1, 18, 366226) August 5, 1945 Therefore, a satyagrahi will never seek rights; these will come to him unsought.
('88', 251, 1, 19, 366322) August 6, 1945 Even one drop of the poison of untruth will poison the entire milk ocean of Truth.
('88', 252, 0, 1, 366420) VOL.88: 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 253
('88', 252, 1, 2, 366465) August 7, 1945 Nanak says: “Man is born of woman as woman is born of man.” Then, why is it that we find sexual immorality in the world?
('88', 252, 1, 3, 366601) August 8, 1945 Nanak lay in the open under the sky.
('88', 252, 1, 4, 366653) A kind hearted householder suggested to him, “There is a beautiful dharmsala nearby.
('88', 252, 1, 5, 366738) Why not go there?” Nanak replied: “The whole earth is my dharmsala and the sky is its roof.” August 9, 1945 Nanak says: “The craving for happiness is a veritable disease.
('88', 252, 1, 6, 366909) Sorrow or suffering is its remedy.” August 10, 1945 Says Nanak again: “Whatever you give away is yours; whatever you keep is not yours.” August 11, 1945 Whatever we take, we are snatching from the mouths of others.
('88', 252, 1, 7, 367124) Therefore, whenever we acquire anything, let us see that it is really needed and that our wants are as few as possible.
('88', 252, 1, 8, 367244) August 12, 1945 Nanak says: “He who earns his bread by the sweat of his brow and shares with others what he so earns, can be called truly honest.” August 13, 1945 Nanak says: “The more one indulges oneself, the more unhappy one becomes.” August 14, 1945 St. Catherine of Italy had no money with her.
('88', 252, 1, 9, 367544) She had only a cloak which she was wearing.
('88', 252, 1, 10, 367588) A destitute asked for it and she gave it away.
('88', 252, 1, 11, 367635) Someone, thereupon, asked her: “How will you go about now?” She replied: “The raiment of love will cover me far more securely than the cloak.” August 15, 1945 Money alone can keep memory green—how much harm this false notion has done!
('88', 252, 1, 12, 367870) This thought occurs to me today on the anniversary of Mahadev [Desai].
('88', 252, 1, 13, 367941) August 16, 1945 Nanak says: “Dreams are evidence of the fact that the atma (soul) uses the senses as its instruments.
('88', 252, 1, 14, 368059) But it is only when the atma
('88', 253, 0, 1, 368088) 254 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 253, 1, 2, 368130) keeps the senses under control that they become its instruments, and the atma then becomes ripe for union with the Paramatma.” August 17, 1945 The pangs of hunger are not relieved by filling the stomach.
('88', 253, 1, 3, 368334) They can be overcome by taking a limited quantity of food, like medicine, and remaining content with it.
('88', 253, 1, 4, 368439) August 18, 1945 Fear vanishes only with the annihilation of the ego.
('88', 253, 1, 5, 368508) August 19, 1945 It is an ordeal nowadays to read the newspapers.
('88', 253, 1, 6, 368573) They do not give correct news.
('88', 253, 1, 7, 368604) Nothing would be lost by not reading them.
('88', 253, 1, 8, 368647) August 20, 1945 It is as difficult to make the impossible possible, as it is easy to make the possible impossible.
('88', 253, 1, 9, 368762) August 21, 1945 What seems impossible is not always really so.
('88', 253, 1, 10, 368825) August 22, 1945 One person has God on his side; millions have Satan on theirs.
('88', 253, 1, 11, 368904) Must, therefore, one fear the millions?
('88', 253, 1, 12, 368944) August 23, 1945 Supposing God is on the side of both, then who should fear whom?

('88', 253, 1, 17, 369330) August 28, 1945 Because of our physical limitations, we cannot have a conception of the existence of God.

('88', 254, 1, 2, 369481) August 29, 1945 How can one believe in Truth if one has no belief in nonviolence?
('88', 254, 1, 3, 369563) If non violence is not put into practice, Truth, too, cannot be.

('88', 254, 1, 6, 369890) If all that he does is informed with knowledge, it is action indeed.

('88', 254, 1, 8, 370075) September 2, 1945 One man commits a theft, another aids and abets it, while the third only harbours the intention to commit it.

('88', 262, 10, 20, 381684) Right from my childhood I have lived with Muslims and when I went to London Providence placed me in close association with Christians, Muslims and Parsis.
('88', 262, 10, 21, 381839) Hindus of course were there.
('88', 262, 10, 22, 381868) I came into contact with the intellectuals among them and that is how I read the holy books of all the four religions.
('88', 262, 10, 23, 381987) I came to the conclusion that we could know the true facts about any religion only after reading its sacred books.
('88', 262, 10, 24, 382102) I also read quite a few criticisms of them.
('88', 262, 10, 25, 382146) I can say that I have also read the Muslim critics you mention in your letter.
('88', 262, 10, 26, 382225) I had a talk with Muslims in South Africa about those books and also with an Englishman who had become Muslim.
('88', 262, 10, 27, 382336) After coming here I read the works of Maulana Shibli.
('88', 262, 10, 28, 382390) As a result I have realized that every religion contains both truth and untruth.

('88', 266, 1, 2, 387526) 525. LETTER TO BHARATAN KUMARAPPA
('88', 266, 2, 3, 387560) NATURE CURE CLINIC, POONA, November 2, 1945
('88', 266, 3, 4, 387604) MY DEAR BHARATAN,
('88', 266, 4, 5, 387622) I had your letter yesterday.
('88', 266, 4, 6, 387651) You have given a cautious and judicious opinion on Bhailal’s 1
('88', 266, 5, 7, 387714) project.
('88', 266, 5, 8, 387723) That is not what I wanted exactly from you.
('88', 266, 5, 9, 387767) Did I tell you that I lent him your book 2 in typescript, which you gave me to read for my foreword, and he cock suredly told me that his scheme was exactly in conformity with your thesis?
('88', 266, 5, 10, 387956) I said to him, and I repeat it now, that if I have understood your thesis correctly, his project is quite contrary to the letter and the spirit of your thesis.
('88', 266, 5, 11, 388116) The rule of thumb that I applied was to know whether his scheme would succeed if it was multiplied to the extent of covering 700,000 villages.
('88', 266, 5, 12, 388259) And my answer was it could not succeed within a measurable distance of time.
('88', 266, 5, 13, 388336) This fundamental objection is apart from the fact that he, a tried engineer and therefore an accurate man, has dared to build his scheme largely on his calculation that people will do this and that and the other thing will come true.
('88', 266, 5, 14, 388570) If what I have said is true and really flows from your book, as it does from my instinctive belief, you have to say so in black and white.
('88', 266, 5, 15, 388709) If my argument is sound, the way to amend your opinion is to supplement what you have given already by adding that, according to your book as interpreted by you, the project is bound to fail in terms of the millions, and is likely to fail even within the limited compass, because he has built largely upon speculations, a thing which a tried engineer should never do.
('88', 266, 5, 16, 389077) Did you also notice that his project contemplates a mill 3 split up into fragments, owned by the villagers or one intelligent villager?
('88', 266, 5, 17, 389213) Just think what it means.
('88', 266, 5, 18, 389239) It must resolve itself into one gigantic State owned mill or mills centrally situated.
('88', 266, 5, 19, 389326) In other words, 700,000 villages must be converted into 700 or 70 cities.
('88', 266, 5, 20, 389400) In still other words, a large portion of the population must die of starvation, famine and the like or be cut to pieces by the sword or
('88', 266, 6, 21, 389536) 1 Bhailalbhai Patel, an enthusiast of rural development through application of modern technology; he later became leader of the Swatantra Party in Gujarat.
('88', 266, 6, 22, 389692) Vide also “Letter to Bhailalbhai Patel”, 26 12 1945. 2 Capitalism, Socialism or Villagism ?

('88', 268, 3, 11, 392796) 527. LETTER TO NARAHARI D. PARIKH
('88', 268, 4, 12, 392830) November 2, 1945
('88', 268, 5, 13, 392847) NARAHARI,
('88', 268, 6, 14, 392857) Your questions are very good.
('88', 268, 6, 15, 392887) This much is clear to me: whether public institutions have members of different religious persuasions or not, members belonging to the majority communities cannot celebrate their festivals in a manner which would hurt the religious sentiments of others.
('88', 268, 6, 16, 393141) The Ganapati festival, and such others, are entirely of a political character and have nothing to do with religion.
('88', 268, 6, 17, 393257) We cannot, therefore, celebrate them.
('88', 268, 6, 18, 393295) But celebrations which are part of religious practice must be observed.
('88', 268, 6, 19, 393367) For instance, in the Ashram Imam Saheb used to give, at my instance and request, the call to the faithful and we used to pray.
('88', 268, 6, 20, 393494) The call is an essential practice in Islam.
('88', 268, 6, 21, 393538) It is believed to be superior to the Church bell of the Christians.
('88', 268, 6, 22, 393606) I think I have now answered your question regarding public institutions.
('88', 268, 6, 23, 393679) If I have left out any point, please ask again.
('88', 268, 6, 24, 393727) It is not easy to answer the question what should be done now regarding Hindu practices.
('88', 268, 6, 25, 393816) It is very easy for me to describe what I myself do.
('88', 268, 6, 26, 393869) And I am also quite clear in my mind about the correctness of what I do.
('88', 268, 6, 27, 393942) But I am not so clear how far the Hindu community should go or which reforms to advocate even in the face

('88', 269, 1, 4, 394296) I could not accept this.

('88', 269, 1, 6, 394399) The Ganapati also is an imaginary figure and stands merely for “Aum”.

('88', 269, 1, 9, 394766) There is much in the Arya Samaj that I love, but I just cannot accept Satyarthaprakash as scripture.

('88', 275, 4, 10, 405954) 535. THE CHARKHA SANGH AND POLITICS
('88', 275, 5, 11, 405990) A khadi worker has sent the above letter 1 to Jajuji, Secretary of the Charkha Sangh.
('88', 275, 5, 12, 406076) He has forwarded it to me to discuss it in Khadi Jagat and to give my opinion on it.
('88', 275, 5, 13, 406161) The Charkha Sangh is not a small organization.
('88', 275, 5, 14, 406208) Even today the workers or the servants—whatever you call them—of the Sangh are to be found all over India.
('88', 275, 5, 15, 406315) Their number is about 3,000. I consider this a small number.
('88', 275, 5, 16, 406376) Their number should increase considerably when khadi spreads in the country.
('88', 275, 5, 17, 406453) Even if we have one worker for every village, the number of workers on the rolls of the Charkha Sangh should be 700,000. This requires a lot of money.
('88', 275, 5, 18, 406604) But from this one should not conclude that it is impossible to have so many workers.
('88', 275, 5, 19, 406689) I have never believed that.
('88', 275, 5, 20, 406717) When the cause is good and there is a spirit of service among the workers the money is always found.
('88', 275, 5, 21, 406818) I have founded and conducted insitutions all my life.
('88', 275, 5, 22, 406872) In my experience there has not been a single institution which was closed down or which could not make progress for want of money.
('88', 275, 5, 23, 407003) On the contrary I have found that some institutions ceased functioning or could not make progress for want of workers.
('88', 275, 5, 24, 407122) You should not ask how, if not on the strength of money, big factories function and recruitment to the Government offices is made.
('88', 275, 5, 25, 407253) Those who do not understand fully what I have said above, raise such doubts.
('88', 275, 5, 26, 407330) I never said that money could serve no purpose.
('88', 275, 5, 27, 407378) If money served no purpose how could we have become its slaves?
('88', 275, 5, 28, 407442) I would go to the extent of saying that without money we cannot go ahead.
('88', 275, 5, 29, 407516) But what I want to say is that if we want to become slaves of money we should give up the
('88', 275, 6, 30, 407606) 1 Not reproduced here.

('88', 276, 1, 2, 407821) idea of serving the people.
('88', 276, 1, 3, 407849) And it is the lot of slaves to be suppressed.
('88', 276, 1, 4, 407895) If however we consider money as our slave and use it as a means and that too for rendering service, then we are making good use of it.
('88', 276, 1, 5, 408030) For the work of service, our first and indispensable need is workers and when we have such workers money will come chasing them.
('88', 276, 1, 6, 408159) They will not have to go in search of money.
('88', 276, 1, 7, 408204) That is why I say if we get seven lakh or even more workers we may take it as though we had the money in the safe.
('88', 276, 1, 8, 408319) It may be said that we do not pay enough to tempt or attract workers.
('88', 276, 1, 9, 408389) I admit it.
('88', 276, 1, 10, 408401) But it is only the spirit that matters.
('88', 276, 1, 11, 408441) Those who join such philanthropic institutions as the Charkha Sangh do so for the sake of service and not for salaries.
('88', 276, 1, 12, 408561) They do take monthly salaries because like the rich the poor too have to feed themselves, but they do so only to keep themselves alive and fit for service.
('88', 276, 1, 13, 408717) Such workers do not eat or drink or dress merely for pleasure.
('88', 276, 1, 14, 408780) If we assume that such are the workers of the Charkha Sangh then they do not have any time to take part in politics.
('88', 276, 1, 15, 408897) The Charkha Sangh cannot function at all if the workers devote eight hours to office work and spend the rest of thetime in pleasure or otherwise.
('88', 276, 1, 16, 409043) Because they are the people who will make or mar the Sangh.
('88', 276, 1, 17, 409103) Therefore they should devote their spare time to making themselves more competent for improving its activities, such as learning all the processes of khadi making, studying its science, and doing well all that they do.
('88', 276, 1, 18, 409322) This does not mean that the workers of the Charkha Sangh have no interest in politics or other activities.
('88', 276, 1, 19, 409429) They are and should be interested in such activities.
('88', 276, 1, 20, 409483) However, they should keep that interest in check and give expression to it through their work in the Charkha Sangh.
('88', 276, 1, 21, 409599) Then only can they understand true politics.
('88', 276, 1, 22, 409644) A Charkha Sangh worker will remain a true voter and will vote for the candidate put up by the Congress but he will not bother to canvass for him.
('88', 276, 1, 23, 409790) He will not deliver speeches supporting him.
('88', 276, 1, 24, 409835) He will not devote his time to such work.
('88', 276, 1, 25, 409877) Congress work is peoples’ work.
('88', 276, 1, 26, 409909) The Congress belongs to the people.
('88', 276, 1, 27, 409945) The Charkha Sangh has been created by the Congress and the Charkha Sangh also belongs to the people.
('88', 276, 1, 28, 410046) Just as political work is Congress work the Sangh work is also Congress work.
('88', 276, 1, 29, 410124) How can a man ride two horses at the same time?
('88', 276, 1, 30, 410172) One who joins the Charkha Sangh should devote himself wholly to its activities and one who joins politics should devote his entire time to politics.
('88', 276, 1, 31, 410321) In this way both supplement each other’s work.
('88', 276, 1, 32, 410368) What I said above is at the back of the
('88', 277, 0, 1, 410408) 278 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 277, 1, 2, 410450) rule that the workers of Charkha Sangh should not take active part in politics.
('88', 277, 2, 3, 410530) POONA, November 3, 1945 [From Hindi]
('88', 277, 3, 4, 410567) Khadi Jagat, December, 1945

('88', 280, 8, 16, 414947) SUSHILA, I wonder whether you know it, but Kishorelal and Gomati behn are getting weaker and weaker.
('88', 280, 8, 17, 415048) The cold of Sevagram does not suit them.
('88', 280, 8, 18, 415089) They shrink from asking for anybody’s services.
('88', 280, 8, 19, 415137) Gomatibehn is actually ill.

('88', 280, 8, 22, 415256) We trust and hope that it will come down to normal.
('88', 280, 8, 23, 415308) But it will take some time for her to leave the sick bed, and it will be quite a while before she is able to look after herself.
('88', 280, 8, 24, 415437) She would not accept the services of anyone who may offer them, and if they can help it, neither of them would accept anybody’s services.
('88', 280, 8, 25, 415575) I would like it if someone were to stay with them now and look after them.

('88', 280, 8, 27, 415798) But wouldn’t my heart complain?
('88', 280, 8, 28, 415830) If, therefore, you can get away from there and go to Sevagram, and if your health permits you to look after them, I think it would be the best

('88', 285, 4, 10, 423195) 550. LETTER TO SIR EVAN M. JENKINS
('88', 285, 5, 11, 423230) NATURE CURE CLINIC, 6 TODIWALA ROAD, POONA, November 6, 1945
('88', 285, 6, 12, 423291) DEAR SIR EVAN, A copy of the petition sent to His Excellency on behalf of Shri Basuda Singh of Fyzabad District has been sent to me for seeking Government sympathy.
('88', 285, 6, 13, 423456) From the petition, I gather that it is a case of political hue, belonging to the 1942 disturbances period.
('88', 285, 6, 14, 423563) It easily falls under the principle that guided His Excellency’s decision in the Ashti Chimur 1 cases.
('88', 285, 6, 15, 423666) May I therefore ask for the usual commutation of the death sentence 2?
('88', 285, 6, 16, 423737) May I also ask for an early consideration of the case by reason of the fact that the period for execution has been fixed for 19th instant?
('88', 285, 7, 17, 423876) Yours sincerely, M. K. GANDHI
('88', 285, 8, 18, 423906) Gandhiji’s Correspondence with the Government, 1944 47, p.

('88', 288, 10, 27, 428050) 557. LETTER TO DINSHAW K. MEHTA
('88', 288, 11, 28, 428082) POONA, November 6, 1945
('88', 288, 12, 29, 428106) DINSHAW, I could not write to you yesterday but I kept mulling over things.
('88', 288, 12, 30, 428182) You can have anything you like under the Trust, but I would
('88', 288, 13, 31, 428242) 1 Vide “Letter to Mridula Sarabhai”, 7 1 1945
('88', 289, 0, 1, 428288) 290 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 289, 1, 2, 428330) say that we cannot start anything at Singhgadh right now.
('88', 289, 1, 3, 428388) It is another matter if I think of something to start there.
('88', 289, 1, 4, 428449) The Bombay centre will have to be closed down.
('88', 289, 1, 5, 428496) I would advise you to keep it for your own diversion and as a source of income.
('88', 289, 1, 6, 428576) I cannot afford to have it under the Trust.
('88', 289, 1, 7, 428620) I have still not received the figures about your personal expenses.
('88', 289, 1, 8, 428688) If you are provided board and lodging and Rs. 500/ per month from here, in my view, you should not think of making extra money from nature cure.
('88', 289, 1, 9, 428833) But here you must ask your own conscience.
('88', 289, 1, 10, 428876) If this is a bitter pill, then you must live in Bombay and carry on your practice.
('88', 289, 1, 11, 428959) If you put it in the Trust, it may be closed down soon after.
('88', 289, 1, 12, 429021) You do not have to worry at all about the expense here.
('88', 289, 1, 13, 429077) I shall manage.
('88', 289, 1, 14, 429093) I am anticipating that there will not be a single rich patient left here by the end of December.
('88', 289, 1, 15, 429190) The facilities here will solely be for those whom I send.
('88', 289, 1, 16, 429248) The person I send to manage things here will stay here.
('88', 289, 1, 17, 429304) Meat will be cooked in the kitchen for only Maji and any members of your family who may be visiting but not for any patient.
('88', 289, 1, 18, 429429) My dharma tells me that non vegetarian food, such as mutton, liver, etc., have no place in nature cure.
('88', 289, 1, 19, 429533) I do not suggest that those things have not benefited or cannot benefit anyone.
('88', 289, 1, 20, 429613) All I say is that in my view they cannot be included in nature cure.
('88', 289, 1, 21, 429682) The entire portion I am occupying at present will be reserved for you and Gulbai and it should not be necessary at any time to vacate it even for me.
('88', 289, 1, 22, 429832) Whenever I come, I can live anywhere on the upper floor.
('88', 289, 1, 23, 429889) It will not be difficult for me even to stay in the room which Saralabehn is at present occupying.
('88', 289, 1, 24, 429988) If it rains I can settle in the bathroom.
('88', 289, 1, 25, 430030) But it is not the least bit fair for me to occupy the portion especially built for Gulbai.
('88', 289, 1, 26, 430121) A ‘stock list’ should be prepared for the Trust.
('88', 289, 1, 27, 430170) Perhaps it cannot be done till Bhimnag comes, though of course I have with me so many people here that I can easily get the stock list and such other things prepared.
('88', 289, 1, 28, 430337) But your method of getting work done is altogether different.
('88', 289, 1, 29, 430399) I do not like it.
('88', 289, 1, 30, 430417) That way there are many things that I do not like, but I put up with them.
('88', 289, 1, 31, 430492) If you take up the responsibility, most of the things here can be settled while I am here.
('88', 289, 1, 32, 430583) I consider it wrong that you do not get patients to work.
('88', 289, 1, 33, 430641) Vanamala is capable of doing a lot of work.
('88', 289, 1, 34, 430685) All the patients would not be bed ridden.
('88', 289, 1, 35, 430727) From now on, only the poor must be admitted.
('88', 289, 1, 36, 430772) If there is any rich patient, he will be brought only by me and he will serve some purpose.
('88', 289, 1, 37, 430864) I may even take money from him and he will stay at my pleasure.
('88', 289, 1, 38, 430928) It irks me that you have not trained even Gulbai properly.
('88', 289, 1, 39, 430987) No one here seems to be
('88', 290, 0, 1, 431011) VOL.88 : 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 291
('88', 290, 1, 2, 431057) getting any training.
('88', 290, 1, 3, 431079) I do not even see the three year training being given here which you thought was necessary.
('88', 290, 1, 4, 431171) That is not correct.
('88', 290, 1, 5, 431192) But in this matter, I have got to be content with whatever you can easily provide.
('88', 290, 1, 6, 431275) If you think that thereby the whole thing would completely change and if it is not proper for me to interfere to such an extent, you can remove me.
('88', 290, 1, 7, 431423) If I were to involve myself in the matter, I would let things continue as they are.
('88', 290, 1, 8, 431507) I receive letters from people from all over.
('88', 290, 1, 9, 431552) They are willing to help in this or even join in.
('88', 290, 1, 10, 431602) Some of them I must admit are very good.
('88', 290, 1, 11, 431643) But till such time as I see you as a votary of nature cure and know who will be the right people to work with you, I would not like to admit any nature cure expert.
('88', 290, 1, 12, 431808) If I run this workshop I would like to pass on its benefits to the thousands of people outside.
('88', 290, 1, 13, 431904) For that, I would naturally need to have a large number of workers.
('88', 290, 1, 14, 431972) Only when that happens, can we at last have something like a university.
('88', 290, 1, 15, 432045) Give some thought to this.
('88', 290, 1, 16, 432072) I have not kept a copy of this letter.
('88', 290, 1, 17, 432111) Return it to me after reading.
('88', 290, 1, 18, 432142) I shall have it copied and then give it back to you.
('88', 290, 1, 19, 432195) I have written down my thoughts as they came while I was still in bed in the morning.
('88', 290, 2, 20, 432281) Blessings from BAPU

('88', 299, 10, 20, 445000) Your handwriting is particularly bad.
('88', 299, 10, 21, 445038) It is not worthy of you.
('88', 299, 10, 22, 445063) In my view each character of the alphabet is a drawing, and no drawing is made by scrawling.
('88', 299, 10, 23, 445156) Whether it is of a mere learner or that of a great painter the broad outline must look the same to the eye.
('88', 299, 10, 24, 445264) The drawings of a parrot made by a learner and an expert artist will look alike in their general form, but the quality of art in each will reveal who is the learner and who the expert.
('88', 299, 10, 25, 445449) Similarly, the shape of “ ” drawn by a
('88', 300, 0, 1, 445488) VOL.88 : 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 301
('88', 300, 1, 2, 445534) learner and that of one drawn by an expert artist must appear alike.
('88', 300, 1, 3, 445603) The difference would be seen only in the quality of art in each.
('88', 300, 1, 4, 445668) But in the drawings of your letters there is no resemblance at all.
('88', 300, 1, 5, 445736) I would blame your teacher more than you for this.
('88', 300, 1, 6, 445787) If you have understood what I have said above and still continue to draw shapeless lines instead of fine letters, I will blame you.
('88', 300, 1, 7, 445919) Your body must have now become as strong as an athlete’s.

('88', 307, 1, 2, 456391) 588. LETTER TO KUSUM
('88', 307, 2, 3, 456412) November 8, 1945
('88', 307, 3, 4, 456429) KUSUM, Kusum is written in quotes: that means it is not your real name.
('88', 307, 3, 5, 456501) Why are you so distressed over your widowhood?
('88', 307, 3, 6, 456548) A true widow does not believe that because the body of her husband has perished, the soul has also perished.
('88', 307, 3, 7, 456657) A woman is married not to a human frame but to the soul which resides in it.
('88', 307, 3, 8, 456734) That is precisely the reason why widow remarriage is taboo.
('88', 307, 3, 9, 456794) That is why your lamenting, thinking of committing suicide and so on are contrary to dharma and justice.
('88', 307, 3, 10, 456899) Your duty is to serve, giving the first place to spinning.
('88', 307, 3, 11, 456958) Learn the processes preceding and following spinning.
('88', 307, 3, 12, 457012) Also study the science of the charkha so that you can understand properly the significance of spinning.
('88', 307, 3, 13, 457116) You have not stated your age and your education.
('88', 307, 4, 14, 457165) Blessings from BAPU KUSUMBEHN C/O SHRI RAJENDRA KUMAR AGRAWAL PANNALAL ROAD ALLAHABAD

('88', 309, 1, 2, 459087) 592. LETTER TO MRIDULA SARABHAI
('88', 309, 2, 3, 459119) November 9, 1945
('88', 309, 3, 4, 459136) MRIDULA, I have your letter.
('88', 309, 3, 5, 459165) The correspondence has been published.
('88', 309, 3, 6, 459204) 1 It is rather interesting how this came about.
('88', 309, 3, 7, 459252) On the one hand Bapa writes to say that I was hasty in getting it published because I had agreed that we should publish it only after the meeting of the Managing Committee.
('88', 309, 3, 8, 459425) How nice it would have been if he had had me put it down in writing.
('88', 309, 3, 9, 459494) I myself have no such recollection.
('88', 309, 3, 10, 459530) Kanu says that he was present at the time and that I had told Bapa that if something had happened and if the matter was to be published, the sooner this was done the better.
('88', 309, 3, 11, 459704) Well, that is as it may be.
('88', 309, 3, 12, 459732) Your own recollection is that I was to give a short statement of my own in the end.
('88', 309, 3, 13, 459816) I remember having said something like that but I had not decided on it.
('88', 309, 3, 14, 459888) Having considered the whole thing I felt that since my letter 22 to you gave the entire background it was better published.
('88', 309, 3, 15, 460012) Now if this step was mistaken how can it be rectified?
('88', 309, 3, 16, 460067) I don’t see anything wrong in publishing the facts.
('88', 309, 3, 17, 460119) I have not seen what has come out in the newspapers.
('88', 309, 3, 18, 460172) If you are talking about the English translation, I had certainly approved it but I do not know if the same has appeared in the newspapers.
('88', 309, 3, 19, 460312) Anyway, for the present I am treating this chapter as closed.
('88', 309, 3, 20, 460374) It is good you are coming on the 12th.
('88', 309, 3, 21, 460413) This of course will be posted.
('88', 309, 4, 22, 460444) Blessings from BAPU
('88', 309, 5, 23, 460464) From a copy of the Gujarati: Pyarelal Papers.

('88', 310, 6, 28, 462144) That is a defect.

('88', 313, 8, 16, 465888) It contains things that Bhai Munshi refutes.
('88', 313, 8, 17, 465933) The report says that Pandit Jawaharlal had sent a nice message but that it was suppressed and was not read out.

('88', 313, 8, 19, 466126) If this is true and someone gave a false report, he should have signed it.
('88', 313, 8, 20, 466201) 2 Jawaharlal is there.
('88', 313, 8, 21, 466224) You could have had a talk with him.
('88', 313, 8, 22, 466260) I want that there should be at least one newspaper in India which has only truth from beginning to end, has no malice and is respected by one and all.
('88', 313, 8, 23, 466411) Why should not the Chronicle which has for its editor, Brelvi, the President of the Editor’s Conference be such a newspaper?

('88', 315, 6, 13, 468469) 604. LETTER TO MRIDULA SARABHAI
('88', 315, 7, 14, 468501) November 11, 1945
('88', 315, 8, 15, 468519) MRIDULA, I am replying to three of your letters together.
('88', 315, 8, 16, 468577) I liked your personal letter but one sentence in it pained me.
('88', 315, 8, 17, 468640) Why do you think I did not approve of what you call your “stand”?—you will yourself explain the meaning.
('88', 315, 8, 18, 468745) If I seem to be changing, it is only an impression.
('88', 315, 8, 19, 468797) Those who know me will not say this.
('88', 315, 8, 20, 468834) I consider you as one of them, but why should I discuss all this with you?
('88', 315, 8, 21, 468909) You are just a child to me while I am an old man.
('88', 315, 8, 22, 468959) You will leave me if and when you are fed up with me.
('88', 315, 8, 23, 469013) Come whenever you wish and have me clarify whatever you want clarified.

('88', 323, 11, 16, 479680) 621. FOREWORD TO “CONSTRUCTIVE PROGRAMME—ITS MEANING AND PLACE”
('88', 323, 12, 17, 479744) This is a thoroughly revised edition of the Constructive Programme which I first wrote in 1941. 1 The items included in it have not been arranged in any order, certainly not in the order of their importance.
('88', 323, 12, 18, 479952) When the reader discovers that a particular subject though important in itself in terms of independence does not find place in the programme, he should know that the omission is not intentional.
('88', 323, 12, 19, 480147) He should unhesitatingly add to my list and let me know.
('88', 323, 12, 20, 480204) My list does not pretend to be exhaustive; it is merely illustrative.
('88', 323, 12, 21, 480274) The reader will see several new and important additions.
('88', 323, 13, 22, 480331) 1 Vide “Constructive Programe” Its Meaning and Place”,13 12 1941
('88', 324, 0, 1, 480396) VOL.88 : 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 325
('88', 324, 1, 2, 480442) Readers, whether workers and volunteers or not, should definitely realize that the constructive programme is the truthful and non volent way of winning poorna swaraj.
('88', 324, 1, 3, 480609) Its wholesale fulfilment is complete independence.
('88', 324, 1, 4, 480660) Imagine all the forty crores of people busying themselves with the whole of the constructive programme which is designed to build up the nation from the very bottom upward.
('88', 324, 1, 5, 480833) Can anybody dispute the proposition that it must mean complete independence in every sense of the expression, including the ousting of foreign domination?
('88', 324, 1, 6, 480988) When the critics laugh at the proposition, what they mean is that forty crores of people will never co operate in the effort to fulfil the programme.
('88', 324, 1, 7, 481138) No doubt, there is considerable truth in the scoff.
('88', 324, 1, 8, 481190) My answer is, it is still worth the attempt.
('88', 324, 1, 9, 481235) Given an indomitable will on the part of a band of earnest workers, the programme is as workable as any other and more so than most.
('88', 324, 1, 10, 481368) Anyway, I have no substitute for it, if it is to be based on non violence.
('88', 324, 1, 11, 481443) Civil disobedience, mass or individual, is an aid to constructive effort and is a full substitute for armed revolt.
('88', 324, 1, 12, 481559) Training is necessary as well for civil disobedience as for armed revolt.
('88', 324, 1, 13, 481633) Only the ways are different.
('88', 324, 1, 14, 481662) Action in either case takes place only when occasion demands.
('88', 324, 1, 15, 481724) Training for military revolt means learning the use of arms ending perhaps in the atomic bomb.
('88', 324, 1, 16, 481819) For civil disobedience it means the constructive programme.
('88', 324, 1, 17, 481879) Therefore, workers will never be on the look out for civil resistance.
('88', 324, 1, 18, 481950) They will hold themselves in readiness, if the constructive effort is sought to be defeated.
('88', 324, 1, 19, 482043) From one or two illustrations it will be seen where it can be and where it cannot be offered.
('88', 324, 1, 20, 482137) Political pacts we know have been and can be, but personal friendship with individuals cannot be, prevented.
('88', 324, 1, 21, 482246) Such friendships, selfless and genuine, must be the basis for political pacts.
('88', 324, 1, 22, 482325) Similarly, centralized khadi can be defeated by the Government, but no power can defeat individual manufacture and use of khadi.
('88', 324, 1, 23, 482454) The manufacture and use of khadi must not be imposed upon the people, but it must be intelligently and willingly accepted by them as one of the items of the freedom movement.
('88', 324, 1, 24, 482629) This can be done only from the villages as units.
('88', 324, 1, 25, 482679) Pioneers even in such programmes can be obstructed.
('88', 324, 1, 26, 482731) They have had to go through the fire of suffering throughout the world.
('88', 324, 1, 27, 482803) There is no swaraj without suffering.
('88', 324, 1, 28, 482841) In violence, truth is the first and greatest sufferer; in non violence it is ever triumphant.
('88', 324, 1, 29, 482935) Moreover, men composing the Government are not to be regarded as enemies.
('88', 324, 1, 30, 483009) To regard them as such will be contrary to the non violent spirit.
('88', 324, 1, 31, 483076) Part we must, but as friends.
('88', 324, 1, 32, 483106) If this preliminary observation has gone home to the reader, he will find the constructive programme to be full of deep interest.
('88', 325, 0, 1, 483236) 326 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 325, 1, 2, 483278) should prove as absorbing as politics so called and platform oratory, and certainly more important and useful.
('88', 325, 1, 3, 483389) POONA, November 13, 1945 Constructive Programme: Its Meaning and Place
('88', 325, 2, 4, 483460) 622. LETTER TO SIR EVAN M. JENKINS
('88', 325, 3, 5, 483495) NATURE CURE CLINIC, 6 TODIWALA ROAD, POONA, November 13, 1945
('88', 325, 4, 6, 483557) DEAR SIR EVAN, I have just seen Reuter’s message from London about the threatened arrest of Pandit Jawaharlal Nehru.
('88', 325, 5, 7, 483674) I admit that Pandit Nehru’s speeches are hot, if the British rulers do not want to part with power and hand over to the people what is theirs.
('88', 325, 5, 8, 483817) They are not, if the British professions are real.
('88', 325, 5, 9, 483868) It will be wrong to attribute hatred or malice to him.
('88', 325, 5, 10, 483923) He undoubtedly speaks strongly against the I. C. S. men.
('88', 325, 5, 11, 483980) But there he speaks the people’s mind.
('88', 325, 5, 12, 484019) And he is right.
('88', 325, 5, 13, 484036) The fine doctrine propounded by His Excellency of “Forget and Forgive” can only apply to the excesses of a soldiery in action but surely not to inexusable butchery, inhumanity, bribery, corruption and the like.
('88', 325, 5, 14, 484247) If his statements are wrong, they should be tested through an open and impartial tribunal.
('88', 325, 5, 15, 484338) If the Government’s hands are clean they have nothing to fear from publicity.
('88', 325, 5, 16, 484416) I will not waste His Excellency’s time by arguing about the obvious.
('88', 325, 6, 17, 484485) Yours sincerely, M. K. GANDHI
('88', 325, 7, 18, 484515) Gandhiji’s Correspondence with the Government, 1944 47, p.
('88', 325, 8, 19, 484574) 1 According to a report Sir Maurice Hallett, Governor of U. P., had sought the Viceroy’s permission to arrest Jawaharlal Nehru.
('88', 325, 8, 20, 484702) The Viceroy declining, he had approached the Secretary of State.
('88', 325, 8, 21, 484767) The Viceroy’s House on April 12 issued a Press Note saying the report was a fabrication.
('88', 325, 8, 22, 484856) The Transfer of Power, Vol. VI, p.
('88', 325, 8, 23, 484891) 481. It is now known, however, that Wavell considered the speeches being made by Nehru, Patel, Pant and other Congress leaders as incitement to violence and was contemplating “before long ……another violent suppression of Congress”.
('88', 325, 8, 24, 485123) Wavell—The Viceroy’s Journal, passim.
('88', 325, 9, 25, 485161) 2 Writing to Secretary of State Wavell said considering Gandhiji’s “present state of health…… it is possible that the letter was written by Patel or Nehru and .merely signed by Gandhi” !
('88', 325, 9, 26, 485348) The Transfer of Power, Vol. VI, p.
('88', 325, 9, 27, 485383) 48. In his Journal, p.
('88', 325, 9, 28, 485406) 185, he describes the letter as malevolent.
('88', 326, 0, 1, 485450) VOL.88 : 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 327
('88', 326, 1, 2, 485496) 623. LETTER TO SHARDA G. CHOKHAWALA
('88', 326, 3, 3, 485532) November 13, 1945
('88', 326, 4, 4, 485550) BABU, I have your letter.
('88', 326, 4, 5, 485576) You have not said what your “one last” 1
('88', 326, 5, 6, 485617) attempt was.
('88', 326, 5, 7, 485630) See that it does not become too late for improvement.

('88', 332, 1, 2, 495276) 631. LETTER TO DINSHAW K. MEHTA
('88', 332, 2, 3, 495308) POONA, November 14, 1945
('88', 332, 3, 4, 495333) DINSHAW,
('88', 332, 4, 5, 495342) My cogitations go on.
('88', 332, 4, 6, 495364) The institution should close down on December 31. From January 1, it should become an institution for the poor and cease to be one for the rich.
('88', 332, 4, 7, 495509) You have so far insisted that the poor should be taken only after the rich have been accommodated but those who are really poor can hardly reach you and if anyone reaches you, they will have to pay the rates the rich pay, which will completely ruin them.
('88', 332, 4, 8, 495764) From the 1st January let the rich come after the poor are accommodated but only if they can live as the poor.
('88', 332, 4, 9, 495874) The institution should have more cleanliness than it has today.
('88', 332, 4, 10, 495938) Money is not necessary for maintaining cleanliness, but it requires care, love, truth and knowledge.
('88', 332, 4, 11, 496039) So it is better that cleaning work is started from today, but I am afraid it is not possible because no one listens to the others and everyone is his own master.
('88', 332, 4, 12, 496201) If anyone takes interest in work, it is only to please you.
('88', 332, 4, 13, 496261) Therefore there can be improvement only if someone from among the people I mentioned above starts working from today.
('88', 332, 4, 14, 496379) If this thing does not appeal to you, both of us will have to repent ultimately because I believe that cleanliness is a part of God.
('88', 332, 4, 15, 496512) I would amend the saying “cleanliness is next to godliness” and say “cleanliness is godliness”.
('88', 332, 4, 16, 496608) But only if cleanliness is both internal and external can we call it an attribute of God.
('88', 332, 4, 17, 496698) A sign board should be hung here from January 1. It should be written in Marathi, Devanagari, Urdu and English.
('88', 332, 4, 18, 496810) I have not in my mind formed a precise idea but it would be somewhat as follows.
('88', 332, 4, 19, 496891) “The poor are given nature cure treatment here”.The name Healthotorium should be removed.
('88', 332, 4, 20, 496981) There is no need for any name.
('88', 332, 4, 21, 497012) It does not befit a poor institution.
('88', 332, 4, 22, 497050) In fact it does not befit any.
('88', 332, 4, 23, 497081) The English would consider it “vulgar”.
('88', 332, 4, 24, 497121) We should not use foreign things whether they are patent or not.
('88', 332, 4, 25, 497186) The poor cannot afford a bottle of Isapgol pakced in England, Robinson Barley, Quaker Oats, Sanatogen, Horlicks, malted milk or Merck’s Glucose.
('88', 332, 4, 26, 497331) We, from here, cannot teach the people to take these things—it is immaterial who is here—whether Sardar, some Raja or I.
('88', 333, 0, 1, 497452) 334 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 333, 1, 2, 497494) We must make Sanatogen here.
('88', 333, 1, 3, 497523) Things similar to Horlicks and malted milk should be made here and also something like glucose should be available.
('88', 333, 1, 4, 497639) The kitchen can no longer function on the lines it has been doing so far.
('88', 333, 1, 5, 497713) Today you have the means to feed even a king.
('88', 333, 1, 6, 497759) But those means must be given up tomorrow.
('88', 333, 1, 7, 497802) The liberality with which fruit and other things are used here hurts me much.
('88', 333, 1, 8, 497880) It ought to be changed.
('88', 333, 1, 9, 497904) Can’t we manage with jaggery and lemon?
('88', 333, 1, 10, 497944) You must develop the habit of writing.

('88', 333, 1, 19, 498524) Therefore I am helpless.

('88', 335, 10, 15, 501458) 635. LETTER TO MANGALDAS PAKVASA
('88', 335, 11, 16, 501491) November 15, 1945
('88', 335, 12, 17, 501509) BHAI MANGALDAS, I have your letter.
('88', 335, 12, 18, 501545) I see you are working at great speed.
('88', 335, 12, 19, 501583) I on my part am doing what I can from here.
('88', 335, 12, 20, 501627) I have gone through Motilal’s and your opinion.
('88', 335, 12, 21, 501675) I agree with it.
('88', 335, 12, 22, 501692) But there is one thing neither of you appear to have considered.
('88', 335, 12, 23, 501757) The words are: “one should not refuse to sell [khadi] which is worth buying”.
('88', 335, 12, 24, 501835) Now the question is which khadi should be considered “worth buying”.
('88', 335, 12, 25, 501904) One might say that the khadi which had been produced according to the conditions laid down by me was “worth buying”.

('88', 335, 12, 32, 502492) But if there is something wrong in my way of thinking, I should not proceed with it for the moment.
