('88', 342, 1, 2, 512333) 643. LETTER TO ATULANAND CHAKRAVARTY
('88', 342, 2, 3, 512370) POONA, November 16, 1945
('88', 342, 3, 4, 512395) BHAI ATULANAND,
('88', 342, 4, 5, 512411) I have your postcard.
('88', 342, 4, 6, 512433) I have sent the thing on to a historian who has also made a serious study of the Hindu Muslim question.
('88', 342, 4, 7, 512537) I am awaiting his reply.
('88', 342, 4, 8, 512562) A leading Congressman told me that it would not do any good to write anything like this in the name of the Congress because the atmosphere was such that people had shut their ears to objectively expressed views of others and such being the case anything said was bound to be misunderstood.
('88', 342, 4, 9, 512852) Therefore, I am not keen to have this published.
('88', 342, 4, 10, 512901) Seeing the atmosphere that prevails I myself hold a similar view.
('88', 342, 4, 11, 512967) But lest I do injustice to your endeavour I have sent it to a historian for his opinion.
('88', 342, 4, 12, 513056) This much I can say that it will not be possible to have it published as quickly as you want.
('88', 342, 4, 13, 513150) Let us see what comes of it and what I finally decide.
('88', 342, 4, 14, 513205) My visit to Bengal will not be long in coming now.
('88', 342, 4, 15, 513256) I hope to reach there on December 1st.
('88', 342, 4, 16, 513295) Do meet me there.
('88', 342, 4, 17, 513313) Let me, however, tell you that the final decision lies not with those with an English education but with the millions of people who know their mother tongue or the national language.
('88', 342, 4, 18, 513496) Therefore, write the original in your mother tongue, Bengali; and for other provinces in the national language in both the scripts.
('88', 342, 4, 19, 513628) If you agree with what I say, start reading and writing the national language in both the scripts.
('88', 342, 4, 20, 513727) Would Rabi Babu’s writings and poetry have had any impact on Bengali if he had written in English?

('88', 348, 1, 2, 520771) 654. LETTER TO JIVANJI D. DESAI
('88', 348, 2, 3, 520803) POONA, November 18, 1945
('88', 348, 3, 4, 520828) JIVANJI, Please read the enclosed letter and return it to me with your opinion on what should be done.
('88', 348, 3, 5, 520931) They have sent the money as royalty on the sales of the translation, but since we are not entitled to it I feel tempted to utilize it for the many other activities under my charge instead of crediting it to the Navajivan account.
('88', 348, 3, 6, 521161) But then I also feel that I had better send it to you.
('88', 348, 3, 7, 521216) I am, therefore, sending the cheque herewith.
('88', 348, 3, 8, 521262) If, now, you yourself feel that the money should not be credited to the Navajivan account, then, and only then, return it to me.
('88', 348, 3, 9, 521391) At present I am spending money as it comes from different accounts.
('88', 348, 3, 10, 521459) I do not see any of these to be specially in need of this money.
('88', 348, 3, 11, 521524) Hence both of us can consider the matter objectively.
('88', 348, 3, 12, 521578) I sent you yesterday the pamphlet on constructive programme after revising it with great labour.
('88', 348, 3, 13, 521675) Inadvertently, it was posted as unregistered packet.
('88', 348, 3, 14, 521728) I shall, therefore, feel worried till I get an acknowledgment from you.
('88', 348, 3, 15, 521800) For I have kept no copy of it.
('88', 348, 3, 16, 521831) But I derive what comfort I can from the story of Newton who, after being slightly upset when the manuscript on which he had been working for many years was destroyed in a fire by somebody, proceeded to write it all over again.
('88', 348, 3, 17, 522059) And with this thought I keep patience.
('88', 348, 3, 18, 522098) I hope it will not be lost on the way.
('88', 348, 3, 19, 522137) But if it is, I will revise another copy.
('88', 348, 3, 20, 522179) It will mean loss of some time, of course.
('88', 348, 3, 21, 522222) If, therefore, you receive it safely, spend money on a wire, but if you don’t get it send another copy with your suggestions so that I may start work on it immediately.
('88', 348, 3, 22, 522391) Enclosures: 1 cheque and 1 letter
('88', 348, 4, 23, 522425) From a photostat of the Gujarati: G.N. 9958. Also C.W. 6932. Courtesy: Jivanji D. Desai

('88', 351, 1, 2, 525653) 658. LETTER TO G. D. BIRLA
('88', 351, 2, 3, 525680) POONA, November, 18, 1945
('88', 351, 3, 4, 525706) GHANSHYAMDAS, I have no doubt that you have done everything possible with regard to the land at Nasik.
('88', 351, 3, 5, 525809) Dinshaw is an eccentric man but he is very good, generous and simple hearted.
('88', 351, 3, 6, 525887) In the matter of nature cure he is the only man on whom my eyes are fixed.
('88', 351, 3, 7, 525962) I shall go on encouraging him in his virtues and, if I can do so, it will be of much help to the patients.
('88', 351, 3, 8, 526069) Therefore, when I saw that he was himself not keen on going to Nasik, I dropped the matter.
('88', 351, 3, 9, 526161) With that I also decided to begin the new term of the institution from here and run it for the poor.
('88', 351, 3, 10, 526262) So far only the rich have come and the poor have remained behind.
('88', 351, 3, 11, 526328) But now the rich who wish to be admitted here will have to come after the poor.
('88', 351, 3, 12, 526408) The rich will get the same facilities as the poor.
('88', 351, 3, 13, 526459) At the same time it is certain that an attempt will be made to observe the rules of cleanliness as meticulously as possible.
('88', 351, 3, 14, 526584) No doubt it is a difficult task.
('88', 351, 3, 15, 526617) I should not cultivate such an interest in my declining years.
('88', 351, 3, 16, 526680) But what lay dormant for years has awakened without any effort on my part.
('88', 351, 3, 17, 526755) How can I resist it?
('88', 351, 3, 18, 526776) God’s will alone will prevail.
('88', 351, 3, 19, 526807) For the time being the insti tution of which you too are a trustee has been closed.
('88', 351, 3, 20, 526891) If it is to come into existence out of the activities here, it will.
('88', 351, 3, 21, 526960) Whatever happens will be proper from all points of view.
('88', 351, 3, 22, 527017) I shall write to you if I have to go to Nasik or need money to carry on this institution.
('88', 351, 3, 23, 527107) At present I am just watching.
('88', 351, 3, 24, 527138) There is some money lying with me.
('88', 351, 3, 25, 527173) I shall manage with it.
('88', 351, 3, 26, 527197) Since it is the condition of this trust that the management will not be left in Dinshaw’s hands, you may as well say that the responsibility will mine.
('88', 351, 3, 27, 527349) I have read Shivnath Singh’s letter you sent me.
('88', 351, 3, 28, 527398) It did not make a favourable impression on me.
('88', 351, 3, 29, 527445) He has written at great length 1. I am writing a brief note to him.

('88', 356, 4, 8, 532800) 668. DISCUSSION WITH HINDUSTANI PRACHAR SABHA WORKERS
('88', 356, 5, 9, 532854) BOMBAY, [Novemeber 19, 1945] 1
('88', 356, 6, 10, 532885) To a questions why the Urdu script should be imposed on a person who did not like it and wished to learn the national language only through the Devanagari script, Mahatma Gandhi replied: It is not a question of liking or disliking.
('88', 356, 6, 11, 533117) If you do not like the Urdu script, then I conclude that you do not like Hindustani.
('88', 356, 6, 12, 533202) The Urdu script must be learnt.
('88', 356, 6, 13, 533234) Without effort and sacrifice we cannot dream of winning freedom.
('88', 356, 6, 14, 533299) So far as the provinces of Bombay, Gujarat and Maharashtra are concerned, the question of learning the Nagari script does not arise at all as everybody knows it already.
('88', 356, 6, 15, 533469) Then, where does Hindustani Prachar come in?
('88', 356, 6, 16, 533514) In learning the other script, do not think you are conferring a favour on anyone.
('88', 356, 6, 17, 533596) It should be considered as your duty.
('88', 356, 6, 18, 533634) It is a national work and everyone should do it.
('88', 356, 6, 19, 533683) By learning both the scripts you can better understand both the Hindi and the Urdu developments of the language.
('88', 356, 6, 20, 533796) I can understand Sanskritized Hindi, but what about the masses?
('88', 356, 6, 21, 533860) It is our duty to learn both the scripts.
('88', 356, 6, 22, 533902) Then alone can we hoenstly serve the country in a humble way.
('88', 356, 6, 23, 533964) According to me one who does not have a liking for the Urdu script has no liking for swaraj also.
('88', 356, 6, 24, 534062) The masses do not understand pure Hindi or pure Urdu, so Hindustani should be evolved in such a way that even the illiterate masses can understand it.
('88', 356, 6, 25, 534213) Mere slogans would not help in achieving the goal of freedom.
('88', 356, 6, 26, 534275) Taking as little trouble as possible and looking to your worldly advancement will leave your swaraj just a dream.
('88', 356, 6, 27, 534389) Nagari and Urdu are

('88', 357, 1, 4, 534595) Our swaraj cannot be given to us as a gift, but we shall have to win it through our untiring efforts.

('88', 358, 5, 14, 537497) 670. STATEMENT TO THE PRESS
('88', 358, 6, 15, 537525) WARDHA, November 21, 1945 I had purposely refrained from correcting or contradicting reports about my shifting to Poona and establishing a nature cure hospital on an extensive plot of ground in Poona or even Nasik.
('88', 358, 6, 16, 537740) All this was wrong, as most unauthentic reports in the Press are.
('88', 358, 6, 17, 537806) These have always cost me dear, perhaps the public more than me.
('88', 358, 6, 18, 537871) There was, however, a grain of truth in the ounce of rumour.
('88', 358, 6, 19, 537932) Dr. Dinshaw Mehta knew me before I knew him and, ever since I have known him, I have liked him.
('88', 358, 6, 20, 538028) I have been myself a nature cure man before all known to me.
('88', 358, 6, 21, 538089) Of them, Dr. Dinshaw has made the greatest impression on me and he is a dreamer like me.
('88', 358, 6, 22, 538178) He wants a nature cure university; so do I. He has made over to a Trust his concerns at Poona and Sinhgad.
('88', 358, 6, 23, 538285) Their nominal cost, according to the schedules to the Trust, is, in round figures, Rs. 50,000. I have allowed myself to be one of the Trustees.
('88', 358, 6, 24, 538429) The other two are Dr. Mehta himself and Mr. Jehangir Patel who is interested in nature cure.
('88', 358, 6, 25, 538522) Hitherto Dr. Mehta’s institution has been meant for monied men and then for as many poor people as he could safely take.
('88', 358, 6, 26, 538643) Patients have all been residential.
('88', 358, 6, 27, 538679) From the 1st of January next, this institution will be devoted to
('88', 359, 0, 1, 538745) 360 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 359, 1, 2, 538787) the service of the poor.
('88', 359, 1, 3, 538812) The rich will be taken only if they can accommodate themselves to remain with the poor, and expect no more space or comforts than the poor will get at this institution.
('88', 359, 1, 4, 538981) The guarantee will be that the standard of cleanliness, shorn of luxury, will be the highest attainable in any institution of the kind.
('88', 359, 1, 5, 539117) Treatment will be both indoor and outdoor.
('88', 359, 1, 6, 539160) Outdoor will naturally be more than indoor.
('88', 359, 1, 7, 539204) The Birlas have interested themselves in me for years.
('88', 359, 1, 8, 539259) And they were prepared to give me in Nasik as much land with buildings as were required for the institution.
('88', 359, 1, 9, 539368) But Dr. Dinshaw was not whole heartedly inclined to favour the Nasik idea, unless I consented to include in the Trust the going concerns at Poona too.
('88', 359, 1, 10, 539519) I could not shoulder the burden.
('88', 359, 1, 11, 539552) Hence the Nasik project had to be dropped, for the time being at any rate.
('88', 359, 1, 12, 539627) 1 Dr. Dinshaw will still remain the sole Director so far as the technical part is concerned.
('88', 359, 1, 13, 539720) This institution, if it is to grow at all, will require the silent blessings of the poor, the financial support of the rich, active co operation of genuine naturopaths of India and sympathy of the medical fraternity.
('88', 359, 1, 14, 539937) Its present site is too small for the requirements of the poor.
('88', 359, 1, 15, 540001) Moreover, it will largely depend upon the leaseholder whether the institution can in any case remain located on the present site.

('88', 361, 1, 7, 542610) I have given the same advice to Kumarappa, nemely, that he should deposit the Village Industries Association’s funds in that Bank.

('88', 361, 1, 32, 544310) He suggested, therefore, that it would be wise to withdraw the money in time.

('88', 363, 1, 2, 547150) 675. TALK TO STUDENTS OF SAMAGRA GRAMSEVA VIDYALAYA 1
('88', 363, 2, 3, 547204) SEVAGRAM, November 22, 1945
('88', 363, 3, 4, 547232) I expect much from the students who have come here for study.
('88', 363, 3, 5, 547294) Not only I but also those who take interest in this work, expect much from you.
('88', 363, 3, 6, 547374) There are many educated people in India who criticize and run down our programme.
('88', 363, 3, 7, 547456) Some of them oppose it on principle.
('88', 363, 3, 8, 547493) At present I do not want to say anything about them, though I have a ready answer for them.
('88', 363, 3, 9, 547585) But we should listen to those who have some interest in this work and wish to take some part in it.
('88', 363, 3, 10, 547685) Such people hope for much from khadi work, village industries, goseva and work of Harijan uplift.
('88', 363, 3, 11, 547783) We should therefore make strenuous efforts to fulfil their expectations.
('88', 363, 3, 12, 547856) If you have come here in order merely to earn your livelihood, then that hope will not be realized.
('88', 363, 3, 13, 547956) Many people study in Government colleges.
('88', 363, 3, 14, 547998) They get degrees there.
('88', 363, 3, 15, 548022) They think that with that education they will earn money and fame and at least become clerks in some Government office, or if not, they can certainly get jobs as peons.
('88', 363, 3, 16, 548191) And they become peons not for the sake of work, but in the hope of getting promotions in future and making some money on the side.
('88', 363, 3, 17, 548322) This means that they believe that once they enter Government service, their life is secure.
('88', 363, 3, 18, 548414) This is a matter which needs careful thinking.
('88', 363, 3, 19, 548461) The Government has provided several facilities in their colleges.
('88', 363, 3, 20, 548527) They have provided spacious buildings, offered large scholarships and given travelling facilities.
('88', 363, 3, 21, 548626) How can we compete with all this?
('88', 363, 3, 22, 548660) I have already shown several ways of solving this problem.
('88', 363, 3, 23, 548719) You have not come here for comforts or for the sake of salary.
('88', 363, 3, 24, 548782) If you want to succeed in your aim bear in mind that you have not come here merely to learn crafts.
('88', 363, 3, 25, 548882) Of course you have to learn crafts but you should not rest content with that.
('88', 363, 3, 26, 548960) Artisans are already there in villages.
('88', 363, 3, 27, 549000) They have been doing the same work from generation to generation.
('88', 363, 3, 28, 549066) How can you compete with them?
('88', 363, 3, 29, 549097) Do learn the process, but along with that you must acquire scientific knowledge.
('88', 363, 3, 30, 549178) We should think again and again why we are doing this work, how we should proceed about it, how we can link it with swaraj.
('88', 363, 3, 31, 549302) Swaraj has to be attained through non violence.
('88', 363, 3, 32, 549350) There are crores of people living in the villages of
('88', 363, 4, 33, 549403) 1 The institution started functioning from October 2, 1945.
('88', 364, 0, 1, 549463) VOL.88 : 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 365
('88', 364, 1, 2, 549509) We have to emancipate them, serve them and make them understand the value of this work.
('88', 364, 1, 3, 549597) If you believe that the mill owners can feed the people and if you are satisfied with it then you should not study here.
('88', 364, 1, 4, 549718) But the mill owners can provide for only a handful.
('88', 364, 1, 5, 549770) Mill owners never think at all of the crores of people.
('88', 364, 1, 6, 549826) I have not come across any mill owner so far who has told me that mills can provide work for the millions.
('88', 364, 1, 7, 549933) You have come here to accomplish a Herculean task.

('88', 364, 1, 19, 550654) Its way is straight.

('88', 370, 2, 3, 559904) SEVAGRAM, November 25, 1945
('88', 370, 3, 4, 559932) DEAR SIR EVAN, I write this in continuation of my letter 1 of 10th October.
('88', 370, 3, 5, 560008) Since then I have seen other such accounts in the papers and now I have with me a young man (Shri Prabhu Dayal Vidyarthi) who came to me while he was yet in his teens, without being recommended by anybody, as a poor youngster.
('88', 370, 3, 6, 560235) This was in the year 1935. Ever since then he has never been out of my observation.
('88', 370, 3, 7, 560319) He was arrested in connection with the 1942 disturbances, and has lately been discharged.
('88', 370, 3, 8, 560409) He came to Wardha in a dilapidated condition.
('88', 370, 3, 9, 560455) I was then at Poona.
('88', 370, 3, 10, 560476) He reported his arrival and I telegraphed to him to come there so that I could look after him better and, if necessary, get Dr. Mehta’s assistance at his sanatorium where I was staying.
('88', 370, 3, 11, 560662) He narrates tales of terrible torture, into the details of which I do not wish to go at this stage.
('88', 370, 4, 12, 560762) On top of this I have received a communication from Dr. Lohia’s friends and they tell me that Dr. Lohia has gone through torture himself.
('88', 370, 4, 13, 560900) He is an able, cultured man who sacrificed a position of ease and luxury for the sake of the cause of India’s independence.
('88', 370, 4, 14, 561024) I know him well and, through him, also his father.
('88', 370, 4, 15, 561075) It is difficult to disbelieve all the accounts that have appeared in the Press and the two incidents mentioned above.
('88', 370, 4, 16, 561193) I suggest that His Excellency goes deeper into the matter and not reject the statements as an exag geration undeserving of any attention.
('88', 370, 4, 17, 561331) I take comfort from the fact that in your letter of 1st November in reply to mine of 10th October, you tell 3 me that though His Excellency believes the story to be exaggerated, he is making further investigations.
('88', 370, 4, 18, 561546) I plead for investigation into all other such statements and, if he proposes to do so, I am prepared to send you such details as I possess about the two

('88', 378, 1, 2, 572122) 699. LETTER TO INAYATULLA KHAN
('88', 378, 2, 3, 572153) SEVAGRAM, November 27, 1945
('88', 378, 3, 4, 572181) ALLAMA SAHEB 1, I have your letter of the 21st instant.
('88', 378, 3, 5, 572237) I am sorry and surprised that you have again misinterpreted my letter.
('88', 378, 3, 6, 572308) I had not suggested that because the correspondence between us was still going on you should not have your letter published.
('88', 378, 3, 7, 572433) I had only expressed my view that this correspondence should not be released to the press.
('88', 378, 3, 8, 572524) However, if you think it proper, you may have it published.
('88', 378, 3, 9, 572584) You are right in saying that Dastagir 2 can come here if he so desires.
('88', 378, 3, 10, 572656) I had not said I would comment on each separate clause of the constitution you have drafted.
('88', 378, 3, 11, 572749) I had only said that if broad questions are prepared in regard to it, I could try to reply to them.
('88', 378, 3, 12, 572849) But from your letter I have begun to fear that you may misunderstand anything I may say.
('88', 378, 3, 13, 572938) Be that as it may, if you formulate a few questions for me, I shall give you written replies to them.
('88', 378, 3, 14, 573040) It is unnecessary for Dastagir to come just to collect my replies.
('88', 378, 3, 15, 573107) Besides there is not even enough time for that.
('88', 378, 3, 16, 573155) But whatever you send at this address will reach me wherever I may be.
('88', 378, 3, 17, 573226) I have got one more complaint, namely, why do you write to me in English?
('88', 378, 4, 18, 573300) Yours sincerely, M. K. GANDHI

('88', 379, 0, 1, 573531) 380 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 379, 1, 2, 573573) 700. WHY THE INSISTENCE ON THE YARN CLAUSE 1
('88', 379, 2, 3, 573618) November 27/28, 1945 This is an old argument.
('88', 379, 2, 4, 573664) 2 One wants to do many good things but is too lazy.
('88', 379, 2, 5, 573716) However, when a rule is made the work becomes easy.
('88', 379, 2, 6, 573768) Then one finds that one has gained the strength to do the work one could not do before.
('88', 379, 2, 7, 573856) By making the yarn clause compulsory, we do not coerce people.
('88', 379, 2, 8, 573919) We only make it easy for those who want to spin.
('88', 379, 2, 9, 573968) How long can they spin who have no heart in it?
('88', 379, 2, 10, 574016) It will be hypocritical if they spin as a demonstration.
('88', 379, 2, 11, 574073) Hyprocrites only do harm to themselves.
('88', 379, 2, 12, 574113) They cannot harm khadi in any way.
('88', 379, 2, 13, 574148) I would in fact go so far as to say that he who takes up spinning out of a desire for praise will gradually develop an interest in the activity and then continue to spin willingly.
('88', 379, 2, 14, 574329) If even after long practice he cannot find interest in spinning, if he still finds it a tedium he will give up khadi.
('88', 379, 2, 15, 574447) That will not harm us in any way.
('88', 379, 2, 16, 574481) If the khadi bhandars close down because of the yarn clause they well may.
('88', 379, 2, 17, 574556) And I do not care whether anyone buys khadi or not.
('88', 379, 2, 18, 574608) I do not wish to run a shop.
('88', 379, 2, 19, 574637) I want people to learn spinning.
('88', 379, 2, 20, 574670) In Bombay 300 or 350 charkhas are plied.
('88', 379, 2, 21, 574711) But this number means nothing.
('88', 379, 2, 22, 574742) What I want is that there should be as many charkhas plying there as there are homes.
('88', 379, 2, 23, 574828) If the cities are to imbibe non violence there is no other way.
('88', 379, 2, 24, 574892) The Government have the force that destroys; I have the charkha.
('88', 379, 2, 25, 574957) The charkha alone can save us from destructive force.
('88', 379, 2, 26, 575011) All other methods are useless.
('88', 379, 2, 27, 575042) If the enforcement of the yarn clause results in reduced sales of khadi and if the consequent loss forces us to close down the khadi bhandars, we may close them down.
('88', 379, 2, 28, 575209) We cannot maintain khadi bhandars to sell khadi.
('88', 379, 2, 29, 575258) You will say that if khadi bhandars in the city close down we shall have to sell khadi in the villages and that khadi cannot sell in the villages as it can in the cities.
('88', 379, 2, 30, 575429) I agree that khadi cannot sell in the villages and it should not.
('88', 379, 2, 31, 575495) Khadi is not to be sold in the villages, it is to be worn there.
('88', 379, 2, 32, 575560) It is to be spun and worn.
('88', 379, 2, 33, 575587) Rather than that we should have to get licences from the Government for khadi bhandars it is better that khadi dies, it is better that the khadi
('88', 379, 3, 34, 575732) 1 According to the source this is a summary of what Gandhiji had said at discussions with the Charkha Sangh workers on November 27 and 28.
('88', 379, 4, 35, 575871) 2 It had been suggested that those who could not tender yarn for the purchase of khadi should be allowed to buy it for cash, and that making the tendering of yarn compulsory would amount to coercion.
('88', 380, 0, 1, 576071) VOL.88 : 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 381
('88', 380, 1, 2, 576117) shops close down.
('88', 380, 1, 3, 576135) Khadi cannot survive if it has to depend on others for its survival.
('88', 380, 1, 4, 576204) Then it will be its lot to disappear.
('88', 380, 1, 5, 576242) Once you understand the idea behind khadi you will not be nervous.
('88', 380, 1, 6, 576309) You will not wonder how khadi bhandars and khadi centres will carry on.
('88', 380, 1, 7, 576381) Since we have taken that step, since we have dared, we must be prepared to face difficulties.
('88', 380, 1, 8, 576475) If we have to suffer set backs we must be prepared for it.
('88', 380, 1, 9, 576534) You ask about woollens and silks.
('88', 380, 1, 10, 576568) Who wears them?
('88', 380, 1, 11, 576584) Can the poor do so?
('88', 380, 1, 12, 576604) Why should we take all the trouble for a few rich people?
('88', 380, 1, 13, 576662) These things cannot become universal.
('88', 380, 1, 14, 576700) We may certainly keep stocks of woollens and silks in khadi bhandars as we keep other things there but we must understand that that is no part of our work.
('88', 380, 1, 15, 576856) We may not apply the yarn clause to woollens and silks.
('88', 380, 1, 16, 576912) We may not ask for yarn when selling these.
('88', 380, 1, 17, 576956) Do we ask for yarn when selling other village handicrafts?
('88', 380, 1, 18, 577015) Woollens and silks come in that category.
('88', 380, 1, 19, 577057) If we remain steadfast, the importance of khadi will not diminish.
('88', 380, 1, 20, 577124) If we think of meeting the expenditure of khadi bhandars out of the proceeds from the sale of woollens and silks, it will not help khadi, it will only harm it.
('88', 380, 1, 21, 577284) If we carry on the khadi activity with the help of woollens and silks we shall become crippled.
('88', 380, 1, 22, 577380) We shall not be able to carry on with the khadi work.
('88', 380, 1, 23, 577434) Khadi work can sustain itself.
('88', 380, 1, 24, 577465) It does not require dependence on anyone.
('88', 380, 1, 25, 577507) No one can kill khadi.
('88', 380, 1, 26, 577530) How can mills do so?
('88', 380, 1, 27, 577551) Mills may themselves be destroyed.
('88', 380, 1, 28, 577586) We do not worry on that account.
('88', 380, 1, 29, 577619) All the activities concerned with khadi, right from the picking of cotton to the weaving of khadi, should be carried on by the khadi bhandars.
('88', 380, 1, 30, 577762) Selling of khadi is only a minor activity.
('88', 380, 1, 31, 577805) Kakubhai is the secretary of the Bombay khadi bhandar.
('88', 380, 1, 32, 577860) I want to see how skilled he is.
('88', 380, 1, 33, 577893) I want to see in his hand not a pen but a charkha.
('88', 380, 1, 34, 577944) He should be an expert in all the processes employed in khadi.
('88', 380, 1, 35, 578007) If I were in a bhandar I would spin, I would card.
('88', 380, 1, 36, 578058) We have to teach people spinning and weaving through the bhandars.
('88', 380, 1, 37, 578125) Today we do try to teach people how to ply the charkha.
('88', 380, 1, 38, 578181) But if khadi is to reach every home we must teach people ginning, carding and all the other processes.
('88', 380, 1, 39, 578284) I do not much care for buying slivers.
('88', 380, 1, 40, 578323) One should make slivers oneself.
('88', 380, 1, 41, 578356) Today machine made slivers are used.
('88', 380, 1, 42, 578393) The practice must stop.
('88', 380, 1, 43, 578417) Everyone should card his own cotton, make his own slivers and then spin.
('88', 380, 1, 44, 578490) Only then can we say that we have adopted khadi.
('88', 380, 1, 45, 578539) I have become a lover of hand carding.
('88', 380, 1, 46, 578578) Even inferior cotton such as mathia, hand carded, can yield yarn of the fineness of 20 counts.
('88', 380, 1, 47, 578673) The mills cannot produce yarn of a count higher than six or seven from this cotton.
('88', 380, 1, 48, 578757) I prefer hand carding to carding with a bow.
('88', 380, 1, 49, 578802) It does not expose one to the risk either of consumption or asthma.
('88', 380, 1, 50, 578870) Even a queen in her palace can easily take
('88', 381, 0, 1, 578913) 382 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 381, 1, 2, 578955) this up.
('88', 381, 1, 3, 578964) Even children and old men can card and make slivers.
('88', 381, 1, 4, 579017) It is a simple and easy activity.
('88', 381, 1, 5, 579051) Today we must not think of spreading khadi by carrying it about on our backs and hawking it.
('88', 381, 1, 6, 579144) We have not to give anyone ready made khadi.
('88', 381, 1, 7, 579189) We shall say, ‘take this charkha, take this cotton, card it, make slivers and spin.
('88', 381, 1, 8, 579273) Get the weaver in your village to weave it and then wear it.’ I would in fact say that the khadi bhandars not only should not have khadi, they should not even have slivers and cotton.
('88', 381, 1, 9, 579457) If people demand them we may give them cotton and the necessary tools and arrange for spinning to be taught.
('88', 381, 1, 10, 579566) You will then see that the country will have no dearth of khadi or cloth as such.
('88', 381, 1, 11, 579648) Cloth is frequently rationed and still cloth famine persists.
('88', 381, 1, 12, 579710) I can remove it.
('88', 381, 1, 13, 579727) If I was made responsible for it, I could provide cloth to everyone.
('88', 381, 1, 14, 579796) I am going to Bengal.
('88', 381, 1, 15, 579818) If they do as I desire, I shall see that there will be no cloth famine there.
('88', 381, 1, 16, 579896) You ask if you should provide khadi for hospitals.
('88', 381, 1, 17, 579947) For where will the patients find yarn, how will they be able to spin?
('88', 381, 1, 18, 580017) Similarly there are the Congress committees, the district boards, the banks.
('88', 381, 1, 19, 580094) Then there are exhibitions, Congress meetings and so on, which require khadi worth thousands of rupees.
('88', 381, 1, 20, 580198) Where can they all find the yarn?
('88', 381, 1, 21, 580232) Would it not be right to give them khadi without insisting on yarn being tendered?
('88', 381, 1, 22, 580315) I say that if these institutions cannot tender yarn they should give up the idea of khadi.
('88', 381, 1, 23, 580406) They can borrow the yarn, they can make their members spin or they can obtain it from friends.
('88', 381, 1, 24, 580501) I want to allow no exceptions to the rule.
('88', 381, 1, 25, 580544) I have taken in hand the nature cure clinic of Dinshaw Mehta at Poona.
('88', 381, 1, 26, 580615) Do you think I can use mill cloth there?
('88', 381, 1, 27, 580656) I said to Dinshaw, ‘I shall give you my yarn and you can buy khadi in exchange.’ Everyone will have to give yarn, be he a raja or a maharaja.
('88', 381, 1, 28, 580798) The yarn clause allows for buying yarn from the neighbours, but this is against my intention.
('88', 381, 1, 29, 580892) I do not want this.
('88', 381, 1, 30, 580912) What I have said is that people may take yarn from their neighbour but they may not pay for it.
('88', 381, 1, 31, 581008) We do not take things from our friends by paying for them.
('88', 381, 1, 32, 581067) That would be commerce.
('88', 381, 1, 33, 581091) If we do not have something we take it from the neighbours and later when we get it ourselves, we return it.
('88', 381, 1, 34, 581200) As a good neighbour he may not take it back but in any case no payment is involved.
('88', 381, 1, 35, 581284) There is in the resolution also the provision for one’s servant doing the spinning.
('88', 381, 1, 36, 581368) It is the same as the members of one’s family spinning and one tendering the yarn in one’s name.
('88', 381, 1, 37, 581465) But it would not be right if someone were to employ a servant specifically for spinning because that is the same as buying the yarn.
('88', 381, 1, 38, 581598) If a servant employed for
('88', 382, 0, 1, 581624) VOL.88 : 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 383
('88', 382, 1, 2, 581670) household work spends a little time on spinning for his employer we can have no objection.
('88', 382, 1, 3, 581761) At the Times of India office, Bombay, they wanted some khadi.
('88', 382, 1, 4, 581823) They came to me and asked, ‘Where shall we find the yarn?’ I said, ‘You have so many peons and workers in your office who do nothing but paste addresses.
('88', 382, 1, 5, 581977) Allow them an hour or two every day for spinning.
('88', 382, 1, 6, 582027) Teach them the art.
('88', 382, 1, 7, 582047) And use the yarn so produced to buy khadi.’ I suggested spinning clubs being organized in cities.
('88', 382, 1, 8, 582145) But I see a different meaning has been put upon what I had said.
('88', 382, 1, 9, 582210) The Club at Bombay became an agency for the sale of yarn.
('88', 382, 1, 10, 582268) Workers are employed who spin for wages and then people buy the yarn to procure their khadi from the bhandars.
('88', 382, 1, 11, 582379) This is to murder truth.
('88', 382, 1, 12, 582404) What I had said was that since large cities are too cramped and people have to live in very small rooms where there is no space for spinning or keeping the charkha or carding, clubs should be organized in various localities and in the precincts of khadi bhandars where people could go to card, make slivers and spin.

('88', 382, 1, 15, 582835) But the clubs that have been started are of a totally different kind and they should be discontinued.
('88', 382, 1, 16, 582937) We should not leave hold of truth.
('88', 382, 1, 17, 582972) We must not deceive ourselves.
('88', 382, 1, 18, 583003) We must give up the lure of selling khadi.

('88', 388, 6, 16, 595254) 707. ANSWERS TO QUESTIONS
('88', 388, 7, 17, 595280) Q. The object of the constructive programme is stated to be the preparation of the people for a non violent political order.
('88', 388, 7, 18, 595405) Is this definition correct?
('88', 388, 7, 19, 595433) Or will it be better to define such a social and political order as one in which no one would be able to exploit the labour of another?
('88', 388, 8, 20, 595569) A. Your definition is correct but it is incomplete.
('88', 388, 8, 21, 595621) In what way it is incomplete will be explained in the answer to your next question.
('88', 388, 9, 22, 595705) Q. If my definition is correct I feel such a social and political order can be achieved theoretically even by our making the largest use of machinery.
('88', 388, 9, 23, 595856) In that case is it necessary to have the maximum number of village industries for the non violent political order?
('88', 388, 9, 24, 595971) If so why?
('88', 388, 10, 25, 595982) A. Non violence cannot be divided into compartments.
('88', 388, 10, 26, 596035) Non violence is an inherent attribute of man or, at any rate, it should be an attribute of man during his waking hours.
('88', 388, 10, 27, 596155) Devotion to non violence is the highest expression of his conscious state.
('88', 388, 10, 28, 596230) If we thus conceive ahimsa we should satisfy all our necessities by the labour of our
('88', 388, 11, 29, 596316) 1 Nature Cure Clinic at Uruli Kanchan
('88', 389, 0, 1, 596354) 390 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 389, 1, 2, 596396) If we do not do this we shall have to depend upon other powers and as long as such condition persists we shall be unable to realize a state of fearless ness.
('88', 389, 1, 3, 596554) Another danger in making more and more use of machinery is that we have to make great efforts for the protection of it, that is to say, we shall have to keep an army as is being done today elsewhere in the world.
('88', 389, 1, 4, 596767) The fact is that even if there is no danger of aggression from outside we shall be slaves to those who will be in control of the big machinery.
('88', 389, 1, 5, 596911) Take the case of the atom bomb.
('88', 389, 1, 6, 596943) Those nations who have atom bombs are feared even by their friends.
('88', 389, 1, 7, 597011) If we take a wise view, we shall be saved from the working of machinery.
('88', 389, 2, 8, 597084) Q. One of the reasons given in favour of hand spinning is that it makes one self sufficient.
('88', 389, 2, 9, 597177) Can one who is self sufficient serve society better than one who is dependent on others?
('88', 389, 2, 10, 597266) Do you mean to say that there is such a connection between self sufficiency and social service that the more one is self sufficient the more is one’s capacity for social service?
('88', 389, 2, 11, 597445) A. In order to satisfy this doubt also we will have to keep in mind the non violent outlook because truth and non violence form the foundation of the order of my conception.
('88', 389, 2, 12, 597619) Our first duty is that we should not be a burden on society, i.e., we should be self sufficient.
('88', 389, 2, 13, 597716) That means self sufficiency by itself is a kind of service.
('88', 389, 2, 14, 597776) After becoming self sufficient we shall use our spare time for the service of others.
('88', 389, 2, 15, 597862) If all become self sufficient no one will have any difficulty.
('88', 389, 2, 16, 597925) In that case no one will be required to undertake service of others.
('88', 389, 2, 17, 597994) But we have not yet reached that stage and therefore we have to think of social service.
('88', 389, 2, 18, 598083) Even if we succeed in realizing complete self sufficiency, man being a social animal we shall have to accept service in some form or other.
('88', 389, 2, 19, 598223) That is, man is as much dependent on others as he is dependent on himself.
('88', 389, 2, 20, 598298) When dependence becomes necessary in order to keep society in good order it is no longer dependence but becomes co operation.
('88', 389, 2, 21, 598424) There is a fragrance in co operation and there is no one weak or strong among the co operators.
('88', 389, 2, 22, 598520) Everyone is equal.
('88', 389, 2, 23, 598539) There is a feeling of helplessness in dependency.
('88', 389, 2, 24, 598589) Members of a family are as much self dependent as interdependent, but there is no feeling of mine or thine.
('88', 389, 2, 25, 598697) That is why they are called co operators.
('88', 389, 2, 26, 598739) Similarly when we take a society, a nation or the entire mankind as a family all men become co operators.
('88', 389, 2, 27, 598845) If we can conceive a picture of such co operation we shall find that there is no need of depending upon lifeless machines.
('88', 389, 2, 28, 598968) Or we shall have to use them the least, not the most, and therein lies the real security and self protection of society.
('88', 390, 0, 1, 599089) VOL.88 : 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 391
('88', 390, 1, 2, 599135) Q. You lay more emphasis on spinning than on agriculture.
('88', 390, 1, 3, 599193) Is there any political reason behind it?
('88', 390, 1, 4, 599234) Or is it because people cannot take to farming as easily as they can to spinning?
('88', 390, 1, 5, 599316) A. I do not make such divisions as social, economic and political.
('88', 390, 1, 6, 599383) What is political is also social and economic.
('88', 390, 1, 7, 599430) One includes the others.
('88', 390, 1, 8, 599455) It is true that we make and have to make such divisions for clarity of understanding.
('88', 390, 1, 9, 599541) One of the reasons why I have not laid stress on agriculture is that even my knowledge of it is almost nil.
('88', 390, 1, 10, 599649) How will I be able to enlighten you if I put emphasis on it?
('88', 390, 1, 11, 599710) It is not so in the case of the charkha.
('88', 390, 1, 12, 599751) I have acquired enough knowledge of it.
('88', 390, 1, 13, 599791) Secondly under foreign rule the charkha had died out; it had been destroyed.
('88', 390, 1, 14, 599868) Agriculture can never be destroyed but its form has been so changed that it has increased the slavery of the people.
('88', 390, 1, 15, 599985) The third reason for putting emphasis on the charkha is that skill of hand has a very small place in agriculture.
('88', 390, 1, 16, 600099) There is hardly any other industry in which the hands and the fingers are so much used as they are in the various processes that go to make khadi.
('88', 390, 1, 17, 600246) The fourth reason is that foreign power first takes hold of the land and through it controls the other things.
('88', 390, 1, 18, 600357) Therefore Government help is very necessary for improvement in agriculture.
('88', 390, 1, 19, 600433) For these and other similar reasons I have laid more emphasis on hand spinning.
('88', 390, 2, 20, 600513) Q. One of the features of the material development of human society appears to be that man is tending to move more and more from self sufficiency to dependency.
('88', 390, 2, 21, 600674) Don’t you think this tendency is not right and that there will be revival of the opposite tendency?
('88', 390, 2, 22, 600774) A. I take this question to mean that society is advancing towards machinery.
('88', 390, 2, 23, 600851) If I have understood the question right, my answer is that society must get rid of its slavery to the machine.
('88', 390, 2, 24, 600962) By being slaves to the machine our slavery to our senses and their activity also increases immensely.
('88', 390, 3, 25, 601064) Q. Are you confident that the constructive programme will be able to achieve its object during your lifetime by mere propaganda?
('88', 390, 3, 26, 601193) Don’t you think taking into consideration human frailties (lust, anger, greed, infatuation, pride and jealousy) that there will be need for “legislative aid” 1 to make the people take to the constructive programme on any wide scale especially in this machine age?
('88', 390, 3, 27, 601457) Will there be any violation of the principle of non violence in taking such help from the elected representatives of the people?
('88', 390, 3, 28, 601586) If so how?
('88', 390, 4, 29, 601597) A. I have said many a time that we will have to take help from the Government on our own terms.
('88', 390, 4, 30, 601693) Not only that, we will have to take help from the whole world There was a time when I felt that we could have only the barest minimum of help from the legislators in the matter of constructive programme.
('88', 390, 4, 31, 601897) But now I have come to realize
('88', 391, 0, 1, 601928) 392 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 391, 1, 2, 601970) that if the representatives of the people go into the legislatures we can secure their help.
('88', 391, 1, 3, 602063) Along with this we must bear in mind that we cannot appreciate the value of the constructive programme properly if we cannot carry it on in adverse circumstances.
('88', 391, 1, 4, 602226) Other people of course can’t.
('88', 391, 1, 5, 602256) I can say dispassionately but from experience that the strength of the people has increased in proportion to the progress of the constructive programme.
('88', 391, 1, 6, 602409) If we can make the constructive programme universal and get it implemented through the people, then swaraj is in our hands.

('88', 392, 12, 20, 604654) Perhaps the expression “Gandhian Constitution” is not a fitting title for Principal Agrawal’s 3 pages.
('88', 392, 12, 21, 604757) It may be acceptable as a convenient and compact title.
('88', 392, 12, 22, 604813) The framework is really Principal Agrawal’s, based on his study of my writings.
('88', 392, 12, 23, 604893) He has been interpreting them for a number of years.
('88', 392, 12, 24, 604946) And as he is anxious not to
('88', 392, 13, 25, 604974) 1 This was written at the back of Arun’s letter to his parents, i.
('88', 392, 13, 26, 605041) e., the addressees.

('88', 393, 0, 1, 605197) 394 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 393, 1, 2, 605239) misinterpret them in any way he would publish nothing without my seeing it.
('88', 393, 1, 3, 605315) This is both an advantage and a disadvantage.
('88', 393, 1, 4, 605361) The advantage is obvious.
('88', 393, 1, 5, 605387) The disadvantage lies in the reader mistaking the particular writing being my view in every detail.
('88', 393, 1, 6, 605487) Let me then warn him against making any such mistake.
('88', 393, 1, 7, 605541) If I were to commit myself to every word appearing in these pages, I might as well write the thing myself.
('88', 393, 1, 8, 605648) Though I have endeavoured to read the constitution twice, with as much attention as I was able to bestow on it during my other engagements, I could not undertake to check every thought and every word of it.
('88', 393, 1, 9, 605855) Nor would my sense of propriety and individual freedom permit me to commit any such atrocity.
('88', 393, 1, 10, 605949) All, therefore, I am able to say is that the brochure contains ample evidence of the care bestowed upon it by the author to make it as accurate as he could.
('88', 393, 1, 11, 606106) There is nothing in it which has jarred on me as inconsistent with what I would like to stand for.
('88', 393, 1, 12, 606205) The author was good enough to make such alterations as I thought were necessary.
('88', 393, 1, 13, 606286) The word “constitution” must not mislead the reader into thinking that the author has made any profession to give him a complete constitution.
('88', 393, 1, 14, 606429) He has made it perfectly clear in the beginning pages that he has only laid down broad lines to indicate what a constitution of my conception would be.
('88', 393, 1, 15, 606581) I regard Principal Agrawal’s to be a thoughtful contribution to the many attempts at presenting India with constitutions.
('88', 393, 1, 16, 606703) The merit of his attempt consists in the fact that he has done what for want of time I have failed to do.

('88', 394, 1, 2, 606949) 712. LETTER TO MANAGING COMMITTEE OF THE TALIMI SANGH
('88', 394, 2, 3, 607003) November 30, 1945
('88', 394, 3, 4, 607021) Yesterday I went to see the Talimi Sangh hostel.
('88', 394, 3, 5, 607070) You know Hoshiaribehn 1 who stays in the Ashram.
('88', 394, 3, 6, 607119) I have sent her son Gajraj to your school.
('88', 394, 3, 7, 607162) He insisted that I should see his school.
('88', 394, 3, 8, 607204) Even yesterday morning he came and said: “You will come, won’t you?” I said: “What shall I do at your school?
('88', 394, 3, 9, 607314) I would rather see the place where you sleep.” I had intended to send his mother too.
('88', 394, 3, 10, 607400) Anyway, I went there after my morning walk to keep my promise.
('88', 394, 3, 11, 607463) I was pained by what I saw there.
('88', 394, 3, 12, 607497) I noticed filth and mismanagement which should not have been there.
('88', 394, 3, 13, 607565) I had not wanted to spend much time there, but I could not bear what I saw there and spent half an hour or threequarters of an hour explaining things to Pandey.
('88', 394, 4, 14, 607726) I found there were puddles of water in front of the verandah of the children’s hospital.
('88', 394, 4, 15, 607815) It offended the eye.
('88', 394, 4, 16, 607836) The children wash themselves right there.
('88', 394, 4, 17, 607878) This breeds mosquitoes and so much of water is wasted.
('88', 394, 4, 18, 607933) We should collect the water in a tub.
('88', 394, 4, 19, 607971) Or we may wash beside the trees near by.
('88', 394, 4, 20, 608012) If there were a thousand boys it would be a disaster.
('88', 394, 4, 21, 608066) Going through the room I found the same thing in front of the verandah on the other side.
('88', 394, 5, 22, 608156) Then I went to the children’s dormitory.
('88', 394, 5, 23, 608197) Even at the entrance there was a lot of dirt.
('88', 394, 5, 24, 608243) I went in.
('88', 394, 5, 25, 608254) Mats were not properly kept.
('88', 394, 5, 26, 608283) I had the bedding of a boy unrolled.
('88', 394, 5, 27, 608320) It was very dirty.
('88', 394, 5, 28, 608339) The bed sheet was torn.
('88', 394, 5, 29, 608363) It was stitched in a couple of places, but very crudely.
('88', 394, 5, 30, 608420) The other tears had not been attended to.
('88', 394, 5, 31, 608462) They should have been patched.
('88', 394, 5, 32, 608493) If the sheet was too badly torn it could have been doubled and stitched.
('88', 394, 5, 33, 608566) Many times in jail I had got mattresses made that way.
('88', 394, 5, 34, 608621) They are warm and strong.
('88', 394, 5, 35, 608647) The cotton of the mattress had collected into big lumps.
('88', 394, 5, 36, 608704) It was not warm.
('88', 394, 5, 37, 608721) That cotton should have been taken out and carded again.
('88', 394, 5, 38, 608778) Several pieces of cloth were discovered from under the mattress.
('88', 394, 5, 39, 608843) They were very dirty.
('88', 394, 5, 40, 608865) I would have kept those pieces clean and used them for patching.
('88', 394, 5, 41, 608930) The mat was very dirty.
('88', 394, 5, 42, 608954) It should have been washed.
('88', 394, 6, 43, 608982) 1 Niece of Balvantsinha.
('88', 394, 6, 44, 609007) According to Balvantsinha Gajraj had complained to Gandhiji that Talimi Sangh was a very dirty place.

('88', 395, 1, 2, 609151) I examined the floor.
('88', 395, 1, 3, 609173) It is used for sleeping but is in a very bad state.
('88', 395, 1, 4, 609225) Pandey said cow dung was not available.
('88', 395, 1, 5, 609265) It is better if cow dung is available.

('88', 397, 0, 1, 613352) 398 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 397, 1, 2, 613394) 715. RATIONAL APPROACH TO NON VIOLENCE 1
('88', 397, 2, 3, 613435) According to me what the All India Congress Committee meant is clear.
('88', 397, 2, 4, 613505) If constructive work is not carried on keeping non violence in mind and accepting it rationally, India will not achieve swaraj as a result of it.
('88', 397, 2, 5, 613651) A lot of work always went on in our villages but it was not informed by the knowledge and the vision of non violence.
('88', 397, 2, 6, 613769) So all we achieved was that we did not become as bankrupt financially as we are today.
('88', 397, 2, 7, 613856) And when foreign invasion started, we abandoned the village industries one after another.
('88', 397, 2, 8, 613946) Work for eradication of untouchability, uplift of Adivasis, equal rights for women, imparting training and bridging the gulf between the poor and the rich and so on had never been taken up.
('88', 397, 2, 9, 614136) When we realized that to achieve real freedom the only royal way was that of non violence and truth, our range of vision extended to the whole of India and beyond it to the whole world, and despite India being a slave country its fame spread in the world.
('88', 397, 2, 10, 614392) I am firmly of opinion that if, as stated in the question, we forget all other aspects of non violence except non killing of human beings, non violence will not remain non violence, it will become bereft of truth, its universality will be lost and we shall never achieve swaraj.
('88', 397, 2, 11, 614671) If ahimsa includes destruction of others’ property, boycotting Government servants, going underground and so on, then, we can neither awaken the crores of people nor give them the correct training in fearlessness.
('88', 397, 2, 12, 614885) If we want to work non violently, then it is necessary to accept the restrictions laid down by me.
('88', 397, 2, 13, 614984) But if we do away with these restrictions then there will be no other alternative for us but to abandon non violence and to train the people for violence.
('88', 397, 2, 14, 615139) That this way is totally futile for us has been proved by this barbarous war.
('88', 397, 2, 15, 615217) At any rate by openly accepting the way of violence we save ourselves from deceiving our own people and the world at large.
('88', 397, 3, 16, 615341) [From Hindi] Khadi Jagat, November 1945
('88', 397, 4, 17, 615381) 1 This was in reply to the question : “How far is the inference correct that in trying to make non violence practical and progressive, people could arrest others or run away, go underground and destroy property but not kill or hurt anyone ?” It was to make this point clear that the All India Congress Committee deliberately added the words “accepting non violence rationally”.
('88', 398, 0, 1, 615759) VOL.88 : 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 399
('88', 398, 1, 2, 615805) 716. SPEECH ON NAYEE TALIM 1
('88', 398, 2, 3, 615834) November 1945 Nayee Talim means teaching through craft.
('88', 398, 2, 4, 615890) That basic craft has to be selected in the light of the conditions and produce of the region.
('88', 398, 2, 5, 615984) For instance, it would not be proper to have khadi as a means of teaching in a region where cotton does not grow, but has to be imported for the purpose.
('88', 398, 2, 6, 616138) If Nayee Talim can be proved to be self supporting through khadi, then the same thing can be applied to other industries too.
('88', 398, 2, 7, 616264) What I mean by making education self sustaining is this.
('88', 398, 2, 8, 616321) Just as the expense on food and clothing for the children studying in Government schools is borne by their parents, similarly, in Nayee Talim schools, parents will have to bear the expenses on food and clothing of their children.
('88', 398, 2, 9, 616551) But the expenses incurred in the schools of today on books and fees will be saved.
('88', 398, 2, 10, 616634) There should be no place for books in Nayee Talim.
('88', 398, 2, 11, 616685) Initially some expenses may have to be incurred on cotton, carding bow, and takli and so on.
('88', 398, 2, 12, 616778) Afterwards the only expenses will be on the teachers’ salaries, stationery, and the salaries of peons, etc., if they have to be engaged.
('88', 398, 2, 13, 616915) Suppose, there are thirty boys in one school.
('88', 398, 2, 14, 616961) They will handle all the processes right from collecting cotton from the field to spinning and weaving the yarn into cloth.
('88', 398, 2, 15, 617085) Through every process the teacher will educate them so that their intellect sharpens day by day.
('88', 398, 2, 16, 617182) This will result in students’ making ever new discoveries in the methods employed in the khadi industry which will make it more productive and profitable.
('88', 398, 2, 17, 617337) The cloth produced by students will be purchased by their parents at any price.
('88', 398, 2, 18, 617417) It will be the teacher’s duty to see that through his students he creates an awareness in their parents that they may not even touch foreign and mill made cloth.
('88', 398, 2, 19, 617579) We should also see that an atmosphere of self sufficiency in cloth and khadi is created.
('88', 398, 2, 20, 617668) We shall have to create an atmosphere of our own.
('88', 398, 2, 21, 617718) For bringing khadi to the stage it has reached today, we had to make efforts and create the climate.
('88', 398, 2, 22, 617819) As a result no one now can root out khadi.
('88', 398, 2, 23, 617862) The same thing can be said of Nayee Talim also.
('88', 398, 2, 24, 617910) If the teacher is unable to create the necessary atmosphere, Nayee Talim cannot become self reliant and cannot make headway.
('88', 398, 2, 25, 618035) If he succeeds in creating the atmosphere and sharpening the intellect of the students, then the entire expenditure from beginning to end on Nayee Talim can be met from the sale of
('88', 398, 3, 26, 618216) 1 This appeared under the title : “Self reliance in Nayee Talim”.
('88', 399, 0, 1, 618282) 400 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 399, 1, 2, 618324) cloth produced by students.
('88', 399, 1, 3, 618352) Students will be equipped for earning when they leave our schools.
('88', 399, 1, 4, 618419) We do not promise them jobs.
('88', 399, 1, 5, 618448) The Government also does not promise employment to students who are trained at enormous expense in Government schools.
('88', 399, 1, 6, 618567) But our students will be brighter than the students of Government schools and will easily find occupations for themselves.
('88', 399, 1, 7, 618690) We must remember that when atmosphere had to be created for Government schools, they had to put in considerable effort in spite of the way being clear.
('88', 399, 1, 8, 618842) The atmosphere we have to create is for revival.
('88', 399, 1, 9, 618891) That which has been destroyed has to be revived in a new way and we look upon it as a peaceful way of attaining swaraj.
('88', 399, 1, 10, 619011) It should be easy to do this.
('88', 399, 1, 11, 619041) We do not find it easy as we have not gone to the villages with the correct attitude and have made no real attempts at all.
('88', 399, 1, 12, 619165) Now we have Nayee Talim.
('88', 399, 1, 13, 619190) If it does not work a miracle and develop power, then what is it good for?
('88', 399, 1, 14, 619265) We do not realize the full significance of boys and girls being entrusted to our care from their childhood and undergoing craft based education in our schools for seven years or more.
('88', 399, 1, 15, 619449) And the modern education which is being imparted to us teaches us that schooling can never become self supporting.
('88', 399, 1, 16, 619564) This creates some confusion in our minds.
('88', 399, 1, 17, 619606) It is my firm belief that if Nayee Talim cannot become self supporting, then the teachers do not understand what it is.
('88', 399, 1, 18, 619726) In my view, amongst other characteristics self reliance is the most important characteristic of Nayee Talim.
('88', 399, 1, 19, 619835) If this is so for the education of boys and girls, then adult education must also be self supporting.
('88', 399, 1, 20, 619937) If we believe that it is difficult to convince adults about the value of education, then I have to say that this is nothing but an old illusion.
('88', 399, 1, 21, 620082) And the teaching of the three R’s in adult education is no part of our Nayee Talim.
('88', 399, 1, 22, 620166) The meaning of adult education is that we will give them, through their own language, all round education of a pure and socially useful life.
('88', 399, 1, 23, 620308) And if they do not easily become self supporting, in my view there is some serious defect in that education.
('88', 399, 1, 24, 620417) We should not also forget that complete co operation should be the basis from the very beginning.
('88', 399, 1, 25, 620515) Those who know the full meaning of co operation will raise no doubts about self reliance.
('88', 399, 2, 26, 620605) QUESTION: Today only those students go to Government schools whose parents can pay for their food and clothing.
('88', 399, 2, 27, 620717) We expect that under Nayee Talim, all the children of a village will go to school.
('88', 399, 2, 28, 620800) There may be many among them who do not have the necessary food and clothing in their homes.
('88', 399, 2, 29, 620893) What is the responsibility of Nayee Talim in such cases?

('88', 400, 1, 2, 620996) A. I have just stated the ideal that parents will provide for food and clothes.
('88', 400, 1, 3, 621076) Even now boys do eat and wear clothes.
('88', 400, 1, 4, 621115) The parents will pay to school whatever they spend on their children’s food and clothing.

('88', 400, 3, 24, 622682) A. Any price must of course mean reasonable price.

('88', 400, 3, 26, 622886) There will be no question of making a large profit on it.

('88', 400, 3, 32, 623365) Not one will even care for me if this happens during my lifetime.
('88', 400, 3, 33, 623431) All my answers apply to the present time, the present conditions.
('88', 400, 4, 34, 623497) Q. Training of teachers is a vast field that we have before us.

('88', 401, 1, 2, 623666) A. Your question is, how can those who have come here to be teachers become self reliant?

('88', 404, 5, 8, 630078) 721. SPEECH AT PRAYER MEETING
('88', 404, 6, 9, 630108) SODEPUR, December 1, 1945
('88', 404, 7, 10, 630134) He began by referring to his attempts made since 1914, when he was in England to learn Bengali.
('88', 404, 7, 11, 630230) He made some progress in it, though he could not keep up his Bengali studies.
('88', 404, 7, 12, 630308) It was his ambition to be able to speak to the people of Bengal in Bengali so that he might be able to penetrate into their hearts.
('88', 404, 7, 13, 630440) He was sorry he could not do so on the present occasion.
('88', 404, 7, 14, 630497) He was also of the opinion that no Indian could call himself a full fledged citizen of India unless he could speak to the people of the various provinces in their own tongues.
('88', 404, 7, 15, 630673) Failing this proficiency in the different languages it was the duty of every Indian to learn at least Hindustani which alone could be the rashtrabhasha 1 of India.
('88', 404, 8, 16, 630837) He then proceeded to give the etiology of his present visit to Bengal.
('88', 404, 8, 17, 630908) Ever since his release from prison, he had been anxious to visit Bengal but he could not do so owing to ill health.
('88', 404, 8, 18, 631024) Moreover, he did not want to visit Bengal unless he was sure that the authorities would welcome his visit and that there would be no restrictions on his movements.
('88', 404, 8, 19, 631188) He was not prepared to submit to any restrictive orders on the one hand or on the other to offer civil disobedience against such orders under conditions now prevailing in the country.
('88', 404, 8, 20, 631372) Even after the way for his visit to Bengal was clear it had to be postponed for several months on account of Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel who
('88', 404, 9, 21, 631510) 1 National language
('88', 405, 0, 1, 631530) 406 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 405, 1, 2, 631572) was in need of nature cure treatment and needed his (Gandhiji’s) presence by his side.
('88', 405, 1, 3, 631659) He was glad, however, that after all he had been able to come to Bengal.
('88', 405, 2, 4, 631732) Explaining next the object of his visit, Gandhiji said that it was purely to offer whatever consolation his presence in their midst could give to the victims of Bengal famine and to do whatever he could to relieve their distress.
('88', 405, 2, 5, 631962) He had not come to take part in the politics of the province or in the forthcoming elections.
('88', 405, 2, 6, 632056) In fact, as they all knew, he took very little interest in these things.
('88', 405, 2, 7, 632129) Where his chief interest lay was too well known to need reiteration.
('88', 405, 3, 8, 632198) Mahatmaji then concluded after appealing to the people assembled to contribute their mite to the Harijan Fund as a token of their sympathy with the cause of the abolition of untouchability as also to ameliorate the condition of Harijans.
('88', 405, 3, 9, 632436) Incidentally he mentioned that in this way he had collected 2 lakhs of rupees for the Harijans since his release.
('88', 405, 3, 10, 632550) The proceeds of the autograph fees that he charged were earmarked for the Harijan Fund.
('88', 405, 3, 11, 632638) Anyone by paying a fee of Rs. 5 could have his autograph.
('88', 405, 3, 12, 632696) There could be no exemption on the ground of poverty because according to him the autograph hunting was essentially a rich man’s hobby.
('88', 405, 3, 13, 632832) Anyway, there was none poorer than the Harijans and consequently none had a right to cheat the Harijans out of the autograph fees which had been premortgaged to them.

('88', 406, 1, 2, 634115) I. S. We, Englishmen are apt to forget that side of the question.
('88', 406, 2, 3, 634181) G. Habit becomes second nature.
('88', 406, 2, 4, 634213) There may be no deliberate intention either.
('88', 406, 3, 5, 634258) I. S. In the Punjab and Delhi races mix much more freely than elsewhere.
('88', 406, 3, 6, 634331) Was that due to the fact that the disparity in numbers was comparatively less there?
('88', 406, 4, 7, 634416) Gandhiji was of opinion that the contrast presented by Bengal in this respect was perhaps due to the violent spirit having manifested itself there on a much larger scale than in Delhi or in the Punjab.
('88', 406, 4, 8, 634618) The Punjab did show the violent spirit in some measure.
('88', 406, 4, 9, 634674) But it was not a patch upon Bengal.
('88', 406, 4, 10, 634710) The daring of the Chittagong Armoury Raid was neither attempted nor duplicated anywhere else.
('88', 406, 5, 11, 634804) I. S. I have often thought over it, and it has always baffled me how these Bengali young men, so gentle by nature, have drifted into violence.
('88', 406, 6, 12, 634947) G. I have solved it for myself.
('88', 406, 6, 13, 634979) They feel they have been unjustly libelled in the past.
('88', 406, 6, 14, 635035) Lord Curzon harped on their softness.
('88', 406, 6, 15, 635073) It soured them.
('88', 406, 6, 16, 635089) So they say, ‘We may not be wealthy, but surely we are not effeminate.’ So they adopted this devious method and surpassed every other province in daring.
('88', 406, 6, 17, 635243) They defied death, defied poverty and even public opinion.
('88', 406, 6, 18, 635302) I have discussed this question of violence threadbare with so many terrorists and anarchists.
('88', 406, 6, 19, 635396) It is terrible whether the Arab does it or the Jew.
('88', 406, 6, 20, 635448) It is a bad outlook for the world if this spirit of violence takes hold of the mass mind.
('88', 406, 6, 21, 635538) Ultimately in destroying itself it destroys the race.
('88', 406, 7, 22, 635592) I. S. And it has spread all over the world for the last two or three years.

('88', 406, 8, 25, 635858) As I read it, it struck me that this was not the best way to introduce democracy among the Japanese—a race so proud, so sensitive, so highly organized along Western lines.
('88', 406, 8, 26, 636030) They will do what the Italians did in Garibaldi’s time on a much larger scale.
('88', 406, 8, 27, 636109) You cannot deal with the human race on these lines.
('88', 406, 8, 28, 636161) Whatever happens in one part of the world will affect the other parts.
('88', 406, 8, 29, 636232) The world has so shrunk.
('88', 406, 9, 30, 636257) This evoked from the friend the observation that he did not think that the world had deteriorated so much theoretically as it might have during the last three years.
('88', 406, 9, 31, 636423) Gandhiji agreed with him though his grounds, he remarked, were different.
('88', 406, 10, 32, 636497) I. S. My reason for that belief is that in spite of the fact that suffering, for
('88', 406, 11, 33, 636578) 1 Douglas MacArthur, U. S. Army General; Commander of the occupation forces in Japan after the War.

('88', 407, 1, 2, 636720) instance in Indonesia and elsewhere, has been appalling during the last three years, the human mind has not been equally warped.
('88', 407, 2, 3, 636849) G. My hope is based on a detached view of the situation.
('88', 407, 2, 4, 636906) Whilst in detention in the Aga Khan Palace I had leisure to read and think.
('88', 407, 2, 5, 636982) What struck me was that whilst practice showed deterioration, the mind of man had very much progressed.
('88', 407, 2, 6, 637086) Practice has not been able to keep pace with the mind.
('88', 407, 2, 7, 637141) Man has begun to say, ‘This is wrong, that is wrong.’ Whereas previously he justified his conduct, he now no longer justifies his own or his neighbour’s.
('88', 407, 2, 8, 637295) He wants to set right the wrong but does not know that his own practice fails him.
('88', 407, 2, 9, 637378) The contradiction between his thought and conduct fetters him.
('88', 407, 2, 10, 637441) His conduct is not governed by logic.
('88', 407, 2, 11, 637479) Then, of course, there is my standing prediction in favour of non violence that it will prevail— whatever man may or may not do.
('88', 407, 2, 12, 637608) That keeps my optimism alive.
('88', 407, 2, 13, 637638) Extensive personal experience too confirms my belief that non violence is self acting.
('88', 407, 2, 14, 637725) It will have its way and overcome all obstacles irrespective of the shortcomings of the instruments.
('88', 407, 2, 15, 637826) It makes no difference how we arrive at our conclusion, but it keeps us fresh and green.
('88', 407, 3, 16, 637915) The conversation next turned upon Gandhiji’s pet theme of living up to 125 years.
('88', 407, 3, 17, 637997) Gandhiji’s visitor wanted to know how he managed to keep physically fit.
('88', 407, 3, 18, 638070) Gandhiji replied that outwardly he owed his physical fitness to strict adherence to regular habits in eating, drinking and sleeping and to his partiality for nature cure principles which he had adopted strictly in life since 1901. Reminiscently he described how up till 1901 he used the medicine bottle but had almost thrown it away and for forty five years he had lived more or less according to nature cure principles.
('88', 407, 4, 19, 638491) G. But, in a still greater measure, it is due to the practice of detachment of mind.
('88', 407, 4, 20, 638576) By detachment I mean that you must not worry whether the desired result follows from your action or not, so long as your motive is pure, your means correct.
('88', 407, 4, 21, 638733) Really, it means that things will come right in the end if you take care of the means and leave the rest to Him.
('88', 407, 5, 22, 638846) He based his belief on the teachings of the Bhagavad Gita which he had called his “dictionary of action”.
('88', 407, 6, 23, 638952) The friend remarked on the close analogy between the teaching of the Bhagavad Gita and the thesis presented in Aldous Huxley’s 1 Ends and Means.
('88', 407, 6, 24, 639097) The mention of Aldous Huxley’s name revived in Gandhiji’s mind memories of old days
('88', 407, 7, 25, 639181) 1 British novelist and critic; in later life became increasingly drawn to Hindu philosophy.
('88', 408, 0, 1, 639273) VOL.88 : 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 409
('88', 408, 1, 2, 639319) about Aldous Huxley’s father 1 whose writings he used to read during his student days in London in 1889.
('88', 408, 2, 3, 639424) I. S. But there is a physical side all the same?
('88', 408, 3, 4, 639473) G. Yes, only I attach greater importance to the mental.
('88', 408, 3, 5, 639529) What you think you become.
('88', 408, 3, 6, 639556) Thought is never complete unless it finds expression in action and action limits your thought.
('88', 408, 3, 7, 639651) It is only when there is a perfect accord between the two that there is full, natural life.
('88', 408, 4, 8, 639743) I. S. But what about the legacy of one’s past life?
('88', 408, 4, 9, 639795) It cannot be written off the balance sheet.
('88', 408, 5, 10, 639839) G. I have my answer for that.
('88', 408, 5, 11, 639869) If my past conduct does not warrant the full span of life, no matter however correct my present life may be, I can still counteract the effect of past mistakes by attaining complete detachment between the mind and the body.
('88', 408, 5, 12, 640093) Detachment enables one to overcome the effects of past faulty practice as well as handicaps of heredity and environment.
('88', 408, 5, 13, 640214) Normally speaking, every deviation from the rule of nature, whether ignorant or wilful, e.
('88', 408, 5, 14, 640305) g., anger, ill temper, impatience, errors in conjugal life, exacts its toll.
('88', 408, 5, 15, 640382) But there is this promise that if you have arrived at complete detachment you can rub out all these.
('88', 408, 5, 16, 640483) “Except ye be born again, ye cannot have everlasting life.” Conversely, you can have everlasting life if you are “born again”.
('88', 408, 5, 17, 640610) There is no hurdle placed before death.
('88', 408, 5, 18, 640650) You can turn over a new leaf and begin life anew here and now; the past will not disturb its tenor provided you have completely severed yourself from it and its legacy by the axe of detachment.
('88', 408, 6, 19, 640844) On the previous occasion when this friend had visited Gandhiji, Gandhiji had done all the talking and the friend had listened.

('88', 408, 7, 23, 641253) I. S. I am only human.

('88', 409, 4, 5, 641548) F. A. U. MEMBER: However much we may want to be friendly the past tradition clings round your necks and drives you to desperation.

('88', 409, 5, 9, 642146) India, when she has come into her own will need all such assistance.

('88', 411, 6, 8, 646125) Addressing the congregation after the prayer Gandhiji said he would like to thank them and congratulate them because they had maintained silence and were peaceful during the prayer.
('88', 411, 6, 9, 646307) The gathering of this evening was very big indeed.
('88', 411, 6, 10, 646358) On Saturday the prayer meeting was less crowded.
('88', 411, 6, 11, 646407) On both the days they had shown remarkable discipline.

('88', 411, 7, 13, 646547) The prayer song which was sung this evening had a special significance.
('88', 411, 7, 14, 646619) Gandhiji said it was very appropriate in the conditions obtaining at present.
('88', 411, 7, 15, 646697) The song was also sung in a very melodious tune.
('88', 411, 8, 16, 646746) In the song there was an appeal to God to lead humanity from darkness to light.
('88', 411, 8, 17, 646826) It said the humanity was engulfed in thickening darkness and had lost vision.
('88', 411, 8, 18, 646904) So they were praying to God to give them strength and lead them to light.
('88', 411, 9, 19, 646978) The import of the song was that they must be freed from all bondage and attain enlightenment.
('88', 411, 9, 20, 647072) The freedom from bondage also included the winning of swaraj.
('88', 411, 9, 21, 647134) India wanted release from the bondage.
('88', 411, 9, 22, 647173) We are all engulfed in darkness today.
('88', 411, 9, 23, 647212) Not only India but the world also is engulfed in darkness.
('88', 411, 9, 24, 647271) India wants peace.
('88', 411, 9, 25, 647290) So also does the entire world.
('88', 411, 9, 26, 647321) We are all travellers groping in that thickening darkness.
('88', 411, 9, 27, 647380) We are all blind and cannot feel the absence of light.
('88', 411, 9, 28, 647435) The prayer we have offered is the most important thing of this evening.
('88', 411, 9, 29, 647507) I was in South Africa when I used to pray privately.
('88', 411, 9, 30, 647560) When I returned to India I saw the necessity of holding mass prayers.

('88', 417, 4, 7, 654864) 735. LETTER TO VALLABHRAM VAIDYA
('88', 417, 5, 8, 654897) SODEPUR, December 4, 1945
('88', 417, 6, 9, 654923) BHAI VALLABHRAM, I have your letter.
('88', 417, 6, 10, 654960) After I return to Sevagram and settle down there you may certainly come if you wish.
('88', 417, 6, 11, 655045) May be you are not acquainted with my views as they have progressed.
('88', 417, 6, 12, 655114) They were of course implicit in all my writings but of late they have become more explicit.
('88', 417, 6, 13, 655206) I have no longer any interest in marriages, whether within the caste, inter caste or even interprovincial.
('88', 417, 6, 14, 655313) Therefore, so far as possible, I do not say anything anywhere on the subject of marriages.
('88', 417, 6, 15, 655404) As it is I hardly ever attended any and now I have firmly stopped attending them altogether.
('88', 417, 6, 16, 655497) What I believe is that if we want to preserve whatever is good in varnashrama every Hindu has to become not only a Shudra but an atishudra 1, and regard himself as such.
('88', 417, 6, 17, 655667) And as a true indication of it marriages should really take place only between atishudras and the so called other varnas.
('88', 417, 6, 18, 655789) These marriages also should be not for the sake of indulgence but so as to observe restraint and keeping in mind the restrictions it implies.
('88', 417, 6, 19, 655931) Now I can send my blessings to Chi.
('88', 417, 6, 20, 655967) Ramakant and Chi.
('88', 417, 6, 21, 655985) May they be happy, live in restraint and may their alliance be doubly devoted to service.
('88', 417, 6, 22, 656075) Often after a marriage instead of one sevak multiplying into two both the parties drop out of service.
('88', 417, 6, 23, 656178) This is my experience.
('88', 417, 6, 24, 656201) There are exceptions, and may this union be one such.

('88', 420, 5, 15, 661530) JIVANJI, I got your letter and the cheque.
('88', 420, 5, 16, 661573) It has to be considered whether we should go as far as you suggest regarding the copy right.
('88', 420, 5, 17, 661666) Anybody writing to us for permission and our giving it will mean that we have read the work or got it read by someone and approve.
('88', 420, 5, 18, 661797) In this connection Anand Hingorani had suggested different Boards, so that the Tamil Board would decide about the Tamil translation and the Malayalam Board would advise about the translation in that language.
('88', 420, 5, 19, 662006) There would, thus, be a separate Board for each language.
('88', 420, 5, 20, 662064) We have to consider how far it would be advisable and becoming for us to bother ourselves to that extent.
('88', 420, 5, 21, 662170) There are several translations of Tolstoy’s books in the same language.
('88', 420, 5, 22, 662242) All of them are not up to the mark, and the titles of the books also have been translated differently.
('88', 420, 5, 23, 662345) All of them sell, but the translation which is most faithful to the original, most painstaking and beautiful sells more than the other translations.
('88', 420, 5, 24, 662494) The same has happened in the case of the Bible.
('88', 420, 5, 25, 662542) The authorized version is there but there are many others in the field and their publication is not prohibited.
('88', 420, 5, 26, 662654) Every translation has its own circle of readers.
('88', 420, 5, 27, 662703) You have raised the question of the Autobiography.
('88', 420, 5, 28, 662754) A translation has been brought out by one Tamil publisher and now this
('88', 421, 0, 1, 662825) 422 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 421, 1, 2, 662867) is the second.
('88', 421, 1, 3, 662882) How would we know which of the two is really good?
('88', 421, 1, 4, 662933) Or would it be advisable to stop other translations from being published?
('88', 421, 1, 5, 663007) I do not see much benefit in that.
('88', 421, 1, 6, 663042) Even when we decided to claim copyright, I did not go as far as that.
('88', 421, 1, 7, 663112) This matter cannot be looked at from a purely legal point of view, nor from a purely financial one.
('88', 421, 1, 8, 663212) We should look at it wholly from a moral and practical point of view.
