('88', 427, 5, 7, 671669) 753. SPEECH AT PRAYER MEETING 2
('88', 427, 6, 8, 671701) SODEPUR, December 6, 1945
('88', 427, 7, 9, 671727) In his introductory speech Gandhiji referred to the incident which took place at Sodepur Railway Station when one person either in attempting
('88', 427, 8, 10, 671869) to board a running train which was not scheduled to stop at Sodepur or for some such reason was run over and killed.
('88', 427, 9, 11, 671986) They might think that when there were crores of Indians what did it matter if one met with death in such circumstances.
('88', 427, 9, 12, 672106) But that was a totally wrong view.
('88', 427, 9, 13, 672141) And if they allowed themselves to think in that way they would not be able to build up a brotherhood in India and secure her salvation.
('88', 427, 9, 14, 672277) They must instead think that the person who met his death the other day was one of them and must feel sorry for his tragic end.
('88', 427, 10, 15, 672405) Perhaps, said Gandhiji, he himself was partly responsible for his death for the deceased went there either to see him or to attend the prayer.
('88', 427, 10, 16, 672548) The congregation too was partly responsible because after the prayer was over they rushed to the Station, vied with each other to catch the train and thereby created a situation which caused this death.
('88', 427, 10, 17, 672751) They, therefore, should henceforth take the vow with him not to create any such situation in future which might cause the death of a fellow brother.
('88', 427, 11, 18, 672900) All this happened because they were not disciplined.
('88', 427, 11, 19, 672953) The prayer was intended to confer upon man that discipline which he required so urgently.
('88', 427, 11, 20, 673043) If they were mentally disciplined through the practice of prayer they would no more commit the mistake they committed the other day.
('88', 427, 12, 21, 673176) If by prayer they could be mentally disciplined, stated Gandhiji, they would
('88', 427, 13, 22, 673253) 1 The subscription is in Tamil.
('88', 427, 13, 23, 673285) 2 The meeting was also attended by Abdul Ghaffar Khan and Jawaharlal Nehru.
('88', 428, 0, 1, 673361) VOL.88: 30 AUGUST, 1945 6 DECEMBER, 1945 429
('88', 428, 1, 2, 673406) attain a state which was nobler and higher than even the salvation of India.
('88', 428, 2, 3, 673483) Perhaps, freedom of India could be maintained with the help of pistols or swords.
('88', 428, 2, 4, 673565) But were those weapons of any value if their votaries were not disciplined?
('88', 428, 2, 5, 673641) Therefore whether a country was wedded to violence or non violence discipline was of paramount importance to all men.
('88', 428, 3, 6, 673759) Without discipline it was difficult to attain swaraj as he had stated two days ago.
('88', 428, 4, 7, 673843) If they practised prayer with all concentration they would find that all their difficulties would smoothen.
('88', 428, 5, 8, 673951) Concluding, Gandhiji referred to an incident in South Africa when a ship came upon a rock and was about to sink.
('88', 428, 5, 9, 674064) Its Captain was a strong willed and disciplined man.
('88', 428, 5, 10, 674117) He preserved the calm of his mind and realized that he could not save all lives.
('88', 428, 5, 11, 674198) He, therefore, secured the safety of as many men as he could and then went down with a hymn to God on his lips alone with the sinking ship.
('88', 428, 5, 12, 674338) If he was not a disciplined man, said Gandhiji, he could not have saved the lives of the many passengers of the ship whom he brought to safety.
('88', 428, 5, 13, 674482) What was, therefore, urgently required of all was discipline and this all men could aquire by actively participating in prayer.
('88', 428, 6, 14, 674610) Amrita Bazar Patrika, 7 12 1945
('88', 429, 0, 1, 674642) 430 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('88', 429, 1, 2, 674684) APPENDICES
('88', 429, 2, 3, 674695) APPENDIX I
('88', 429, 3, 4, 674706) LORD WAVELL’S VERSION OF HIS TALK WITH GANDHIJI1
('88', 429, 4, 5, 674755) I deplored the recent speeches of Congress leaders and said that the preaching of violence could only lead to violence, especially with the inflammable material in India, of young students and goondas (the Indian equivalent of hooligans); and that fomentation of racial and communal hatred would not produce the atmosphere in which a solution could be produced in next year’s discussions.
('88', 429, 4, 6, 675144) He admitted the violence of Congress speeches and indicated that he was trying to get the tone lowered.
('88', 429, 4, 7, 675248) I said that an agreement of some kind between Hindu and Muslim was necessary, even if it was an agreement to part.
('88', 429, 4, 8, 675363) He said he had always tried for a settlement but was frustrated by the British policy of divide and rule.
('88', 429, 4, 9, 675469) I said this was nonsense, we tried our best to bring them together; that the increase in communal feeling was mainly due to the action of Congress Ministries in 1937 39 which had made Muslims feel they would not get a square deal from Congress and had caused the rise of the Muslim League and the idea of Pakistan.
('88', 429, 4, 10, 675784) He defended the Congress Ministries at some length, and said all Governors had admitted their fairness.
('88', 429, 4, 11, 675888) I said there was no doubt about the psychological effect on the Muslims, whatever the facts may have been; and he admitted this.
('88', 429, 4, 12, 676017) I then said that the British were accustomed to abuse and misrepresentation from Indian Nationalists, but that there was a limit, and that it seemed hardly wise to antagonize us at this moment when we were trying our best to bring about a settlement, and that India after getting her freedom would want Britain’s co operation in defence and in commercial development.
('88', 429, 4, 13, 676385) I added that if any disorder resulted from the hatred now being stirred up, it would of course be my duty to suppress it, and I should do so by all means in my power.
('88', 429, 4, 14, 676552) He assented to this; and then said that India needed no help from Britian in trade or defence.
('88', 429, 4, 15, 676647) She would develop her trade in her own way, and her defence would be the moral force of non violence, which would eventually conquer the world and bring about universal peace.
('88', 429, 4, 16, 676823) I said I did not think either of us would live to see this desirable issue, and that the immediate point was to prevent violence in India during the next year or so.
('88', 429, 4, 17, 676989) We left it at that.
('88', 429, 4, 18, 677009) He was quite friendly though woolly, and seemed in good health.
('88', 429, 5, 19, 677073) The Viceroy’s Journal, pp.
